# Decisions

Architectural / process decisions. Never deleted ŌĆö strikethrough if reversed.

## 2026-06-03 ŌĆö TASK-152 subprocess backend parity (docker compose) for dev services

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-06-03 | **The descriptorŌåÆcompose translation lives in a NEW pure module `packages/sandbox-subprocess/src/compose.ts`** exporting (a) `descriptorsToComposeProject(services, {projectName, sessionId})` ŌåÆ a plain JS compose-file object + (b) a thin `runCompose`/`composeUp`/`composeDown` layer over an INJECTABLE command runner. `open-session.ts` imports it; unit tests exercise the translation with NO real Docker. | Mirrors the established `gitOnce`/`gitWithRetry` injectable-runner seam (patterns.md TASK-137) and keeps the spawn out of the translation so the card's "unit-test the translation WITHOUT a real Docker daemon" is satisfiable. A separate module also survives `vi.mock` cleanly (patterns.md F-1/F-2 lesson: git-orchestrating helper in its own module). | (a) inline the translation + spawn in open-session.ts ŌĆö rejected: can't unit-test translation without a daemon, bloats the 720-line file. |
| 2026-06-03 | **Compose file is passed to `docker compose -f - -p <project> up` via STDIN** (`-f -`), project name = `ax-svc-<sessionId-sanitized>`. Ports published `127.0.0.1:<hostPort>:<containerPort>` (I4 loopback-only). Each service: `image` (digest-pinned), `environment` (descriptor env), `ports`, `healthcheck` (from descriptor tcp/exec ŌåÆ compose `test:`), `tmpfs:` for `writablePaths` (NO host bind mounts ŌĆö I10), `network_mode` left default (bridge; NO host networking), no `privileged`. | `-f -` STDIN avoids writing a compose file to disk (no temp-file cleanup, no path-injection surface). Loopback publish + tmpfs-not-bind + no privileged/host-net is the locked posture the card mandates (I4/I10). sessionId is sanitized to compose's project-name charset `[a-z0-9_-]`. | (a) write compose.yml into socketDir ŌĆö rejected: extra file + cleanup; STDIN is cleaner. (b) named volumes for writablePaths ŌĆö rejected: a named volume persists past `down` unless `-v`; tmpfs is ephemeral-by-construction and needs no teardown bookkeeping. |
| 2026-06-03 | **Fail loud when `input.services` is non-empty AND Docker is unavailable** ŌĆö probe `docker compose version` (injected runner) BEFORE minting the session/listener/spawn; on failure throw `PluginError({code:'services-unavailable'})` and do NOT half-open the session. Services brought up AFTER session+listener+spawn prep but the Docker probe gates earliest so we don't leak a tempdir/session on the common "no Docker" case. | Card: "Fail loud if Docker is unavailable and services were requested" + "don't half-open the session." Probing first is the cheapest fail-fast and avoids any session/listener/proc cleanup. | (a) let `compose up` fail and translate the error ŌĆö rejected: by then we've minted a session + listener + tempdir to unwind; explicit pre-probe is cleaner + a clearer error. |
| 2026-06-03 | **`docker compose down -v` runs in the existing `child.once('close')` cleanup**, alongside the tempdir `fs.rm` ŌĆö best-effort, logged at warn on failure, never throws. The compose project handle (project name) is captured in closure. | Card: "tear them down in the existing close cleanup." Reuses the one teardown chokepoint; `-v` reaps anonymous/tmpfs volumes. Best-effort matches the sibling session:terminate/ipc:stop/fs.rm cleanups already there. | (a) a separate reaper timer ŌĆö rejected: the close handler is the established single teardown site; a second path risks double-down or a leak on the untaken path. |
| 2026-06-03 | **Half-wired window stays OPEN** ŌĆö the subprocess backend now CONSUMES `input.services`, but nothing POPULATES it yet (orchestrator fold + k8s sidecars are separate epic cards; grep confirms chat-orchestrator builds no `services` array and sandbox-k8s ignores it). Noted explicitly in the PR per the card. | This is the documented epic phasing (half_wired_window_pattern). The consumer is fully tested in isolation; the producer lands in a sibling card. Not a Half-Wired violation of the merge gate because the card sanctions the open window and the code IS reachable+tested via the hook + unit tests. | (a) also fold services in the orchestrator here ŌĆö rejected: out of card scope, would balloon the diff into k8s-parity territory the card explicitly defers. |
| 2026-06-03 | **Teardown ordering: bring services up at step 7b (BEFORE the `child.once('close')` cleanup handler is registered at step 8/9), not after.** On bring-up FAILURE the explicit `unwindAfterServicesFailure` SIGKILLs the child + `composeDown` + unwinds session/listener/tempdir; the close handler isn't registered yet so there's NO double-teardown race. On the HAPPY path the close handler is the single teardown chokepoint that issues `down -v` alongside the tempdir `fs.rm`. | The failure path needs synchronous-enough teardown before the throw; doing it inline (not via the async fire-and-forget close handler) is correct. `composeDown` is idempotent (down on an absent project = exit 0) so a double-down is harmless. The "child sync-crashes after successful bring-up but before close-handler attaches ŌåÆ leak" window is IDENTICAL to the pre-existing session/ipc/tempdir cleanup window ŌĆö not a new regression. | (a) bring up AFTER close-handler registration ŌĆö rejected: introduces a close-handler-vs-explicit-unwind double-`composeDown` on the failure path for a leak window already present for the sibling cleanups. |
| 2026-06-03 | **Phase 5 review fallback (TASK-152)**: the `ax-code-reviewer`/`Task` subagent-dispatch tool is STILL absent in this orchestrated env (ToolSearch returned no `Task` tool ŌĆö same as TASK-150/145/141). Substituted a disciplined whole-branch self-review of the staged `main...HEAD` diff + the PR's hosted reviewers. Self-review validated the teardown-ordering decision and confirmed no double-down. Real `docker compose config` validated the generated shape (loopback `host_ip:127.0.0.1`, tmpfs, no host bind). | Established precedent ŌĆö the tool is genuinely absent, not transient. Diff is isolated to `@ax/sandbox-subprocess` (sandbox-k8s has its own `openSessionImpl`, no import) + a new pure module + 2 daemon-free test files. | Block waiting for the tool (rejected ŌĆö absent, would strand the card). |

## 2026-06-03 ŌĆö TASK-150 neutral services descriptor + Capabilities.services grammar + validator

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-06-03 | **`ServiceDescriptor` shape home = `@ax/skills-parser`** (interface in `capabilities.ts` + new runtime Zod `ServiceDescriptorSchema` + `CapabilitiesSchema`). skills-parser had NO zod before (only `js-yaml`) ŌåÆ add `zod` dep. The card says "defined once in @ax/skills-parser, re-validated in @ax/sandbox-protocol." | skills-parser is the canonical neutral capability shape (TASK-90) and is on the eslint runtime allow-list, so a runtime zod export is permitted. The validator + connectors store consume the canonical schema. | (a) define only the TS interface in skills-parser, Zod elsewhere ŌĆö rejected: card explicitly wants the Zod here ("its Zod CapabilitiesSchema"). |
| 2026-06-03 | **`@ax/sandbox-protocol` re-declares `ServiceDescriptorSchema` LOCALLY** (its own zod, not importing skills-parser) + adds `services: z.array(...).max(8).optional()` to `OpenSessionInputSchema`. | Exact precedent: sandbox-protocol already re-declares `McpServerSchema` independently of skills-parser's `McpServerSpec` interface (trust-boundary re-validation ŌĆö a drifted/compromised host must not smuggle a malformed spec). Avoids a new build edge from sandbox-protocol (which imports zod only). | (a) import the schema from skills-parser ŌĆö rejected: breaks the re-validate-at-the-wire posture + adds a cross-package edge sandbox-protocol doesn't currently have. |
| 2026-06-03 | **`@ax/connectors/types.ts` adds `services` to its LOCAL `CapabilitiesSchema`** (re-declare a local `ServiceDescriptorSchema`, default `[]`). | connectors already re-declares the whole `CapabilitiesSchema` locally to keep its skills-parser import TYPE-only (I2). Adding the field there round-trips `services` through the connectors store parse-on-write/read. Minimal blast radius ŌĆö keeps connectors' deliberate type-only stance. | (a) runtime-import skills-parser's schema into connectors ŌĆö allowed by lint but reverses connectors' documented type-only choice (rejected). |
| 2026-06-03 | **Validator = new `@ax/validator-service` plugin registering a `services:validate` service hook** (no DB dep, mirrors `validator-skill`'s `skills:scan`), pushed unconditionally in BOTH the CLI preset (`packages/cli/src/main.ts`) and k8s preset (`presets/k8s/src/index.ts`) alongside the other validators. Enforces digest-pin (I8), descriptor caps, and REJECTS forbidden k8s vocab (pod/container/securityContext/runtimeClassName/volume/emptyDir/initContainers/restartPolicy). | A pure service-hook validator has no DB dependency, so it loads in the Postgres-free CLI preset exactly like `skills:scan` does (validator-skill registers `skills:scan` and loads in CLI even though skills only exist in k8s). One source of truth (I4) for service-descriptor validation, callable by the connectors store / orchestrator fold. | (a) subscriber on workspace:pre-apply ŌĆö rejected: services aren't workspace files, they ride OpenSessionInput + Capabilities. (b) fold validation into connectors store only ŌĆö rejected: card wants a reusable validator wired into BOTH presets + an independent rejection of forbidden vocab the Zod regex alone can't fully express. |
| 2026-06-03 | **validator-service forbidden-vocab deep-scan SKIPS the `env` sub-map** (self-review fix). `findForbiddenVocab` walks descriptor object KEYS at any depth, but does NOT descend into an `env` value ŌĆö env keys are user-defined env-var NAMES (`env: { container: 'ŌĆ”' }` is legitimate), not descriptor structure, and can't influence backend scheduling. The structural smuggling we guard (a `pod`/`securityContext`/ŌĆ” sibling of name/image, or a forbidden key inside `healthcheck`) is still caught. | A security scan that false-positives on a legitimate env var named `container`/`pod` would block valid configs. The threat is a scheduler field injected into descriptor STRUCTURE, which is never an env key. Regression test added. | Scan everything incl. env keys (rejected ŌĆö false positives); scan nothing nested (rejected ŌĆö misses a forbidden key inside healthcheck). |
| 2026-06-03 | **skills-parser `CapabilitiesSchema` is exported-but-not-yet-consumed by runtime callers** (connectors keeps its OWN local schema; validator uses `ServiceDescriptorSchema`). Kept it because the card mandates it ("its Zod CapabilitiesSchema"), it's the canonical contract reference, and it has direct test coverage (service-descriptor.test.ts round-trips through it). NOT half-wired infra ŌĆö it's a tested contract artifact in a pure schema package, same class as the already-exported `ServiceDescriptorSchema`. | Half-Wired Code Policy targets unreachable INFRASTRUCTURE, not exported+tested contract schemas a pure parser package legitimately publishes. | Drop it (rejected ŌĆö card requires it; future connector/orchestrator folds will consume it). |
| 2026-06-03 | **Phase 5 review fallback**: the `ax-code-reviewer` subagent-dispatch tool (Task/Agent) is NOT available in this orchestrated env (ToolSearch: no `Task` tool, twice). Substitute disciplined whole-branch self-review of `git diff main...HEAD` + reliance on the PR's hosted reviewers (CodeRabbit/CodeQL/semgrep/gitleaks). Self-review found + fixed the env false-positive above. | Documented precedent (TASK-145, TASK-141 same day; ARCH-4 2026-05-24). Genuinely absent, not transient. The self-review caught a real issue, validating the fallback's worth. | Block waiting for the tool (rejected ŌĆö would strand the card). |

## 2026-06-03 ŌĆö TASK-145 Harden flush-workspace-host.e2e teardown vs ENOTEMPTY rmdir mirror.git/info race

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-06-03 | Root cause of the `flush-workspace-host.e2e.test.ts` `afterEach` flake `ENOTEMPTY: directory not empty, rmdir '.../mirror.git/info'` (signature `ci:flush-workspace-host.e2e:ENOTEMPTY-rmdir-mirror-info`) is a **teardown rmdir-vs-detached-git-write race**, distinct from the TASK-137 assertion flake and the TASK-5 timeout flake. Each test stands up a REAL bare git mirror under the per-test scratch dir; git's `gc.autoDetach` defaults TRUE (git 2.52.0), so a push/fetch/receive-pack can spawn a `git gc --auto` that **detaches into a background process** and keeps writing into `mirror.git/info` (`update-server-info` writes `info/refs`; gc packs refs) AFTER the foreground git the test awaited exited. `afterEach`'s recursive `fs.rm` then `rmdir`s `mirror.git/info` while it's momentarily non-empty ŌåÆ ENOTEMPTY. Fix: a test-scoped `rmScratch(dir)` helper (`src/__tests__/rm-scratch.ts`) doing `fs.rm(dir,{recursive,force,maxRetries:10,retryDelay:25})`; the `afterEach` calls it. | `fs.rm({force:true})` does NOT retry ENOTEMPTY/EBUSY ŌĆö `force` only suppresses "path does not exist"; ONLY `maxRetries`+`retryDelay` enable Node's backoff-retry that rides out the transient race. HARNESS-ONLY: production never `fs.rm`s a live mirror (host mirror = long-lived storage; runner `commit-notify-resync.ts` is all awaited, no fire-and-forget) ŌĆö so the fix is test-teardown-only, no runner behaviour change. PROVEN by a standalone repro: a writer churning files into an `info/` dir while `fs.rm` removes the tree threw ENOTEMPTY 32/60 with `{recursive,force}` and 0/60 with `maxRetries`. TDD red-check: neuter rmScratch (strip maxRetries) ŌåÆ the regression test throws the EXACT `ENOTEMPTY ŌĆ” rmdir '.../mirror.git/info'`; restore ŌåÆ green. Stress: 25├Ś both-files + 20├Ś regression under 6├Ś CPU overcommit (Ōēł2600 active-writer trials) = 0 ENOTEMPTY. | (a) await pending git ops before teardown ŌĆö NOT actionable: the leftover writer is git's DETACHED background gc, disowned by design, un-awaitable from the test (rejected). (b) set `gc.autoDetach false` on the mirror config ŌĆö narrower (doesn't cover `update-server-info` or other in-flight writes) and `maxRetries` is the robust catch-all + the card's named remedy (rejected as belt-and-suspenders). (c) `.skip` / loosen ŌĆö loses BUG-W2/resync coverage (rejected). |

| 2026-06-03 | Phase-5 review for TASK-145: the `ax-code-reviewer` subagent-dispatch tool (Task/Agent) is NOT available in this orchestrated env (ToolSearch found no `Task` tool ŌĆö only `EnterWorktree`/`Monitor`/etc. matched). Substituted a disciplined whole-branch self-review of the staged diff vs `main` + reliance on the PR's hosted reviewers (CodeRabbit/CodeQL/semgrep/gitleaks). | Mirrors the documented 2026-06-02 + ARCH-4 (2026-05-24) fallbacks where the required review tool was genuinely absent (not transient). The diff is tiny + low-risk: TEST-ONLY (`src/__tests__/rm-scratch.ts` helper + one regression test + a 1-line `afterEach` swap), no hook surface, no IPC, no untrusted-input path, no production code, no new dependency (only `node:fs`). TDD-verified the regression test goes red against the unhardened form. | Block waiting for the tool (rejected ŌĆö absent, not transient, would strand the card); skip review (rejected ŌĆö replaced with self-review + hosted CI reviewers). |

## 2026-06-03 ŌĆö TASK-141 @ax/validator-identity (conversational-agent-identity Phase 3)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-06-03 | **Bootstrap-window signal = `workspace:read('.ax/BOOTSTRAP.md', version=parent)` returns found**, NOT the presence of a `BOOTSTRAP.md` `put` in the change set. The validator declares `optionalCalls: ['workspace:read']`. | This is the gate that closes TASK-139's un-gated bootstrap-trust window: the window must reflect the *host-committed* state, not anything the agent supplied this turn. Reading the parent version (committed state going into the turn) means only a host-seeded/validated BOOTSTRAP.md opens the window. Both presets register workspace:read (CLI=@ax/workspace-git, k8s=git-server client). | Key off a `put .ax/BOOTSTRAP.md` in `changes` (REJECTED ŌĆö an agent could re-create BOOTSTRAP.md to re-open the window and suppress the runner safety floor; exactly the hole TASK-139 flagged). Pass `parent` opaque and infer (REJECTED ŌĆö opaque, can't parse; storage-agnostic invariant). |
| 2026-06-03 | **A `put` to `.ax/BOOTSTRAP.md` is allowed ONLY when its bytes == the canonical `BOOTSTRAP_TEMPLATE` (imported from @ax/agent-identity-templates, on the eslint allow-list); any other content is HARD-VETOED (any window state).** Caught in self-review: the host seeds BOOTSTRAP.md through the SAME workspace:applyŌåÆpre-apply path as an agent (channel-web routes-agent-bootstrap, parent:null, reason:'agent-bootstrap-seed'), so an actor-blind "veto ALL BOOTSTRAP.md puts" would veto the host's own seed and silently break the entire bootstrap flow (seed is best-effort try/catch ŌåÆ no crash, just no BOOTSTRAP.md ŌåÆ agent never bootstraps). | pre-apply carries NO trusted origin signal; `reason` is agent-influenceable free-text (ipc-protocol actions.ts) so keying on reason='agent-bootstrap-seed' is a spoofable bypass. The ONLY trustworthy host-vs-agent distinction is CONTENT: host seeds the canonical compile-time constant; an agent can't forge anything *different* past byte-equality. A re-put of the EXACT canonical script is benign (re-enters the same trusted floor-by-design bootstrap). The threat (runner prompt-engine trust-note) is a NON-canonical BOOTSTRAP.md running verbatim with the floor suppressed ŌĆö byte-equality blocks exactly that. | Veto ALL BOOTSTRAP.md puts (REJECTED ŌĆö breaks the host seed). Allow by actor/reason (REJECTED ŌĆö pre-apply has no trusted actor; reason is spoofable). Allow any put during the window (REJECTED ŌĆö re-creation attack). |
| 2026-06-03 | **Post-bootstrap "flag/announce" = a structured `ctx.logger.warn('identity_self_edit', ŌĆ”)` + PASS**, not a reject and not a payload transform. The user-facing "tell the user ŌĆö it's your soul" is the runner's evolution-guidance job (TASK-139), not the veto-only validator's. | `workspace:pre-apply` is veto-only (the facade ignores transformed payloads). validator-skill's identical posture: pre-apply only ever passes or rejects; its accept-but-annotate lives on a *separate* `skills:scan` service. There is no analogous identity-scan service in this task's scope, so the audit "flag" is the structured log; git history is the durable audit trail (per design). | Add a new `identity:scan` service to annotate (REJECTED ŌĆö out of scope, no consumer; YAGNI; would be half-wired). Reject post-bootstrap identity writes (REJECTED ŌĆö design says allowed-but-flagged, hard veto is reserved for injection). |
| 2026-06-03 | **Injection scan reused by COPYING validator-skill's `regexScan` (Layer-1 pure regex) into validator-identity** (no LLM Layer-2). Identity files (IDENTITY/SOUL/AGENTS) are scanned; an injection signature is a hard `reject()`. | Invariant #2 forbids cross-plugin imports, so the scan code is duplicated (same pattern as validator-skill re-declaring SkillsScanInput). Layer-2 LLM omitted: identity self-edits are small, the agent already authored them in-session (lower injection surface than an installed third-party skill), and the soft-dep wiring adds cost for marginal recall ŌĆö keep Phase 3 thin. Memory note: if validator-skill's regex set drifts, reconcile. | Import validator-skill's scanner (REJECTED ŌĆö Invariant #2). Move the scanner into a shared pure pkg both import (DEFERRED follow-up ŌĆö only 2 consumers today; premature extraction). Include Layer-2 LLM (REJECTED ŌĆö YAGNI for in-session self-edits; adds soft-dep + budget). |
| 2026-06-03 | **`workspace:read` degradation: if unavailable, fail to POST-bootstrap policy** (treat window as closed). | Fail-closed-toward-stricter: post-bootstrap still allows identity writes (so no false veto) but never grants the bootstrap-window BOOTSTRAP.md-delete allowance to an agent that might be re-creating it. The injection scan always runs regardless. In practice both presets always register workspace:read, so this is a unit-test/degraded-harness safety net, mirroring validator-skill's llm soft-dep degrade. | Fail-open to bootstrap window (REJECTED ŌĆö would grant trust when we can't verify host-seeding). Hard-require workspace:read as a `call` (REJECTED ŌĆö a pure subscriber shouldn't crash bootstrap if a future minimal preset lacks a workspace backend; optionalCall + degrade is the established pattern). |
| 2026-06-03 | Phase-5 review: `ax-code-reviewer` subagent-dispatch (Task/Agent) tool absent in this orchestrated env (same as 2026-06-02 TASK precedent). Substitute = the `code-review` skill (high effort) over the whole-branch diff + rigorous self-review + the PR's hosted reviewers (CodeRabbit/CodeQL/semgrep). | Can't fabricate a subagent that isn't exposed. Documented fallback exists; this diff is security-sensitive (untrusted-content gating) so I run the `code-review` skill at high effort, not bare self-review. | Block on the absent tool (REJECTED ŌĆö strands the card); skip review (REJECTED ŌĆö security-sensitive). |

## 2026-06-02 ŌĆö Agent-bootstrap walk follow-ups (#298 follow-up)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-06-02 | First-run done-screen unreachability fix: defer the agent-store mutation (`setSelectedAgent` + `hydrateAgentsOnce`) out of AgentBootstrap's `create()` and into a new `finish()` handler on "Start chatting ŌåÆ". `create()` only stashes `createdAgentId` + `setStep('done')`, leaving the store empty so App's `noAgents` gate stays true and the done screen paints. | The store mutation mid-`create()` populated the agent list, flipping App.tsx's `noAgents` gate to false; in first-run `createAgentOpen` is false so `createAgentOpen \|\| noAgents` went false and AppContent unmounted AgentBootstrap before 'done' painted. Deferring the mutation keeps the gate open until the user leaves the done screen. | Force `createAgentOpen=true` for first-run (rejected ŌĆö abuses the "+ New agent" flag's meaning and the gate would still need the agent selected later); add a separate `bootstrapDone` flag to the App gate (rejected ŌĆö pushes bootstrap-flow state up into App, more coupling than deferring one store write). |
| 2026-06-02 | Extracted the gate predicate `shouldShowAgentBootstrap(...)` into its OWN module `src/lib/agent-bootstrap-gate.ts` (not exported from App.tsx). | The integration regression test must exercise the real gate predicate against the live agent store, but importing it from `App.tsx` drags the whole chat runtime + admin imports (`SkillEditor` ŌåÆ `@ax/skills/manifest`) into the test's vite graph and fails to resolve. A tiny pure module is the faithful, cheap seam. | Keep it in App.tsx and build the runtime (rejected ŌĆö heavy + the test only needs the predicate); copy the predicate into the test (rejected ŌĆö a parallel copy drifts from production). |
| 2026-06-02 | `__LOCALID_` 404 fix: match the literal prefix in history-adapter (`const AUI_LOCAL_ID_PREFIX = '__LOCALID_'`), no import. | assistant-ui mints the placeholder via a template literal `` `__LOCALID_${generateId()}` `` in `@assistant-ui/core` RemoteThreadListThreadListRuntimeCore ŌĆö there's exactly one usage site and NO exported constant, so matching the literal is the only option. A regression test guards the behavior so an assistant-ui upgrade that changes the prefix would surface. | Import a constant (rejected ŌĆö none exported); fetch and swallow the 404 silently (rejected ŌĆö the browser still logs the failed-resource console error, which is the actual complaint). |
| 2026-06-02 | Phase-5 review: the `ax-code-reviewer` subagent-dispatch tool (Task/Agent) was NOT available in this orchestrated env (ToolSearch returned no `Task` tool; only `EnterWorktree` matched). Substituted a rigorous whole-branch self-review against `main` + relied on the PR's hosted reviewers (CodeRabbit/CodeQL/semgrep). Mirrors the documented ARCH-4 fallback (2026-05-24) where a required review tool was genuinely absent. | Can't fabricate a subagent run when the tool is absent. The diff is small + low-risk (pure `@ax/channel-web` UI + one client-internal history-adapter guard; no hook surface, no untrusted-input path), so self-review is adequate; verified each fix goes red against the pre-fix code before declaring the regression tests valid. | Block waiting for the tool (rejected ŌĆö it's absent, not transient, would strand the card); skip review entirely (rejected ŌĆö replaced with documented self-review + hosted CI reviewers). |

## 2026-06-01 ŌĆö TASK-137 De-flake flush-workspace-host.e2e BUG-W2 resync assertion (residual from TASK-123)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-06-01 | Root cause of the `flush-workspace-host.e2e.test.ts > "host-side delete ŌĆ” resyncs cleanly"` **assertion** flake (not a timeout ŌĆö file ~607ms): the test's `makeHostClient` mock runs **real, fallible `git` subprocesses inside its IPC handlers** (`workspace.commit-notify`ŌåÆ`mirrorMain` rev-parse + `fetchBundleAdvance` fetch; `workspace.export-baseline-bundle`ŌåÆ`bundle create`). Under CI's severe multi-package + Docker-testcontainer starvation a SINGLE transient git subprocess hiccup (spawn EAGAIN / a starved non-zero exit) anywhere in the flushŌåÆretireŌåÆcommitŌåÆresync sequence is correctly mapped by production `commitNotifyWithResync` to a DEGRADED outcome (`'kept'` on a thrown commit-notify call; `'rolled-back'` when a transient `rev-parse` returns null ŌåÆ mock omits `actualParent`). The test then asserts `res.outcome==='accepted'` ŌåÆ `expected 'kept' to be 'accepted'`. PROVEN by fault injection: throwing on the resync-retry commit-notify deterministically yields `resyncOutcome=kept`. The git LOGIC is deterministic (200├Ś clean standalone sequence; clean even with a dirty-tree `--autostash`); only the subprocess *scheduling under starvation* is not. | This matches the card exactly (assertion flake, not timeout; the host-deleteŌåÆflushŌåÆrunner-commit resync path). It is NOT a git-ordering race (the parent-mismatch is structural: runner parent=foo-tip vs mirror head=retire) and NOT a fire-and-forget/wall-clock race like memory-strata's Observer ŌĆö so there is no un-awaited promise to await. The "ordering luck" the card names is the implicit bet that all ~6 fallible git subprocesses in the mock succeed on the FIRST try under load. | (a) bump per-test `testTimeout` ŌĆö useless, it's not a timeout (rejected); (b) `.skip` ŌĆö loses real BUG-W2/resync coverage (rejected); (c) loosen the assertion to accept `kept`/`rolled-back` ŌĆö masks a genuine "resync didn't land" regression (rejected). |
| 2026-06-01 | Fix: add a bounded **transient-failure retry seam** to the test's `git()` helper (and the mock's git calls route through it) so a starvation-induced spawn-EAGAIN / transient non-zero git exit is retried-to-completion ("settle") rather than treated as authoritative and mistranslated into a degraded outcome. Regression test: a fault-injecting mock variant that fails a git op on its first attempt and asserts the retry seam still drives the resync to `accepted`. | This is the "await the resync settle via a test seam, not ordering luck" the card asks for, adapted to the actual mechanism (fallible subprocess, not un-awaited async). It keeps the test exercising the REAL resync path while removing the starvation dependence. Production code is UNCHANGED (the degradation behavior is correct; the bug is the TEST betting every git fork succeeds first try). | bump global timeouts (wrong class); add retry to PRODUCTION `runGit` (out of scope + would change real degradation semantics ŌĆö rejected). |

## 2026-06-01 ŌĆö TASK-133 skill editor form-first (settings-unified epic, design card 10)

### TASK-133 gotchas (for TASK-134 adopt-&-edit, which builds on this editor)
- `SkillEditor` prop contract is UNCHANGED (`skillId?`, `onSaved`, `onCancel`, `api?`). All consumers (SkillsAppStore, CatalogTab, UserSkillsPanelBody) mock SkillEditor in their own tests, so the form-first rewrite didn't touch them. TASK-134 reuses the same component + `userSkillsApi` injection.
- The editor's canonical state is structured (`{name,description,connectors,body,version,extra,files,defaultAttached}`); `extra` carries unknown frontmatter keys + `sourceUrl` (folded in via `formFromParsed`) so the formŌćäraw round-trip preserves them. Save assembles a SKILL.md via `assembleSkillMd` (form mode) or uses `rawText` (advanced mode) ŌĆö both flow through the same `skills:upsert/update` wire contract `(skillMd,{defaultAttached,files})`.
- TEST GOTCHA: the connector multi-select trigger has `role="combobox"` (not `button`) ŌĆö query it with `getByRole('combobox',{name:'Add a connector'})`, the aria-label is the accessible name. The `@ax/connectors` list lib must be mocked (`vi.mock('@/lib/connectors')`) in any SkillEditor test or `listConnectors()` hits the network.
- Local test env has NO Docker ŌåÆ every `@ax/skills`/`@ax/agents`/channel-web *server* test that spins a Postgres testcontainer is auto-skipped + the file is marked "failed" (beforeAll throws). Real assertion failures = 0. CI has Docker. Don't chase these.

## 2026-06-01 ŌĆö TASK-124 Per-slot credential refs (settings-unified epic, keystone)

- **The collapse-vs-expand rule keys on `connector.capabilities.credentials.length` (the connector's slot COUNT), NOT on whether two slots resolve to the same service tag.** Spec is explicit: exactly 1 slot ŌåÆ `account:<service>` (byte-identical to today, no migration); Ōēź2 slots ŌåÆ `account:<service>:<slot>` per slot. Rationale: the design wants a connector that declares e.g. CLIENT_ID + CLIENT_SECRET to get two distinct vault rows even though both fall back to the same service tag (the connectorId) ŌĆö that's the collision being fixed. Keying on count is the design's stated rule and is the simplest deterministic predicate every mirror can reproduce from the connector it already holds.
- **`Destination.account` gains optional `slot`; `refForDestination` reconstructs from it.** `{kind:'account', service, slot}` ŌåÆ `account:<service>:<slot>` when `slot` present, else `account:<service>`. The PRESENCE of `slot` on the destination (set by the caller per the count rule) drives collapse-vs-expand at the ref layer ŌĆö `refForDestination` stays a pure deterministic function of its input, no count logic inside it. `assertNoColon` runs on `slot` too (slot names are SCREAMING_SNAKE `^[A-Z][A-Z0-9_]{0,63}$` per @ax/connectors SLOT_RE ŌĆö no colon, safe to append). All 3 mirrors + refs-fixtures.ts add a multi-slot fixture (`{service:'github', slot:'GITHUB_TOKEN'}` ŌåÆ `account:github:GITHUB_TOKEN`) AND keep the single-slot fixture (`{service:'linear'}` ŌåÆ `account:linear`) ŌĆö the byte-identical back-compat assertion.
- **`accountRef` becomes `accountRef(service, slot?)` ŌĆö the single ref-builder used by `deriveCredentialPlan` (both mirrors) and re-derived in the orchestrator fold.** `deriveCredentialPlan` computes `isMulti = connector.capabilities.credentials.length >= 2` once, then maps each slot to `ref: accountRef(serviceTagForSlot(slot, id), isMulti ? slot.slot : undefined)`. `serviceTagForSlot` unchanged. The orchestrator's `foldConnectorCaps` / `connector-card.ts` re-derive the SAME `isMulti`-gated ref locally (I2 ŌĆö no @ax/connectors import), pinned by connector-union.test.ts / connector-card.test.ts.
- **`CredentialPlanEntry` gains the destination-shaping bits so the connect-flow UI does NOT string-parse the ref.** ConnectorConnectDialog today does `entry.ref.slice('account:'.length)` to rebuild `{kind:'account', service}` ŌĆö that breaks for `account:<service>:<slot>` (would yield service=`<service>:<slot>`, failing the account regex). Instead the plan entry carries the structured `account` + optional `slotTag` (or the destination directly) so the UI builds `{kind:'account', service, slot?}` without parsing. This keeps WRITE (card/dialog ŌåÆ setDestinationCredential ŌåÆ refForDestination) and READ (orchestrator fold ŌåÆ resolve vault) addressing the SAME row. Both deriveCredentialPlan copies (connectors + channel-web) carry the field.
- **PermissionCard's two write paths (skill `approveSkill`, connector `approveConnector`) must also emit the per-slot destination.** They currently build `{kind:'account', service: s.account ?? request.connectorId}`. The card's `slots[]` (from connector-card.ts / request-capability.ts) must gain the per-slot `account`+`slotTag` (or a `multiSlot` flag) so the card writes to the same per-slot ref the orchestrator fold reads. `haveExisting` in connector-card.ts / request-capability.ts likewise checks the per-slot ref.
- **Verify-before-merge (acceptance bullet 5): no existing multi-slot connector relies on the colliding `account:<connectorId>` ref.** Checked the codebase ŌĆö there are NO seeded/default multi-slot connectors; the only connectors are test fixtures + admin-authored at runtime. Single-slot back-compat means zero migration for the common case; the per-slot change only activates for Ōēź2-slot connectors, of which none exist with stored keys. Documented in PR.
- **No new service-hook signature.** `credentials:{set,get,list,delete}` unchanged ŌĆö the ref STRING is shaped differently, that's all. Only `Destination` (+ its 3 mirrors + DestinationSchema) gains optional `slot`. Boundary-review: not a new hook surface.
- **`CredentialSlotForm` static `id="cred-payload"` was a latent multi-instance id COLLISION** ŌĆö harmless until a multi-slot connector renders one form per slot (ConnectorConnectDialog). Fixed with `useId()` per instance (label `htmlFor` association); the label text stays "API key" (NOT the slot name) so the existing `getByLabelText(/api key/i)` tests + the parent dialog's `<p>{slot}</p>` heading both hold. The in-chat PermissionCard renders its OWN per-slot Input (`id=perm-cred-<slot>`, labelled by slot name) ŌĆö unaffected.
- **`UserSkillsPanelBody.tsx` authored-skill early-approve slot-write loop is effectively DEAD** ŌĆö `@ax/skills` `pendingCapabilitiesFor` always returns `{}` post-TASK-100 (a skill carries no caps; reach is its connectors, gated by the connector card). So `AuthoredSkillListing.pendingCapabilities` is never populated; its `{kind:'account', service: s.account}` write is the collapsed single-slot form and never sees a multi-slot connector. Left unchanged (changing it = gold-plating dead code); NOT a correctness gap.
- **Verify-before-merge (acceptance bullet 5) CONFIRMED empirically:** no seeded connectors, no migration-inserted connectors (migrations only ADD COLUMNs); all connectors created at runtime by admins/authoring. No multi-slot connector with stored keys exists ŌåÆ the colliding `account:<connectorId>` ref has no live dependents ŌåÆ zero migration needed.

## 2026-06-01 ŌĆö TASK-118 Skills/Catalog tables: lead with human name, demote font-mono IDs

- **The "friendly name" IS the skill `description`.** `SkillSummary` / `AuthoredSkillListing` carry NO separate `name` field ŌĆö only `id` (the slug, e.g. `github-api`) + `description` (the human-readable summary). So "lead with the human name" = make **Description the first/lead column** and demote the `id` to a small muted `font-mono` subline rendered *under* the description in that same primary cell. The dedicated leading "ID" column is removed in all three tables (CatalogTab catalog table; UserSkillsPanelBody catalog table + authored table). The source/default/update-available badges that were attached to the old ID cell move next to the id subline.
- **Raw connector id-badges ŌåÆ demoted behind a tooltip.** `SkillSummary.connectors` is `string[]` of raw connector IDs; the skill summary does NOT carry friendly connector names (those live on `ConnectorSummary.name` in @ax/connectors, unreachable here without a new fetch + state ŌĆö that overlaps TASK-119's connector-display scope and adds a runtime cross-plugin concern). So the demotion = render a compact count summary ("N connectors") whose raw ids live behind the shadcn `Tooltip` (installed but previously unused) + a `title` attr for accessibility/testability. Zero connectors keeps the existing em-dash. Rejected: (a) fetch connector summaries to map idŌåÆname in these tables ŌĆö heavier, overlaps TASK-119, adds network+state; (b) leave the raw id-badges as the connectors column unchanged ŌĆö fails acceptance sub-point 2.
- **Localized to table column structure** (per dispatch note: sibling TASK-119 also touches UserSkillsPanelBody) ŌĆö no changes to dialogs, handlers, fetch logic, or the authored-section approve flow.
- **Review fix ŌĆö `aria-label` not `title` on the ConnectorRefsCell trigger.** A `title` attr on a Radix `TooltipTrigger` fires a SECOND native browser tooltip alongside the Radix one (double-tooltip wart). Moved the machine-readable id list to `aria-label` (`"N connectors: id1, id2"`) ŌĆö read by screen readers + reachable by tests, no native tooltip. Regression test in `ConnectorRefsCell.test.tsx` pins `title === null`.

## 2026-06-01 ŌĆö TASK-109 User-facing connector connect flow (keyMode JIT vs shared-key consent)

- **The connect flow derives the credential plan + consent gate CLIENT-SIDE from the full `Connector` (`getConnector(id)`), NOT a `connectors:resolve` BFF call.** There is no HTTP route for `connectors:resolve` ŌĆö only the 5 `/admin/connectors[/:id]` CRUD routes; `getConnector` already returns `capabilities`. So TASK-96's derivation (`deriveCredentialPlan`/`requiresSharedKeyConsent`/`sharedKeyConsentMessage`/`accountRef`/`serviceTagForSlot`) is **re-declared locally in `lib/connectors.ts`** ŌĆö mirroring the existing local `refForDestination` re-declaration in `lib/credentials.ts`. Rationale: `@ax/connectors` is NOT on eslint's runtime-import allowlist (only `@ax/credentials` is among the credential-ish plugins), and channel-web doesn't even devDepend on it; a runtime import is an I2 violation. A unit test pins the local behavior + the EXACT `SHARED_KEY_CONSENT_COPY` string (the consent text is a security contract). Alternatives rejected: (a) add a `connectors:resolve` HTTP route + lib wrapper ŌåÆ new wire surface for data `getConnector` already carries; half-extra. (b) add `@ax/connectors` to the import allowlist for a drift-guard runtime import ŌåÆ widens the cross-plugin runtime surface for a test convenience; the `refForDestination` precedent is local-re-decl + pin-by-test, not allowlist-widening.
- **keyMode ŌåÆ write route is the EXISTING destination-credential split, no new wire:** `personal`ŌåÆ`scope:'user'` via `setDestinationCredential`ŌåÆ`/settings/destinations/account/credential` (server forces ownerId=actor, any authed user); `workspace`ŌåÆ`scope:'global'` via `/admin/destinations/account/credential` (`requireAdmin`). The consent gate is the design's "act as you" moment surfaced BEFORE the workspace key-entry form is reachable; `requiresSharedKeyConsent` = `keyMode==='workspace' || visibility==='shared'`. A non-admin opening a workspace connector can't store the global key (admin route is admin-gated) ŌåÆ surface "an admin provides this shared key", not a raw 403. Destination = `{kind:'account', service: slot.account ?? connectorId}` ŌåÆ ref `account:<service>` ŌĆö the SAME row TASK-96/97/112 read/write (divergent-ref trap avoided).
- **Connected/not = REAL credential presence, mirroring `CredentialSlotRow`.** Fetch `myCredentials.list()` (user-plan slots) / `adminCredentials.list()` (global-plan slots) once, match `c.ref===ref && c.scope===planScope`; connected iff every plan slot has a stored credential. **Empty plan** (no credential slots ŌĆö an MCP-no-key connector) ŌćÆ connected (nothing to prompt). The user list only returns the actor's own creds, so ref+scope match suffices (the JIT account flow already writes with `ownerId:null`).

## 2026-06-01 ŌĆö TASK-116 KeysTab/CredentialsTab humane errors, no raw-ref leak, friendlier service field

- **Friendlier "Service" field = relabel + silent slugify, NOT a picker.** The card asks for "a friendlier label/picker that does not expose slug grammar." There is NO service catalog anywhere in the codebase ŌĆö `account:<service>` is a free-form slug any skill slot binds to via `account: <service>`; the only sources of service NAMES are the connectors list + the account-usage map (services already referenced). A true picker would need a new catalog wire surface (YAGNI / out of scope). So: keep the text input, relabel to "Which service is this key for?" with a human-name placeholder ("e.g. Linear, GitHub, Notion"), drop the slug-grammar validation copy + `ACCOUNT_SERVICE_RE` early-validation, and add `toServiceSlug()` that lowercases + hyphenates + caps-64 the user's input on SAVE so the result always satisfies the server grammar `/^[a-z][a-z0-9-]{0,63}$/` (`credentials-admin-routes/destination-routes.ts`). Save enabled iff `toServiceSlug(input).length>0 && value.length>0`. Inferable from code+conventions (not a human product call): the contract row is unchanged, grammar is enforced silently rather than surfaced.
- **Humane error = sibling pattern + fixed next-step.** Replace the 5 `setError(String(e))` with a module-level `humanError(e) = e instanceof Error ? e.message : String(e)` (exact ConnectorsTab/ConnectorConnectDialog idiom). The destructive Alert leads with the card-mandated next-step sentence ("We couldn't save your key. Check it's correct and try again ŌĆö your admin can help if it keeps failing.") and shows the technical message as a secondary muted detail.
- **Unknown ref (`other` shape) no longer renders raw `kind:value`.** Map the `kind` segment to a human noun (`providerŌåÆModel provider`, `mcpŌåÆConnector`, `routineŌåÆScheduled task`, fallback "Other credential") and a calm "Managed elsewhere" caption; never render the bare `provider:anthropic`-style string. Rows stay read-only.
- **No hook/IPC/boundary/dep change ŌĆö pure channel-web UI; security-checklist not triggered** (untrusted ref text still renders through auto-escaped React text nodes, same as before).
- **Review (Phase 5, ran `/code-review --effort high` ŌĆö the `ax-code-reviewer` Task subagent isn't available in this env, logged substitution) caught a prototype-key footgun:** `OTHER_KIND_LABEL[kind] ?? 'Other credential'` returns the INHERITED function for `kind==='toString'`/`'constructor'` (and an object for `'__proto__'`), which would crash the row render. Fixed with `Object.hasOwn(OTHER_KIND_LABEL, kind)` + regression test. General rule for a plain-object lookup keyed by ANY external string (even server-issued metadata): guard with `Object.hasOwn` / `Object.create(null)` / a `Map` ŌĆö a bare `obj[k] ?? fallback` leaks the prototype chain.

Alternatives rejected: (a) keep `UserSkillsPanel.tsx` as dead code (Half-Wired Code Policy forbids); (b) delete `UserSkillsPanel.test.tsx` outright (loses ~20 behavioral tests for live code).

## 2026-06-01 ŌĆö TASK-114 Connectors walk polish: re-propose dedup + Vite /settings dev-proxy

- **Re-propose dedup belongs in `connectors:install-authored`, NOT the orchestrator card path or the `connector_propose` tool.** Bug (TASK-101 walk): a warm-turn re-propose of an ALREADY-ACTIVE connector reset the authored draft to `pending`, and `fireUpfrontConnectorCards` (orchestrator) re-fired the upfront approval card every turn (it keys off a pending draft; `applyAuthoredConnectorGrant` clears `upfrontConnectorCardsByConv` on approval so every warm turn re-evaluates). Root cause = `installAuthoredConnector` always (re)wrote a pending draft with no check against the registry TASK-113 promoted into. Fix at the single chokepoint: pass the plugin's OWN live `localStore` (the registry, `ConnectorStore`) into the handler alongside the authored-draft store (both same-plugin ŌåÆ no cross-plugin import, no new `calls` edge), and BEFORE upserting, `registry.getByIdNotDeleted(ownerUserId, connectorId)` ŌĆö if non-null it's a NO-OP (write nothing, return `{connectorId, status:'active'}`). No pending draft re-created Ō¤╣ orchestrator card path sees nothing to card. ONE fix covers BOTH acceptance sub-points. The tool path needed no parallel guard (it calls the hook).
- **Equivalence rule = pure id match, owner-scoped (simplest-correct, per the card's scoping note).** An active (not-deleted) registry connector owned by the SAME user with the SAME connector id. NOT a capability-fill comparison (that would be a product decision the card said to avoid). `getByIdNotDeleted` already filters `owner_user_id` + `deleted_at IS NULL`, so: (a) a different user's connector never triggers dedup (pinned by a cross-owner test), and (b) a SOFT-DELETED (un-approved/removed) connector returns null ŌåÆ falls through to the normal pending+card path ŌåÆ re-approval required (correct security posture ŌĆö tombstone never silently resurrects reach).
- **Wire change = widen `InstallAuthoredOutput.status` `'pending'` ŌåÆ `'pending'|'active'`** (+ its zod `InstallAuthoredOutputSchema` union + the `@ax/tool-connector-propose` `ConnectorProposeOutput.status` mirror, which already passes `out.status` through). Only hook-surface change; `status` is a lifecycle verdict, storage/transport-agnostic, no leak; no boundary-review concern. SECURITY: the short-circuit only fires when an ALREADY-APPROVED (human-gated, TASK-113-promoted) connector exists ŌĆö it grants ZERO new reach (writes nothing) and cannot escalate/bypass approval; if no registry match, the pending+card path is byte-for-byte unchanged.
- **Vite dev-proxy `/settings` gap (item 2):** `packages/channel-web/vite.config.ts` proxy forwarded only `/auth`,`/admin`,`/api` to `AX_BACKEND_URL`; the connector connect/credential write POSTs to `/settings/*`, so a local Vite walk 404'd. Added `'/settings': { target: backendUrl, changeOrigin: false, ws: false }`. Config-only, no test: the MOCK middleware (offline mode) has no `/settings` connector handlers and the walk uses PROXY mode (real backend); real deploys are same-origin so unaffected. (Distinct config from TASK-106 but same dev-parity theme.)
- **Alternatives rejected:** (a) dedup in the orchestrator `fireUpfrontConnectorCards` card path ŌåÆ symptom-patch, leaves the spurious pending draft (fails acceptance sub-point 1's "no pending draft re-created"). (b) dedup in the `connector_propose` tool ŌåÆ the tool has no registry access without an `@ax/connectors` runtime import (I2 violation). (c) capability-fill equivalence ŌåÆ product decision, out of scope.

## 2026-05-31 ŌĆö TASK-104 Fix postgres-testcontainer teardown 57P01 flake at root

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-31 | Fix the uncaught `57P01` ("terminating connection due to administrator command") teardown flake with ONE shared helper `stopPostgresContainer(container)` in `@ax/test-harness`, and migrate all 105 postgres-testcontainer suites (106 call sites) to call it in `afterAll` in place of `await container.stop()`. The helper installs a temporary `uncaughtException`+`unhandledRejection` guard that swallows ONLY the benign 57P01 shape (by `code==='57P01'` OR the message substring), awaits `container.stop()` + one macrotask tick (the socket error surfaces async AFTER stop() resolves), then removes its listeners. No-ops on `undefined`. | Root-caused + reproduced: when `container.stop()` SIGTERMs postgres, the server kills every connection still bound to an OPEN `pg.Pool`. A test-created `pg.Pool` has NO `'error'` listener, so Node re-emits the connection error as an **uncaughtException** ŌĆö and vitest counts an uncaught exception during teardown as a suite failure even when every assertion passed (exact card symptom "This error originated ... while it was running"; control run = `Tests 1 passed / Errors 1 error ŌåÆ EXIT 1`, helper run = EXIT 0). The card's two options are "drain pools before stop" (already mostly done in per-package `afterEach`, but a tick-late socket error still races) and "swallow the benign 57P01" ŌĆö the helper does the swallow as a deterministic BACKSTOP so the residual race can't red the suite, applied through one helper to avoid per-package drift (the card's stated preference). Typed against a minimal `{ stop(): Promise<unknown> }` so `@ax/test-harness` does NOT take a runtime dep on `@testcontainers/postgresql`. Every postgres package already devDepends on `@ax/test-harness`, so no package.json changes. | (a) Per-package `afterEach` pool-draining only ŌĆö rejected: it's necessary but not sufficient; the error surfaces a tick AFTER `destroy()`/`close()` resolves and races `container.stop()`, and TASK-94 already saw it red CI despite drained pools. (b) A global vitest `setupFiles` process guard installed for the WHOLE run ŌĆö rejected: it would mask a real 57P01 raised DURING a test (not just teardown); scoping the guard to the `stop()` window keeps real errors loud. (c) `fileParallelism:false` / serialize the suites ŌĆö rejected: masks the race, slows CI, doesn't root-cause. (d) Add `pool.on('error')` to every test pool ŌĆö rejected: ~100-file churn vs one helper, and still leaves the unawaited-rejection variant. |

## 2026-05-31 ŌĆö TASK-89 Make server early-bind authoritative (retry bind + 503 POST) to close cold-respawn 404 at the source

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-31 | **Replace the single best-effort early-bind in `channel-web/src/server/routes-chat.ts` `postMessage` with a bounded-retry loop, then 503 the POST if the bind never lands.** New helper `bindActiveReqIdAuthoritative(bus, ctx, {conversationId, sessionId, reqId, logger})` ŌåÆ boolean. Loop: capped-exponential backoff (start 25ms, ├Ś2, cap ~150ms) gated on a `Date.now()+BIND_TOTAL_BUDGET_MS` deadline (BIND_TOTAL_BUDGET_MS=400). On success ŌåÆ return true (ŌåÆ 202). On bind throw ŌåÆ keep the existing `chat_bind_session_failed` warn telemetry, sleep the clamped backoff, retry. Budget spent ŌåÆ return false ŌåÆ POST `res.status(503).json({error:'bind-unavailable'})`. | Card contract is "retry the bind, then 503 the POST if it can't be established." 400ms is small (sub-perceptible to a user; the SSE GET race is microseconds) yet absorbs a read-after-write replica lag race or a brief DB blip ŌĆö the realistic transient causes of a first-try bind failure when the row was JUST created/fetched in the same request. The happy path binds first try (one call, zero added latency) ŌåÆ 202 exactly as today. 503 (not 202) on persistent failure means the client never gets a reqId whose `GET /api/chat/stream/:reqId` can never 200 ŌĆö it surfaces the existing CONNECTION_LOST banner + manual retry (TASK-88's client path), which re-POSTs the whole turn. This fix REDUCES how often TASK-88's ~30s client SSE-open budget is even exercised (the 404 window no longer opens on the happy path), without contradicting it. | (a) keep single best-effort + rely only on TASK-88's client retry (rejected: that's the mitigation, not the source fix this card asks for; leaves the 404 window open); (b) await the orchestrator's post-open-session bind instead (rejected: that's seconds later for a cold pod ŌĆö the exact latency this closes; and routes-chat fires agent:invoke fire-and-forget, it can't await the orchestrator); (c) huge retry budget / unbounded (rejected: a genuinely-missing conversation would hang the POST; 400ms bounds it and 503 lets the client retry cleanly). |
| 2026-05-31 | **If `bus.hasService('conversations:bind-session')` is false, return 503 immediately (do not 202).** Keep the `hasService` guard (matches the orchestrator's identical convention ŌĆö bind-session is NOT a manifest-declared call; both routes-chat and orchestrator.ts gate it via `hasService`). | A bind service that isn't registered means the bind can NEVER be established ŌåÆ a 202 would hand back a reqId whose stream can never open, which is exactly the failure this card kills. In prod the k8s preset ALWAYS co-deploys @ax/conversations (verified: only preset booting channel-web, and it boots conversations), so this branch is effectively unreachable in prod; it's the correct contract-honoring fallback for a degenerate preset. Not declaring it in the manifest preserves the established peer convention and keeps blast radius off every harness's verifyCalls walk. | (a) promote bind-session to a hard manifest `call` (rejected: churns every channel-web test harness's verifyCalls + diverges from the orchestrator's hasService convention for the SAME hook ŌĆö one source of truth for the convention); (b) keep silent fall-through to 202 when absent (rejected: that's the bug ŌĆö 202 for an un-openable reqId). |
| 2026-05-31 | **Phase-5 review substitution: the `ax-code-reviewer` subagent + the Agent/Task dispatch tool were UNAVAILABLE in this orchestrated env (same gap as TASK-87/34/35), so I ran the `code-review` skill ŌĆö whose finder/verifier angles ALSO need the Agent tool ŌĆö and performed its 9 angles myself directly over the in-context whole-branch `main...HEAD` diff.** No actionable findings: the retry loop is bounded (no infinite spin ŌĆö `remaining<=0` returns false before sleeping; wait clamped to remaining budget; happy path = 1 call, returns true immediately); telemetry + `existingActiveSessionId ?? placeholder` behavior preserved; the only behavior change (absent service / persistent failure ŌåÆ 503 instead of silent 202) is the card's intent. REUSE angle: no shared backoff/retry util exists (`@ax/core/util` has only safe-path + with-timeout; transport.ts's client loop is a different runtime/semantics ŌĆö I2 makes a cross-boundary util premature), so inlining matches precedent. Test-race check: `chatRunMockPlugin`'s `agent:invoke` mock does NOT call `conversations:bind-session`, so the happy-path `bindCalls===1` assertion is deterministic (not racy on the fire-and-forget orchestrator bind). The PR's hosted reviewers (CodeRabbit/CodeQL/semgrep/gitleaks) are the second pair of eyes in CI. | Block on the missing subagent (rejected: env capability gap, not a code issue; small additive pure-control-flow diff, 7 tests, hosted-reviewer-covered). | ŌĆö |
| 2026-05-31 | **Scope strictly server-side (channel-web) ŌĆö do NOT touch transport.ts.** The card's "client retries the whole turn" is already satisfied: transport.ts `sendMessages` throws on any non-OK POST ŌåÆ runtime onError ŌåÆ CONNECTION_LOST-class banner + manual retry (a deliberate re-POST). A POST 503 flows through that existing path unchanged. | Card explicitly says "Scope (server-side ŌĆö channel-web)". TASK-88 owns the client. | Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |

| 2026-05-30 | **Fix the capability-loss bypass AT THE PARSER (`parseSkillManifest`), not at the gate: hard-reject (`invalid-manifest`) any of `allowedHosts`/`credentials`/`mcpServers`/`packages` declared at the TOP LEVEL of a manifest (outside `capabilities:`).** | The card framed it as "the gate must classify pending", but the gate (`classifyProposal`) was already correct ŌĆö it classifies on its input. The single-source-of-truth fix is to make the parser (the one contract authority, shared by global/user/authored/promote flows) reject the misplaced keys, so a dropped/stripped-cap manifest is a loud structural reject regardless of which flow or which doc drift produced it. Defense-in-depth that holds even if the docs drift again. | (a) Make the GATE re-derive caps from the raw manifest text (REJECTED: duplicates the parser, a second source of truth, I4 violation); (b) have the gate treat "empty caps + a body that mentions hosts" as pending (REJECTED: unbounded heuristic on untrusted body text, false-positive minefield, not a real boundary); (c) silently MOVE top-level caps under `capabilities` in the parser (REJECTED: silently rewriting an adversarial manifest is exactly the wrong instinct ŌĆö fail loud, make the author re-draft). |

The docs were the drifted artifact (TASK-74 wrote `id`+semver+top-level caps). Moving the docs to the parser keeps ONE documented contract; changing the parser to accept `id`/semver/top-level would weaken the validation surface. | Change the parser to accept `id` as an alias (REJECTED: two identity keys = ambiguity + a wider attack surface; `name` is already the established key across every other skill flow). |

No hook SIGNATURE added/changed, no new subscriber payload. | The five-invariant boundary-review checklist fires on hook-surface changes; this PR only changes a handler's internal data source + prunes dead declarations. | ŌĆö |
| 2026-05-30 | **The read-then-`replaceTranscript` (DELETE+re-INSERT, seq renumbered `1..N`) in drop-turn drops git's CAS-parent without a replacement version check, and this is SAFE.** The transcript store is single-writer-per-session (decisions.md:542 design note, NOT git CAS); drop-turn fires from `chat:turn-end` AFTER the turn shipped + completed, so the runner isn't mid-append. `getTranscriptPrefixHash` hashes line CONTENT + `\n` terminators in seq ORDER (not seq VALUES), so dense renumbering after a drop is hash-invisible ŌĆö a resume reads the new max+bytes consistently. A worst-case stale-`fromSeq` append after a drop hits the existing host delta-ship guard ŌåÆ `resync-required` ŌåÆ runner re-ships via replace-transcript (fail-safe, same posture as git's old parent-mismatch). | Removing the CAS-parent looked like a regression vs. the git path's `read.version`-as-parent (TASK drop-turn-against-git test). It isn't: the row store's concurrency model is single-writer + the resync net, not optimistic-CAS. Adding a bespoke version check would duplicate machinery the append guard already provides. | (a) add a version/optimistic-lock arg to replaceTranscript (REJECTED: re-creates CAS the store deliberately doesn't use; the resync guard covers the race); (b) read+rewrite inside one DB transaction (REJECTED: getTranscriptBytes + replaceTranscript are separate hooks/store calls; the single-writer invariant already serializes, and cross-call txn would need a new store method for no real-world race). |

## 2026-05-30 ŌĆö TASK-74 Skills Part D: skill_propose chokepoint + hybrid gate + workspace-draft retirement

|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-30 | **`skill.propose` IPC action carries the bundle EXTRA files as `files[]` (path+contents) IN the JSON envelope ŌĆö NOT a separate `blob.put` upload from the runner.** Envelope: `{ manifestYaml, bodyMd, files[], capabilityProposal, origin: 'authored' }` ŌåÆ `{ skillId, status }`. The host hook `skills:propose` writes the files to the blob store host-side (reuses the merged D2 `createBlobBundleStore` ŌåÆ `blob:put`, exactly as `skills:upsert` does). | Bundle extra files are tiny (validateBundleFiles caps: Ōēż16 files, Ōēż512 KiB total) ŌĆö orders of magnitude under the 4 MiB JSON `MAX_FRAME`, so the artifact_publish reason for a raw octet-stream channel (unbounded artifact bytes) does NOT apply. Sending files[] inline keeps the manifest + body + files together for ATOMIC structural re-validation at the host chokepoint, and reuses the exact byte-store path `skills:upsert` already uses (one storage path, I4). | (a) mirror artifact_publish's `blob.put` + a `skill.propose` metadata envelope referencing a `bundleSha256` (REJECTED ŌĆö adds a second runner blob channel + a two-call atomicity gap for sub-512 KiB text files that fit the JSON frame trivially; the bytes don't need the uncapped channel); (b) one fused IPC action carrying bytes+metadata (REJECTED ŌĆö not needed; files are text and small). |

The SDK-config HARD veto in `workspace:pre-apply` (`.claude/settings.json` etc.) STAYS ŌĆö it is unrelated to skills (guards transcript/upload commits too). | Design D1: "the pre-apply veto survives as a structural gate on skill_propose ŌĆö it keyed off a WRITE CHOKEPOINT, not git." `skills:propose` is that chokepoint now; `.ax/draft-skills` (the only thing the SKILL.md pre-apply branch scanned) no longer exists. `skills:scan` is storage/transport-agnostic (no git/workspace vocab). | (a) keep the validator on `workspace:pre-apply` (REJECTED ŌĆö `.ax/draft-skills` writes are gone; it would never fire for skills, and the card explicitly says fire at the propose chokepoint via a skills:scan-style hook NOT workspace:pre-apply); (b) inline the scan in `skills:propose` with no hook (REJECTED ŌĆö the scan is a separate plugin's concern w/ an LLM soft-dep; a subscriber hook keeps validator-skill decoupled, I2). |

## 2026-05-30 ŌĆö TASK-68 Attachments & artifacts onto the blob store; /ephemeral working tier (drop attachments:commit)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-30 | **Add the REQUEST-direction binary IPC channel as `client.callBinaryUpload(action, payload, bytes)`** ŌĆö POSTs the raw blob bytes as `application/octet-stream` body with the JSON metadata in the `x-ax-payload` header; host dispatcher reads the RAW body (NOT `readJsonBody`, so it bypasses the 4 MiB `MAX_FRAME` cap, like the existing response-direction streaming) up to a 100 MiB ceiling. First (and only) action: `blob.put`. Returns small JSON `{sha256,size}`. | callBinary today is response-direction only (hostŌåÆrunner, streams bytes to a temp file). Upload is the mirror: runnerŌåÆhost raw bytes, JSON envelope back. Octet-stream body matches design Part A ("bytes ride the callBinary octet-stream channel, never the 4 MiB JSON frame"). Header-carried JSON keeps the body pure bytes so the host streams it without a multipart parse. | (a) base64 the bytes into a JSON `blob.put` body (rejected ŌĆö re-introduces the 33% tax + 4 MiB cap that BUG-W3 removed); (b) multipart (rejected ŌĆö heavier parse, no benefit over header+raw-body for a single blob). |
| 2026-05-30 | **`blob.get` over IPC is response-direction: extend the EXISTING `callBinary` action union to include `blob.get`** (JSON request `{sha256}` ŌåÆ octet-stream response streamed to a temp file). The runner reads the temp file. | The runner-side materialization of `/ephemeral/uploads` needs blob bytes from the host store; the response-direction callBinary already streams binary to disk under the disk-bounded cap ŌĆö `blob.get` is exactly that shape. No new transport, just a new action name in the union + a host dispatcher path. | A JSON `blob.get` returning base64 (rejected ŌĆö same cap/tax problem). |
| 2026-05-30 | **Artifacts: keep the sandbox-side `artifact_publish` executor's lstatŌåÆsize-capŌåÆreadŌåÆsha256, re-point the path allowlist to `/ephemeral/artifacts/**`, then the executor streams the read bytes to the host via `callBinaryUpload('blob.put', ŌĆ”)` and calls a new host IPC action `artifact.publish` to insert the metadata row** `{conversationId, sha256, displayName, mediaType, size}`, returning `ax://artifact/<id>`. Durability is observable at `artifact_publish` return (the blob.put success), not turn-end. | Design Part C, outbound. The executor already does the validation + sha256; it gains the blob.put + metadata insert. The host owns the metadata row (the runner has no DB). The two IPC calls (blob.put bytes, artifact.publish metadata) are idempotent on sha256 so a retry is safe. | Have the host re-read the file (rejected ŌĆö host can't reach the sandbox `/ephemeral`); single fused IPC action carrying bytes+metadata (rejected ŌĆö bytes must ride octet-stream, metadata is JSON; splitting keeps the body pure). |
| 2026-05-30 | **Artifact namespace moves to `/ephemeral/artifacts/**` but ALSO keep `/permanent/workspace/**` publishable (Pattern A double-home).** The allowlist gains `/ephemeral/artifacts/` (primary) and retains `/permanent/workspace/` (the rare ax-hosted-project case the design's "what git keeps" section calls an intentional double-home). Drop `/permanent/.ax/artifacts/`. | Design: `/ephemeral/artifacts/` is the new artifact namespace; `/permanent/workspace/` Pattern A code may still publish a snapshot as an artifact ("git holds editable history, the blob holds the immutable shared snapshot"). The old `.ax/artifacts/` namespace is retired with the git artifact path. | Keep `.ax/artifacts/` (rejected ŌĆö that's the git artifact path Part C removes); `/ephemeral/artifacts/` only (rejected ŌĆö drops the legit Pattern A double-home the design names). |
| 2026-05-30 | **Inbound uploads: `attachments:store-temp` already holds the bytes; on send, REPLACE `attachments:commitŌåÆworkspace:apply` with a new `attachments:commit` impl that calls `blob:put` host-side + inserts an `attachments_v1_files` metadata row** `{conversationId, sha256, displayName, mediaType, size, path}` and returns the same `CommitOutput` shape (path now `.ax/uploads/<conv>/<turnId>/<file>` kept as the stable transcript reference key). NO git commit. The shared-mirror parent-mismatch race is gone with the `workspace:apply` call. | Design Part C inbound: store via blob:put host-side, attachments row, drop the git path. Keeping the `attachments:commit` hook NAME + output shape means routes-chat.ts and the transcript `attachment` block path reference are unchanged ŌĆö minimal blast radius, and the path string stays the download/scope key. | Rename the hook (rejected ŌĆö churns routes-chat + transcript schema for no gain); store at upload time instead of commit time (rejected ŌĆö the conversationId/turnId binding only exists at send/commit, and store-temp is pre-conversation; commit is the right chokepoint). |
| 2026-05-30 | **Download (`GET /api/files` ŌåÆ `attachments:download`): resolve pathŌåÆrowŌåÆ`blob:get`ŌåÆstream instead of `workspace:read`.** Keep the full ACL ladder (normalize ŌåÆ owner-gate via conversations:get ŌåÆ path-scope via transcript scan ŌåÆ fetch). The path-scope check still scans the transcript (unchanged); only the final byte-fetch swaps `workspace:read` for a metadata-row lookup keyed by (conversationId, path) ŌåÆ sha256 ŌåÆ `blob:get`. Artifacts resolve the same way (artifact row keyed by (conversationId, path or artifactId) ŌåÆ sha256 ŌåÆ blob:get). | Design Part C download. The ACL is the load-bearing security boundary and is untouched; only the storage backend behind it changes. Move uploads off git Ō¤╣ the file is no longer in `/permanent`, so it MUST be materialized to a path the agent can Read. `/ephemeral/uploads/` is the design's named home. Session-start is correct: the conversationId is known at boot (session.get-config), uploads are immutable per conversation, and a lazy-per-turn fetch can't satisfy a model that Reads the path before any attachment-translation runs. ## 2026-05-30 ŌĆö TASK-71 @ax/blob-store-s3 backend + MinIO-in-kind + GCS Workload-Identity chart

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-30 | Implement `@ax/blob-store-s3` as a SECOND registrar of the EXISTING `blob:put/get/stat/delete` hook surface (TASK-65). Re-export structurally-identical `Blob*Output` types + `Blob*OutputSchema` zod schemas (the I2 two-backend pattern, like storage-sqlite/storage-postgres). Do NOT change the hook contract: payloads stay sha256/bytes/size only; bucket/endpoint/region/creds are plugin CONFIG, never payload fields. | Card scope + invariant I1 (storage-agnostic hooks). The schemas co-locate per-registration (ARCH-13 drift guard); a structurally-identical copy keeps the two backends honest. | Import the schemas from blob-store-fs (REJECTED ŌĆö cross-plugin import, invariant I2). |
| 2026-05-30 | Use `@aws-sdk/client-s3` pinned EXACT (no caret) to the latest 3.1057.0 ŌĆö the one new dependency. S3Client with `forcePathStyle:true` (MinIO/GCS need path-style), `endpoint`+`region` config, credentials resolved via the SDK's default provider chain when not given (so Workload Identity / IRSA / GKE metadata works with NO static keys in the tree). MinIO dev keys come from config (sourced from the credential vault / a k8s Secret), never hardcoded. | Card names @aws-sdk/client-s3; exact-pin matches the repo's "pin everything" posture + makes pnpm audit deterministic on the pinned range. Default provider chain is exactly how Workload Identity injects creds with zero static keys. | aws4fetch / minio SDK (REJECTED ŌĆö card names @aws-sdk; one impl covers all S3-compatible targets); caret range (REJECTED ŌĆö repo pins). |
| 2026-05-30 | Reuse the SAME content-addressed store SEMANTICS as fs: object key = `<sha[0:2]>/<sha[2:4]>/<sha>` within the bucket; put hashes bytes in-process (compute sha256, PutObject under the key); get re-verifies the digest and throws `corrupt` on mismatch; stat = HeadObject; delete = DeleteObject (idempotent, swallow NotFound/404); put idempotent via HeadObject fast-path before PutObject. Same SHA256_REGEX gate before building any key (no traversal via key). | Mirrors fs backend's integrity guarantees so the shared conformance suite passes identically; the key prefix is irrelevant to S3 but keeps parity + avoids one giant flat prefix. | Let S3 compute checksums (REJECTED ŌĆö we want digest re-verify on read regardless of backend; content-addressing is OUR invariant). |
| 2026-05-30 | Per-deployment registrar selection in the k8s preset via a new `blob` config block (discriminated `backend: 'fs' \| 's3'`), driven by `AX_BLOB_BACKEND` env (default `fs`). Exactly ONE of createBlobStoreFsPlugin / createBlobStoreS3Plugin is pushed ŌĆö mirrors workspace local/git-protocol. fs root defaults to a sibling dir on the workspace PVC; s3 reads endpoint/region/bucket/forcePathStyle + optional access-key/secret-key env. NOTE: blob-store-fs was NOT yet wired into the preset by TASK-65 (no consumer) ŌĆö this card wires BOTH backends in as the selectable seam (closes the half-wired window for fs too, justified because the canary round-trip exercises whichever is selected). | Invariant I3 (no half-wired): the s3 backend must be reachable via config. Wiring the selection is the only way "a deployment can select fs OR s3" is true. The canary test boots the selected plugin through bootstrap. | Wire only s3, leave fs dangling (REJECTED ŌĆö selection requires both arms; and fs being unwired is the pre-existing gap this card naturally closes). |
| 2026-05-30 | MinIO in kind: render a MinIO Deployment+Service+Secret in the chart, gated `minio.enabled` (default false in prod values, true in kind-dev-values), single-replica emptyDir (dev parity, not durable). Prod GCS: `blob.backend: s3` with endpoint=`https://storage.googleapis.com`, Workload-Identity ServiceAccount annotation, NO static keys (creds via the SDK metadata provider). The s3 backend's bucket/endpoint/region are plugin config; access keys (dev/MinIO only) ride a k8s Secret ŌåÆ env, NEVER committed. | Card scope (Phase 6) + design Part A. emptyDir MinIO is fine for dev/test parity; durability is a prod-GCS concern. Workload Identity = the design's "no static keys" requirement. | Bitnami MinIO subchart (REJECTED ŌĆö heavier, another chart dep + Bitnami's flaky index; a small Deployment is enough for dev parity). |
| 2026-05-30 | Phase-5 review caught a CONFIRMED runtime-compat bug: AWS SDK JS v3 Ōēź early-2025 (3.1057 here) defaults `requestChecksumCalculation: WHEN_SUPPORTED`, adding an x-amz-checksum-crc32 / STREAMING-ŌĆ”-TRAILER header to PutObject that MinIO (pre-trailer releases) and GCS's S3 endpoint REJECT ŌĆö so a plain blob:put would fail against exactly the dev (MinIO) + prod (GCS) targets this backend exists for. The in-memory fake can't see it (no real HTTP). Fix: pin `requestChecksumCalculation` + `responseChecksumValidation` to `WHEN_REQUIRED` in buildS3Client (restores pre-2025 behavior every S3-compatible server accepts) + a build-client.test.ts regression guard that fails if the pin is dropped. | This is the design's "MinIO-in-kind round-trip ACTUALLY works" acceptance criterion ŌĆö without the pin it silently doesn't. Our own digest re-verify-on-read is the integrity guarantee, so dropping the SDK's redundant checksum costs nothing. | Leave the default (REJECTED ŌĆö breaks MinIO+GCS); per-server conditional (REJECTED ŌĆö WHEN_REQUIRED is correct for AWS too; no downside). |
| 2026-05-30 | Phase-4 whole-branch gate caught a real integration break: wiring blob-store-fs into the preset by DEFAULT made every preset acceptance test that boots via `bootstrap` with `backend: git-protocol` try to `mkdir /var/lib/ax-next/blobs` (the prod default fs-root for the non-local workspace backend) ŌĆö EACCES in the test sandbox. Fix: add explicit `blob: { backend: 'fs', root: path.join(tmp, 'blobs') }` to each preset-booting test config (the prod `/var/lib/ax-next/blobs` default is CORRECT ŌĆö the chart mounts a PVC there; only the test env needs the override). The local-backend tests were already fine (root derives under their tmp repoRoot). | Per-test override is explicit + mirrors how those tests already pass an explicit workspace; the prod default stays correct. The break is exactly the "shared-table / repo-wide" class the whole-branch gate exists to catch (yolo-ship Phase 4). | Change the preset's git-protocol default to a tmp path (REJECTED ŌĆö wrong for prod); skip the blob plugin in those tests (REJECTED ŌĆö they boot the REAL preset on purpose; dropping it hides the wiring). |
| 2026-05-30 | Lockfile recipe DIVERGES from TASK-65's "splice importer block only": this package adds a NEW third-party dep (@aws-sdk/client-s3) with a large transitive tree (@smithy/*, etc.) absent from the lockfile today, so new snapshot entries ARE required.
