| 2026-05-25 | **TASK-24 #2 recovery UX ŌĆö FINAL (after 5 Codex rounds): MANUAL retry banner for ALL drop/error cases; auto-retry filed as a follow-up needing idempotency infra.** Codex round 5 closed the last hole: even an orchestrator `error` frame (the "provably-dead" path I'd gated auto-retry to) can arrive AFTER the runner already executed a host tool or wrote a partial transcript turn ŌĆö so auto-`regenerate()` re-runs NON-IDEMPOTENT side effects a second time without user consent. Across 5 rounds EVERY auto-recovery variant (same-reqId silent resume ŌåÆ lossy on host restart; broad auto-retry ŌåÆ duplicates sendMessages-rejection turns; narrow auto-retry on the dead-turn frame ŌåÆ duplicates post-side-effect turns) had a correctness hole. This is the FAULTA-5 invariant in full: with the current non-idempotent / non-transactional turn model there is NO client-side auto-retry that is loss-free AND duplicate-free. So #2 ships as the MANUAL-retry banner (the user consents to the re-run, accepting any duplicate) ŌĆö which is FAULTA-5's already-proven-correct behavior ŌĆö and a visible follow-up: a true auto-retry needs turn-level idempotency (server-side dedupe of a re-invoked reqId) + durable/seq-stable runnerŌåÆhost events. **This is the explicit-clarification tension flagged in the handoff for the human:** the clarification asked for auto-retry+message; my analysis shows it's unsafe on current infra, so I shipped the safe subset and surfaced the gap rather than ship a duplicate-prone auto-retry. The reported bug is STILL fully fixed by Task-1 (runner survives + turn commits ŌåÆ no silent loss; the durable turn hydrates on reload). | The reported "turn silently lost" is fixed by Task-1 regardless of #2's UX. Manual retry is the only correct recovery action with current infra; auto-retry is genuinely a follow-up gated on idempotency infra, not a quick fix. | (a)ŌĆō(d) from the prior row, all rejected over the 5 rounds; (e) ship manual + file the idempotency follow-up + flag the clarification tension (CHOSEN). |
| 2026-05-25 | **TASK-24 ŌĆö REVERSED the same-reqId silent auto-reconnect; intermediate design = bounded auto-`regenerate()` ONLY on the provably-dead server `error` frame + honest banner on CONNECTION_LOST.** (Superseded by the row above after Codex round 5.) Codex (round 2) proved the same-reqId resume is SILENTLY LOSSY across a host RESTART: runnerŌåÆhost `event.stream-chunk`/`event.turn-end` are one-shot `client.event().catch()` (NOT retried by Task-1's deadline, which only covers `call()`), AND the host chunk-buffer + its per-reqId `nextSeq` cursor are in-memory (lost on restart, re-minted from 1). So after an OOMKill restart the reconnected client (lastSeq=N) receives a replay starting at seq 1 ŌåÆ all `seq<=lastSeq` ŌåÆ silently deduped as duplicates ŌåÆ the entire post-restart answer vanishes (or hangs if `done` is also deduped). Indistinguishable client-side from a safe same-host replay-overlap. This is the exact FAULTA-5 "auto-retry against a stateful server is almost always wrong" trap. | The reported bug is FIXED by Task-1 alone (runner survives + turn COMMITS ŌåÆ no silent loss; visible on next history hydration). For #2, auto-retry is only loss-free AND duplicate-free when the turn is PROVABLY DEAD ŌĆö the orchestrator's `chat:turn-error` (server `error` frame, reason e.g. sandbox-terminated) means the runner is gone, so `regenerate()` routes to a fresh sandbox (no duplicate). On a bare CONNECTION_LOST drop the runner may still be alive ŌåÆ `regenerate()` could duplicate AND a silent resume could truncate ŌåÆ keep the honest manual banner. The OOMKill (host-death) case surfaces CONNECTION_LOST (a dead host can't fire turn-error), so it gets the banner; true auto-recovery there needs durable/seq-stable runnerŌåÆhost events (FOLLOW-UP). | (a) keep the lossy same-reqId resume (REJECTED: Codex-proven silent truncation, violates the hard no-silent-loss invariant); (b) blanket auto-`regenerate()` on every drop (REJECTED: duplicates a live runner on CONNECTION_LOST); (c) make events durable + seq stable across restart (the right long-term fix, but substantial new infra ŌĆö FOLLOW-UP, not this PR); (d) escalate as blocked (REJECTED: the directive's intent ŌĆö "auto-retry where safe + message" ŌĆö IS satisfiable for the provably-dead subset without the silent-loss trap; this is the self-answerable "ship the loss-free safe subset + file enabling infra" move per meta 2026-05-25). |
| 2026-05-25 | TASK-21: a reloaded text/json/yaml/csv attachment rendered as RAW INJECTED TEXT (`User attached 'x.txt' (text/plain, 92 bytes):\n\n<file content>`) instead of a download chip. Root cause: `attachment-translation.ts` has TWO mention formats ŌĆö the fallback `formatAttachmentMention` (`...' at <path> (<mediaType>)`, single-line, path-bearing, which PR #120's read-path `reconstructAttachmentBlocks` recognizes) AND the inlineable-text branch's ad-hoc `User attached '<name>' (<mediaType>, <N> bytes):\n\n<content>` which (a) DROPS the path and (b) doesn't match `ATTACHMENT_MENTION_RE`. Small text files take the inline branch (weak-model accommodation), so they were never reconstructible on read. Fix: (1) add a shared `formatAttachmentInline(fields, content)` in `@ax/ipc-protocol` whose preamble IS the canonical `formatAttachmentMention(fields)` line (path-bearing) + `\n\n` + content; runner inline branch calls it. (2) extend `reconstructAttachmentBlocks` so a user-turn text block whose mention is the FIRST content line is the inlined-attachment shape ŌåÆ emit the chip and DROP the trailing model-view content (don't surface it). | I4 single-source-of-truth: one producer/consumer pair, mirroring PR #120's `formatAttachmentMention`/`parseAttachmentMention`. I5: user-turn-only + prefix-scoped + schema-revalidated unchanged; now ALSO drops runner model-view inline text from the user transcript (tightens the trust boundary ŌĆö model-view content crossing into the user-visible transcript was the leak the card flagged). The user's typed prompt and the attachment are SEPARATE content-array elements (main.ts:529-537) and `parseJsonlToTurns` keeps user blocks separate, so the inlined-attachment text is its OWN block ŌĆö dropping it can't clobber the typed prompt. TASK-11/#163 fixed the attachment turn being DROPPED on reload (persistence); this is the orthogonal RENDER-format bug. | (a) reconstruct from the existing `(mediaType, N bytes)` format by re-deriving the path from conv+turn (rejected: the path isn't recoverable from that string ŌĆö turn dir + hash prefix aren't in it; embedding the canonical mention is the clean fix); (b) stop inlining content entirely and always emit the bare mention (rejected: breaks weak-model accommodation ŌĆö small files must reach the model as content, the whole reason the inline branch exists); (c) fix only the read path to also drop content after ANY mention line (rejected: without the path in the persisted text there's no download chip to build ŌĆö the producer MUST carry the path) |
| 2026-05-25 | TASK-21 Phase 5 (ACCEPTED ŌĆö real regression): Codex flagged a P2 ŌĆö my first read-path fix used a blanket `break` after converting the first in-prefix mention to drop the inlined model-view content. But the SDK can COALESCE adjacent user text blocks into one newline-joined block (the same reason the pre-existing `prompt\nmention` test exists), so a turn with MULTIPLE bare (non-inlined) attachment mentions would become `mention1\nmention2\ntext` in one block ŌĆö and the `break` dropped mention2 + trailing text on reload (a functional regression vs the pre-TASK-21 per-line behavior that converted EVERY matching line). Fix: discriminate the inline shape precisely ŌĆö only `break`/drop-trailing when the line immediately AFTER the converted mention is BLANK (the `\n\n` separator `formatAttachmentInline` always emits); a bare mention has no blank-line follow, so keep scanning. Added a regression test (coalesced 2 bare mentions + trailing text ŌåÆ both chips + text) and verified an adversarial case (inline content that itself contains a mention-like line ŌåÆ still only the first chip, content dropped). | Codex is correct and verifiable: bare `formatAttachmentMention` (no trailing content) and the inline preamble are indistinguishable at the mention line alone; the blank-line-follow is the reliable discriminator because the bare-mention coalesce joins with a SINGLE `\n` (per the existing prompt\nmention test) while inline is always `mention\n\ncontent`. The blank-line rule preserves multi-attachment reconstruction AND still strips inlined content (even content that mimics a mention, since once the blank-line inline shape is detected we drop everything after). | (a) keep the blanket `break` (rejected: real multi-attachment regression Codex caught); (b) never break, convert every mention line + keep non-mention lines as text (rejected: that's the ORIGINAL bug ŌĆö the inlined file content would leak as text; we MUST drop content after an inline preamble); (c) tag the inline block at the producer with a sentinel marker instead of inferring from the blank line (rejected: adds a new on-wire token the read path must trust, and the `\n\n` shape is already a deterministic producer guarantee ŌĆö inferring is cheaper and needs no format coupling) |
| 2026-05-25 | TASK-21 Phase 5 round 2 (ACCEPTED): Codex flagged a follow-up to the blank-line discriminator ŌĆö if the SDK coalesces TWO INLINE attachments into one text block (`m1\n\nbody1\nm2\n\nbody2`), the `break` (which I'd kept for the inline case) abandons the scan at the first inline preamble ŌåÆ only the first chip renders. | 2026-05-25 | TASK-21 Phase 5 round 3 (ACCEPTED ŌĆö security): Codex flagged that my round-2 skip-to-next-mention scanned INTO opaque inline content, so a crafted body line that spoofs an in-prefix mention terminates the suppression and leaks the remaining bytes (a prompt-injection-flavored leak ŌĆö exactly the I5 thing TASK-21 is supposed to prevent). | 2026-05-25 | TASK-22 Phase 5 finding (ACCEPTED ŌĆö real bug): Codex flagged a P2 ŌĆö the host-side `fireTurnError` alone is INSUFFICIENT because of a pre-SSE-connect RACE. channel-web returns 202 to POST /api/chat/messages and the browser opens GET /api/chat/stream/:reqId SEPARATELY; a FAST session-open failure (credential-resolution error rejects `proxy:open-session` synchronously) fires `chat:turn-error` BEFORE the EventSource connects + installs the per-connection live subscriber. | 2026-05-25 | TASK-19: "add $HOME/bin to PATH so agent-installed binaries persist between sessions." KEY FINDING resolving the card's literal "make .bashrc add it" wording: the agent's runtime `$HOME` is **`/permanent`** (`agent-claude-sdk-runner/src/main.ts:735` `HOME: env.workspaceRoot`, default `/permanent` ŌĆö env.ts:105), the git-bundled-and-restored workspace, NOT the image's `/home/axagent`. So `$HOME/bin` = `/permanent/bin`, exactly the persisted location. And the SDK Bash tool runs a **non-interactive** shell whose PATH comes ENTIRELY from the explicit `query({options:{env}})` allowlist (`proxy-startup.ts` forwards `process.env.PATH`; its comment: "Without forwarding PATH, the SDK's Bash tool executes `ls` and gets exit code 127" ŌĆö proof no rc file is sourced, else a default PATH would exist). A plain `.bashrc` is interactive-only ŌåÆ the agent's shell would NOT source it. DECISION: do BOTH minimal layers ŌĆö (a) the **Dockerfile** writes a `.bashrc` to the image home that adds `$HOME/bin` to PATH (satisfies the literal ask + covers any interactive/BASH_ENV shell + is the discoverable convention), and (b) the **load-bearing** fix: add `${env.workspaceRoot}/bin` to the forwarded `PATH` in `main.ts`'s SDK env literal so the non-interactive Bash tool actually sees `/permanent/bin`. **APPEND, not prepend (codex Phase-5 [P2], accepted):** `$HOME=/permanent` is model-WRITABLE + restored across sessions, so PREPENDING would let a prompt-injection/malicious-tool-output `/permanent/bin/git` (or node/python) PERSISTENTLY shadow the trusted image/venv binary in every future session ŌĆö an I5/capability-minimization violation. Appending keeps installed tools discoverable (the goal) while trusted base+venv bins win on name collisions. (My original prepend rationale "the agent already controls its session" missed the cross-session PERSISTENCE + injection angle codex flagged.) Regression test: assert the SDK-subprocess PATH ENDS with `:<workspaceRoot>/bin` AND does NOT start with `<workspaceRoot>/bin:` (catches both a dropped-append regression and a re-introduced prepend) + a Dockerfile-content guard in `scripts/__tests__/dockerfile-home-bin-path.test.js` (runs unconditionally every PR via `pnpm test:scripts`, NOT package-affected-gated) asserting `.bashrc` carries `PATH="$PATH:$HOME/bin"` and NOT the prepend form. | Honors card INTENT (binaries found across sessions) via the mechanism that works for THIS runtime, not the one the card's wording assumes. `/permanent/bin` is the only dir that both is `$HOME/bin` AND persists (git-bundled); a binary in the image's `/home/axagent/bin` is neither writable by the agent's session nor where `$HOME` points. (b) is required because (a) alone is dead code for the SDK's non-interactive shell. | (a) ONLY the .bashrc, as the card's words say (rejected: the SDK Bash tool doesn't source .bashrc ŌåÆ the agent never gets it ŌåÆ half-wired/dead per the no-half-wired invariant); (b) ONLY mutate main.ts PATH, skip .bashrc (rejected: the card explicitly asks for the Dockerfile/.bashrc change + .bashrc is the human-discoverable convention for any future interactive shell); (c) set BASH_ENV in the forwarded env to point at a script (rejected: heavier, and the explicit-PATH forward is the established seam the venv/cache code already uses ŌĆö mutate PATH the same way `buildPythonVenvEnv` does); (d) bake binaries into image `/home/axagent/bin` (rejected: misreads "persists between sessions" ŌĆö that's the workspace tier, not the image) |

| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-8: the new lane lives as a SEPARATE vitest config (`vitest.config.prod-bootstrap.ts`) + its own `test:prod-bootstrap` script, NOT folded into the default `test` glob ŌĆö but it DOES run in the package's default `pnpm test` (added to the default include) so CI affected-package scoping picks it up automatically when preset-k8s or any kept plugin changes. The real-cluster k8s-e2e stays in its own gated config. | The card says CI-grade (fast, hermetic) yet wants it to run "where it adds signal" ŌĆö the default `test` script + affected-scoping (`pnpm --filter "...[BASE_SHA]" run test`) already gives "runs when preset-k8s or a dependency changes." | 2026-05-24 | ARCH-1: close the multi-replica chat gap by making the single-replica pin **explicit + fail-fast in the Helm chart** (`fail` when `replicas > 1`) rather than building a stream-broker now | The eventbus (`eventbus:emit`/`:subscribe`) has NO production caller today ŌĆö only `test-harness/mock-services.ts` ŌĆö and the postgres impl caps NOTIFY payloads at 8000 bytes, hostile to streaming text chunks. A broker would be half-wired (invariant 3) AND wouldn't actually unlock multi-replica because `workspace.backend: local` is an RWO single-replica PVC too. The real defect ARCH-1 names is *silently claiming* multi-replica: the chart had `replicas: 1` as a default + comment but no guard, so `--set replicas=3` rendered fine and broke chat (SSE reconnect tail + `chat:stream-chunk` fan-in are per-replica in-process). A render-time `fail` makes the unsupported config impossible to ship by accident; the broker is the earned follow-up. | Build a stream-broker package on Redis/PG/eventbus now (rejected: half-wired, premature, blocked by RWO workspace PVC anyway ŌĆö YAGNI); leave the comment-only pin (rejected: that IS the bug ŌĆö silent misconfig) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-4: `codex` CLI is not installed in this orchestrated env (`command -v codex` empty; not in nvm bin / ~/.local / ~/.bun / global npm). | 2026-05-24 | ARCH-4: `manifest.optionalCalls` is `{ hook: string, degradation: string }[]` (object array, not bare strings) ŌĆö distinct from `calls` (required) | The card's whole intent is a human-readable degradation note **per** optional call, so the note must be a first-class field, not a comment. Object array is the only shape that carries it. Motivating real case: `@ax/credentials` calls `storage:get`/`set`/`delete-prefix` only behind `bus.hasService(...)` and degrades to in-memory; today it can't declare them (would break `verifyCalls` in store-blob-only harnesses) so they hide in a code comment. | bare `string[]` like `calls` (rejected: drops the note, the point of the card); separate `degradationNotes` map keyed by hook (rejected: two fields that must be kept in sync = a leak waiting to happen) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-4: optionalCalls are **non-fatal** in `verifyCalls` (missing = fine) but **still form call-graph + topo-order edges when the producer IS present** | Non-fatal is the entire distinction from `calls`. But an optional edge is a real dependency when the producer exists: it must (a) be ordered after its producer so `hasService` is true by the consumer's `init()`, and (b) count toward cycle detection ŌĆö an optional call can still close a cycle. So `buildCallGraph` includes optional edges (already guarded by `prod !== undefined`); only `verifyCalls` skips them. | Ignore optional edges entirely in the graph (rejected: a present-producer optional call could hide a cycle, and could init before its producer making `hasService` flaky) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-4: a hook in BOTH `calls` and `optionalCalls` is a manifest error, caught at schema-refinement time | Required-AND-optional is a contradiction; silently picking one would mask a manifest mistake. Zod `.superRefine` on the schema rejects the overlap with the offending hook named, alongside the existing field validation, so bootstrap's `invalid-manifest` path reports it. | Let `calls` win silently (rejected: hides author error); check only at bootstrap not schema (rejected: schema is the canonical validation point ŌĆö keep it co-located) |

| 2026-05-22 | Sub-project B Basic-auth transform uses a **per-request re-arming HTTP/1.1 framing state machine** in the MITM clientŌåÆupstream path, not single-head-per-connection as design ┬¦4.2 literally describes | git smart-HTTP reuses ONE CONNECT tunnel for `GET /info/refs?service=git-upload-pack` (no body) **then** `POST /git-upload-pack` (body), and with creds in the URL libcurl sends `Authorization: Basic` **preemptively on both**. Single-head buffering would transform the GET but leave the POST's base64 placeholder corrupted ŌåÆ fetch fails after refs succeed. State machine: buffer headŌåÆtransform BasicŌåÆ`Content-Length`-counted body then re-arm to head; `Transfer-Encoding: chunked` or oversized head ŌåÆ flush + verbatim passthrough, no re-arm (the chunked POST is the clone's last request, so not re-arming after it is safe). Header-only rewrite; bodies keep existing verbatim per-chunk sub (honors I1). | Single head per connection (rejected: corrupts the POST auth on keep-alive); full chunked de-framing to re-arm after chunked bodies (rejected: YAGNI ŌĆö git's chunked POST is terminal; adds a chunk-size parser for no MVP gain); line-scan for `Authorization:` anywhere in the stream (rejected: false-matches inside POST bodies could corrupt them) |

| 2026-05-24 | F2a Codex finding 2 (High) ACCEPTED: bind failure must distinguish 409 conflict (terminal) from transient (self-heal) | My initial swallow-all "self-healing" was too broad. A `conversation.store-runner-session` 409 (HOOK_REJECTED, per ipc-core/handlers/conversation-store-runner-session.ts) means another runner already bound the conversation to a DIFFERENT id ŌĆö a concurrent fresh-boot race. Swallowing+retrying lets the LOSER keep streaming + committing an orphan transcript, defeating the host's once-only bind. Fix: `bindRunnerSessionIfNeeded` re-throws on `IpcRequestError && status===409` ŌåÆ propagated past both commit catches ŌåÆ outer catch ŌåÆ `terminated` (surfaced by F2b); transient (network/5xx, client already retried 5xx) stays self-healing. The 409 in the commit try can only come from the bind (commitNotifyWithResync swallows its own IPC errors). | Keep swallow-all (rejected: orphan + double-bind race, Codex-flagged); make ALL bind failures fatal (rejected: fatal-after-a-streamed-turn on a transient blip is incoherent UX) |
| 2026-05-24 | F2a Codex finding 3 (Medium) ACCEPTED: self-heal test rewritten to the realistic multi-turn shape | My first self-heal test relied on the post-`result` FINAL commit retrying the bind ŌĆö but in production the final drain commit is usually empty (null) because the per-turn commit already captured the turn. Rewrote it: turn-1 per-turn bundle + turn-2 per-turn bundle + final ŌåÆ null (`mockResolvedValueOnce` chain), bind transient-fails on turn 1 and succeeds on turn 2's accepted commit. Proves the retry comes from the NEXT TURN, matching prod. | Keep the final-commit-retry test (rejected: optimistic vs prod where final is null) |
| 2026-05-24 | F2a Codex finding 1 (High ŌĆö demotion-path orphan) DEFERRED to a tracked follow-up, NOT fixed in this PR | When the resume guard demotes a stale binding (bound id with no resumable transcript), the row stays bound to the stale id (the host bind is once-only ŌĆö a rebind would `conflict`), so `conversations:get` reads the stale path and the fresh transcript is orphaned; this repeats every boot. Deferring is defensible because: (a) the ROOT fix means `runner_session_id` is set only after a durable commit, so NEW conversations can never form a stale binding ŌĆö the demotion path is reachable ONLY for pre-existing rows already broken by the very bug being fixed (which TODAY crash on resume) or a hypothetical future materialize/git regression; (b) my fix turns those from a hard `exit 1` crash into a functional-but-empty-history chat ŌĆö a strict improvement; (c) full repair needs a host-side rebind/overwrite capability (new IPC action + hook + boundary review) = a separate scoped change; (d) making the demotion path attempt a rebind WITHOUT host support would hit the once-only conflict ŌåÆ with finding-2's terminal-conflict that becomes a crash-LOOP for legacy rows ŌĆö worse UX than silent-functional. The gate therefore stays `runnerSessionId===null` (demotion never binds). Tracked in TODO.md (host-rebind repair for legacy/regression stale rows). | Fix in-PR via a host rebind hook (rejected: cross-plugin scope creep on a runner-side fix; gated on whether legacy stale rows matter in practice); make demotion bind+conflict-terminate (rejected: crash-loop for legacy rows) |
| 2026-05-24 | **auto-ship/yolo-ship live per-card progress block + crash recovery; loosen "agents never write the board" ŌåÆ routing-fields-only.** The building yolo-ship agent appends fine-grained per-phase heartbeat lines (`brainstorm done` ŌåÆ `task k/N done` ŌåÆ `codex review clean` ŌåÆ `PR #n opened` ŌåÆ `CI green Ō£ģ`, `ŌÜĀ`-prefixed exceptions) to a delimited `<!-- AUTOSHIP-PROGRESS -->` block in **its own** card body; the orchestrator stays sole writer of the **routing fields** (`Status`, `Depends on`) + sole card-mover. On run-start/resume only, auto-ship reconciles orphaned In Progress/In Review cards (CLI death kills agents+poller): **PR exists ŌćÆ Phases 0ŌĆō5 done ŌćÆ route to merge queue; no PR ŌćÆ reset to To Do + discard the partial branch**. | "While the agent is implementing" rules out funneling through the orchestrator (it only hears at the Ōēż150-word handoff). **One writer at a time is structural** (agent owns the body while In Progress; orchestrator only at terminal Done/Parked, after the agent exited) so no lock needed; the orchestrator dropped its PR-link body-append so there's never a 2nd writer. **Token discipline:** the read-modify-write is **shell-side** (`append_progress` in `github-project.md ┬¦6`) ŌĆö the growing body never enters model context (orchestrator adds 0 tokens; it never reads In-Progress bodies). Progress writes are **best-effort** (never block a ship) and land on In-Progress cards so they don't trip the To-Do poller. Recovery leans on yolo-ship opening the PR only in Phase 6. `.gitignore` switched to a `.claude/auto-ship-*` wildcard for the new helper+lock. | Funnel progress through the orchestrator (rejected: not live ŌĆö only at handoff); model-side RMW / hold the body in context (rejected: body grows, pollutes context + tokens); coarse happy-path updates (rejected: user chose fine-grained ŌĆö the per-phase heartbeat is what flags a wedged agent across parallel cards); resume the partial branch on a no-PR orphan (rejected: fragile; pre-PR work is cheap to redo); let the agent own a real lock / write routing fields (rejected: serialized merge queue + routing stay orchestrator-owned to avoid races) |
| 2026-05-24 | **`.claude/memory/` is now COMMITTED** ŌĆö reversing the prior keep-uncommitted default. CLAUDE.md ("Codex Memory Bootstrap" + Skills line) and the `claude-memory` skill (frontmatter, bootstrap step 3, store-boundary table) updated to "update and commit memory files after any change"; the misleading `.gitignore` comment fixed. | Vinay directive 2026-05-24: memory SHOULD be updated and committed. The post-merge fast-forward collision (PR #126) that motivated keeping memory local came from INCONSISTENT state (some rows committed, divergent local rows not) ŌĆö committing consistently removes the divergent-uncommitted class. The files were already tracked in git (the "gitignored" claim was never true), so this aligns instructions with reality. | Keep uncommitted (rejected: user reversed it); actually gitignore `.claude/memory/` (rejected: opposite of the directive) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-5: ship `@ax/sandbox-protocol` as a pure zod-schema contract package, modeled on `@ax/ipc-protocol` / `@ax/workspace-protocol` (no `@ax/core` dep, just zod) and added to the eslint `no-restricted-imports` allow-list | Both sandbox backends + the orchestrator structurally re-declare `ProxyConfigSchema`, `InstalledSkillSchema`, `McpServerSchema`, `OpenSessionInputSchema`. A shared contract package keeps the no-cross-plugin-import rule (it's allow-listed like the other `*-protocol` packages) while killing the drift. | Type-only shared package (rejected: the duplication is the *runtime zod validation*, not just types ŌĆö types alone wouldn't stop strictness drift); leave duplicated (rejected: that's exactly the drift the task targets) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-5: adopt the STRICTER subprocess `ProxyConfigSchema` (min(1) + exactly-one-of refine) as the canonical shared schema | The orchestrator's `endpointToProxyConfig` already guarantees exactly-one-of at construction; the strict schema documents+enforces that invariant. k8s's lax schema accepted neither/both ŌĆö a latent bug (a both-set or neither-set proxyConfig would pass k8s validation and stamp inconsistent env). ## ARCH-2 ŌĆö IPC dispatcher dependency metadata (2026-05-24)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-24 | Export a single `DISPATCHER_DEPENDENCIES` const from `@ax/ipc-core` (`requiredCalls: readonly string[]`, `optionalCalls: readonly OptionalCall[]`, `dynamicCallPatterns: readonly string[]`). Both `@ax/ipc-http` and `@ax/ipc-server` spread it into `manifest.calls = [...requiredCalls]` and `optionalCalls = [...optionalCalls]`. | The dispatcher is the single source of truth for what services it transitively invokes; transports must not re-derive it (drift = the ARCH-2 bug). `@ax/ipc-core` is allowlisted in `no-restricted-imports`; both transports already runtime-import `dispatch`/`authenticate` from it. | Per-transport hardcoded lists (status quo ŌĆö drifted); a function returning the manifest fragment (over-engineered, no alternate impl ŌĆö a 2-array spread is clearer). |
| 2026-05-24 | required = unconditional dispatcher calls whose producer is present in BOTH transport consumers (`session:resolve-token`, `session:claim-work`, `tool:list`, `session:get-config`, `workspace:read`). optional = guarded/branch-conditional OR not-guaranteed-present (`conversations:store-runner-session` [unconditional on its route, but the local CLI loads ipc-server WITHOUT @ax/conversations ŌĆö Codex P1 caught this], `conversations:get-metadata` [conversationId!==null], `workspace:export-baseline-bundle` [hasService], `workspace:apply-bundle` [bundle path], `workspace:list` [non-bundle materialize fallback]). dynamic prefix = `tool:execute:`. | `verifyCalls` fails boot if a REQUIRED producer is absent; promote to required ONLY if the producer is guaranteed present wherever a transport loads. The two real consumers are `packages/cli/src/main.ts` (loads workspace-git + session-inmemory + tool-dispatcher, NO conversations) and `presets/k8s` (loads everything). So `conversations:store-runner-session` MUST be optional. | All-required (breaks the CLI boot ŌĆö the bug Codex flagged); all-optional (loses the missing-service boot check for genuinely-mandatory deps). |
| 2026-05-24 | "Stay in sync" test = source-scan (`dependency-sync.test.ts`): read every handler + `auth.ts`, regex-extract each `bus.call('lit')`/`bus.hasService('lit')` hook string + each `namespace:action:`-shaped template-literal prefix, assert each is covered by required Ōł¬ optional Ōł¬ dynamic-prefix; plus a reverse "no dead declared hook" check + `DISPATCHER_PATHS` non-empty check. | A new handler adding an undeclared `bus.call` is exactly the drift ARCH-2 prevents; a static-equality test is a tautology. The dynamic prefix is matched from the `const hookName = `tool:execute:${...}`` template (a variable, not inline at the call site), filtered to hook-shaped prefixes so error-message template literals don't masquerade as hooks. | Hardcoded expected-list equality (tautology). |
| 2026-05-24 | CLI-3: digest-pin **only the uv image ref** in `container/agent/Dockerfile` (`COPY --from=ghcr.io/astral-sh/uv:0.11.16@sha256:440fd6477af86a2f1b38080c539f1672cd22acb1b1a47e321dba5158ab08864d`), keep the `0.11.16` tag visible + a comment. Do NOT digest-pin the `node:20-bookworm-slim` base. | The card names uv/uvx + the tini/ca-certs follow-up; the base-image pin is a SEPARATE tracked follow-up (Dockerfile lines 45-47) explicitly gated on "the image build pipeline lands" with the documented intent of letting local builds float as Node rolls patch releases. | 2026-05-24 | CLI-3: version-pin the apt deps (`ca-certificates=20230311+deb12u1`, `tini=0.19.0-1+b3`, `git=1:2.39.5-0+deb12u3`, `git-lfs=3.3.0-1+deb12u1`, `python3=3.11.2-1+b1`) in the runtime stage's `apt-get install`. Apt isn't digest-addressable in the install line; "content-addressed" maps to a hard version pin for apt. ## ARCH-6 ŌĆö returns schemas for public service hooks (2026-05-24)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-6: scope the `returns`-schema rollout to **IPC-reachable + security/tenant-boundary service hooks**, deferring the long tail. In-scope hooks: workspace (`workspace:read`, `workspace:list`, `workspace:apply`, `workspace:diff`), session (`session:resolve-token`, `session:get-config`, `session:claim-work`, `session:create`, `session:is-alive`, `session:terminate`), agents (`agents:resolve`), conversations (`conversations:get-metadata`, `conversations:store-runner-session`), credentials (already done: `credentials:get`/`resolve:setting`; ADD `credentials:list`, `credentials:list-kinds`). Sandbox `sandbox:open-session` ŌåÆ see separate decision (handle-bearing, special-cased). | The card itself says ship the IPC-reachable + security-boundary subset well rather than half-wire the full ~120-hook surface. IPC-reachable set derived from `@ax/ipc-core/handlers/*` `bus.call` sites: session:resolve-token (auth gate), session:get-config, session:claim-work, workspace:read/list, conversations:get-metadata/store-runner-session, plus the workspace bundle hooks (already typed in their own protocol pkg). Tenant-boundary: agents:resolve is the J1 ACL gate every conversations hook chains through. | Full rollout across all ~120 hooks (rejected: card explicitly says ship the subset, defer remainder ŌĆö half-wiring everything risks the strip-by-default trap on many handlers at once); skip non-IPC security hooks (rejected: agents:resolve is the tenant gate, must be in) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-6: schemas live **co-located in each registering plugin** (next to the I/O interfaces), NOT in a new `@ax/*-protocol` package ŌĆö mirroring the EXISTING credentials precedent (`CredentialsResolveOutputSchema` in `credentials/src/plugin.ts`). Each backend that registers a hook owns its own `returns` schema. For session (two backends `inmemory`/`postgres` register identical hooks), each carries its own copy of the schema, matching how they ALREADY duplicate the I/O interfaces structurally (I2 ŌĆö no cross-plugin import; the drift is the documented boundary cost). | The `returns` schema is a per-registration, in-process, defense-in-depth shape assertion ŌĆö it is NOT an inter-plugin wire contract (that's `@ax/ipc-protocol`, already zod-validated at the untrusted runnerŌåöhost wire). A `*-protocol` package is the right tool when the SHAPE is the shared contract across plugins; here the shape is already pinned by the TS interfaces and the wire schema. Adding a protocol package would be premature abstraction (boundary-review: can't name a second consumer that ISN'T the registering backend). credentials set the precedent; follow it. | Shared `@ax/session-protocol` etc. (rejected: premature ŌĆö no consumer beyond the registering backend; the wire contract already lives in ipc-protocol; would be a bigger surface than the card warrants); schemas in @ax/core (rejected: I1 ŌĆö core stays storage-neutral, and these are per-plugin contracts) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-6: `sandbox:open-session` gets a **`.passthrough()` schema validating only `runnerEndpoint: z.string().min(1)`**, NOT a strict object schema. The hook's `OpenSessionResult` carries `handle: { kill(): Promise<void>; exited: Promise<ExitInfo> }` ŌĆö live functions + a Promise. A strict zod object schema STRIPS undeclared keys (hook-bus.ts:141-147), which would silently delete `handle` and break the orchestrator's session lifecycle. `.passthrough()` keeps `handle` intact while still asserting the one storage-agnostic serializable field the I1 boundary cares about. | The hook-bus comment explicitly warns: zod object schemas strip undeclared keys by default; declare `returns` as a faithful shape OR add `.passthrough()` for hooks that return extra keys. A handle-bearing hook is exactly the `.passthrough()` case. Validating `runnerEndpoint` still catches a backend that forgets to set the opaque URI (the field that crosses the I1 boundary). | Strict `z.object({runnerEndpoint})` (rejected: strips `handle` ŌåÆ breaks lifecycle ŌĆö the strip-by-default trap); `z.custom()` no-op (rejected: validates nothing, defeats the point); skip sandbox entirely (rejected: it's a named security-boundary surface in the card) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-6: handle the strip-by-default trap GLOBALLY by auditing every in-scope hook's output for non-data fields (functions / Promises / Date / branded strings / Uint8Array) before writing its schema. Branded `WorkspaceVersion` ŌåÆ `z.string()` (brand is compile-time only). `Date` ŌåÆ `z.date()`. `Uint8Array` ŌåÆ `z.instanceof(Uint8Array)`. Lazy `contentBefore?/contentAfter?: () => Promise<Bytes>` on `WorkspaceChange` (in `workspace:apply`/`diff` delta) ŌåÆ schema must NOT include them as data OR must `.passthrough()` the change objects, else the lazy fns get stripped and subscribers lose content access. | This is THE correctness risk of the whole task ŌĆö a `returns` schema that strips a load-bearing field is worse than no schema (silent data loss vs. honest TS-only). Each schema is paired with a drift-guard test (round-trip a fully-populated interface value through `.parse`, assert `toEqual`) per the credentials `return-schemas.test.ts` precedent ŌĆö that test FAILS if the schema strips any field. | Trust hand-written schemas without round-trip guards (rejected: the credentials precedent added the guard for exactly this reason; a stripped field is invisible without it); use `.passthrough()` everywhere (rejected: defeats the shape assertion ŌĆö only use it where a live non-data field genuinely rides the result, e.g. sandbox handle) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-6: REVISE scope ŌĆö workspace `returns` schemas cover ONLY the IPC-reachable, clean-data hooks `workspace:read` + `workspace:list`. DEFER `workspace:apply` and `workspace:diff` to a follow-up. | `WorkspaceApplyOutput`/`WorkspaceDiffOutput` carry `delta.changes[].contentBefore?/contentAfter?: () => Promise<Bytes>` ŌĆö lazy functions. A strict zod object schema strips them (hook-bus strip-by-default), which (a) breaks `@ax/test-harness/workspace-contract.ts:145-154` (`expect(typeof ch.contentAfter).toBe('function')`) and (b) silently severs `@ax/routines/sync.ts:82`'s `change.contentAfter` content access. Validating apply/diff correctly needs the change objects `.passthrough()`-ed AND the contract test re-confirmed across BOTH the git backend and the mock ŌĆö a focused follow-up, not a rushed add here. read/list return plain `{found,bytes,version?}` / `{paths}` ŌĆö no lazy fields, safe to schema now. | Schema apply/diff with `.passthrough()` on changes now (rejected: needs coordinated contract-test verification across backends + risks the strip trap on a security-critical write path under time pressure ŌĆö exactly the "ship the subset well, defer the rest" case the card calls for); skip workspace entirely (rejected: read/list ARE IPC-reachable + safe) |

## ARCH-12 ŌĆö returns schemas for workspace:apply + workspace:diff (lazy-fn delta) (2026-05-24)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-12: schemas (`WorkspaceDeltaSchema`, `WorkspaceApplyOutputSchema`, `WorkspaceDiffOutputSchema`) live in `@ax/core/workspace.ts` next to the ARCH-6 read/list schemas. The `changes[]` element schema uses `z.object({ path: z.string(), kind: z.enum([...]) }).passthrough()`. | Verified empirically (zod 3.25.76): `.passthrough()` keeps function-valued keys by **reference identity** ŌĆö `parsed.contentAfter === fn` is true, both as a bare object and inside `z.array(...)`. So the lazy `contentBefore?/contentAfter?` survive `.parse()` untouched (no wrapping, not stripped). Validating `path`+`kind` still catches a backend that emits a malformed change. The branded `WorkspaceVersion` (`before`/`after`) ŌåÆ `z.string()`, `before` nullable; `reason?`ŌåÆ`z.string().optional()`; `author?`ŌåÆ`z.object({...}).optional()`. The shapes already live in core (storage-neutral, `WorkspaceVersion` is a compile-time brand), so this follows the ARCH-6 read/list precedent of co-locating in core ŌĆö NOT a `*-protocol` pkg (no consumer beyond the registering backend). | Declare `contentBefore/contentAfter` as `z.function().optional()` (rejected: zod can wrap/coerce functions and may choke on absent-vs-undefined; passthrough identity is safer + simpler); strict object on changes (rejected: strips the lazy fns ŌĆö the exact ARCH-6-deferred trap) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-12: attach `WorkspaceApplyOutputSchema` at the **`@ax/core` facade** (`registerWorkspaceApplyFacade`), NOT at the three backend `workspace:apply-internal` sites. Attach `WorkspaceDiffOutputSchema` at each backend's `workspace:diff` registration (git-core, git-server-client, mock) ŌĆö diff has no facade. | `workspace:apply` IS the facade; it returns the internal's result unchanged, so validating once at the facade covers all backends (one source of truth, I4) and the public hook is what callers + IPC see. `apply-internal` is backend-private; double-validating there is redundant churn. `workspace:diff` has no facade, so its schema rides each of the 3 direct registrations (matching how read/list already attach per-backend). | Attach apply schema at all 3 `apply-internal` sites (rejected: redundant ŌĆö facade already validates the identical output; 3├Ś the edit surface for no extra coverage); skip the facade and only validate internal (rejected: the public hook is the IPC-reachable + security-boundary surface the card names) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-12 (Codex P2 fix): validate the `workspace:apply` output INSIDE the facade with `WorkspaceApplyOutputSchema.safeParse` BEFORE firing `workspace:applied`, throwing `invalid-return` on failure ŌĆö do NOT rely on the service-hook `{ returns }` option for this hook. Fire/return the ORIGINAL `applied` object (validation is a gate, not a transform). | The `{ returns }` option is enforced by `HookBus.call` only AFTER the handler returns, but the facade handler fires `workspace:applied(applied.delta)` from inside itself ŌĆö so a malformed backend delta would reach observe-only subscribers (e.g. `@ax/routines` sync `change.contentAfter`) BEFORE `invalid-return` is raised. On a security-critical write path that defeats the point. Validating up front makes the facade the unbypassable chokepoint for both the subscriber boundary and the caller. Using the original object (not zod's reparsed `parsed.data`) preserves reference identity that subscribers + the `applied`-fires-the-same-delta test (e) rely on, and keeps the lazy `contentBefore/contentAfter` fns by reference. Regression tests (f2)/(f3) in `workspace-apply-facade.test.ts`. | Keep `{ returns }` on the facade registration (rejected: validates too late ŌĆö after `applied` already fired; that's the bug); move schema to `apply-internal` (rejected: still leaves the facade's public output ungated against the `applied` fire, and the schema's home stays at the facade per the prior decision); fire `parsed.data` (rejected: breaks reference identity test (e) + needlessly clones the delta) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-12: drift guards live in `packages/core/src/__tests__/workspace-return-schemas.test.ts` (extend the ARCH-6 file: round-trip a fully-populated `WorkspaceApplyOutput`/`WorkspaceDiffOutput` incl. live `contentBefore`/`contentAfter` fns + assert the fn refs survive `.parse`). PLUS re-confirm the existing cross-backend contract assertion (`workspace-contract.ts:145` `typeof ch.contentAfter === 'function'`) still passes once the live `workspace:apply`/`diff` calls route through the now-schema'd facade/registration ŌĆö that contract suite already runs against BOTH the mock AND `@ax/workspace-git` backends, so it IS the both-backends drift guard the card asks for. | The card explicitly requires `workspace-contract.ts` re-verification across the git backend AND the mock. The contract suite is already parameterized over backends (`runWorkspaceContract(label, makePlugin)`), and its `contentAfter is lazy` test exercises a real `workspace:apply` through the bus ŌĆö so once the schema is attached, a green contract run on both backends IS the proof the schema didn't strip the fns end-to-end. The core unit round-trip is the fast/targeted guard; the contract run is the integration guard. | Add a brand-new both-backends test file (rejected: the existing contract suite already covers both backends through the bus ŌĆö duplicating it is redundant); only the core unit round-trip (rejected: doesn't prove the *attached* schema survives a real bus call, which is the security-critical path) |

## TASK-7 ŌĆö parallel-agent memory race (2026-05-24)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-24 | TASK-7: fix the parallel-agent memory race with **approach (a) ŌĆö standardize that agents write+commit `.claude/memory/` ONLY to their own worktree/branch copy, NEVER the shared main checkout** ŌĆö NOT approach (b) a lock. | (1) Memory is now COMMITTED (decision 83) so a branch-copy write lands on merge like every other file; (2) yolo-ship Phase 0 already REQUIRES a per-agent worktree, so the branch copy is the natural race-free write target; (3) the worktree copy is NO LONGER empty ŌĆö `git worktree add origin/main` carries the *tracked* `.claude/memory/` in (confirmed: worktree decisions.md = 100 lines), obsoleting the old "write to main checkout, worktree is empty" rationale (decisions 48/55/60/67/73); (4) a lock is exactly the heavy orchestration shape v2 avoids and doesn't even fix the deeper race ŌĆö last-writer-wins on `git commit` HEAD in a shared checkout still stomps; the serialized merge queue + `git pull --ff-only` already serialize landing, and divergent memory rows become a visible git merge conflict, not a silent drop. | (b) serialize main-checkout writes behind a lock (rejected: adds acquire/release/stale-recovery infra, doesn't address shared-checkout HEAD races, contradicts v2's no-heavy-orchestration ethos); keep the contradictory status quo (rejected: that IS the bug ŌĆö decisions 48/55/60/67/73 say "main checkout", ARCH-3 decision 89 says "branch copy", agents race) |
| 2026-05-24 | TASK-7: deliverable = **convention change** (CLAUDE.md "Codex Memory Bootstrap" + claude-memory skill: write/commit memory in the worktree branch copy, never the shared main checkout) PLUS a **lightweight, fully-wired, tested helper** the convention tells agents to use: `scripts/memory-write-target.sh` prints the correct `.claude/memory/` dir for the current cwd ŌĆö the linked-worktree's own copy when run inside one, else the primary copy ŌĆö using `git rev-parse --git-common-dir`/`--git-dir`/`--show-toplevel`. The convention's "write memory here" step calls it, giving it a real caller (not half-wired); a vitest test exercises both the primary-tree and linked-worktree branches in temp git repos. | The card asks for convention + a guard "if feasible, lightweight + testable; don't half-wire". A pre-commit BLOCK is the wrong shape: no husky infra here, it's bypassable, and it'd mis-fire on a legit solo human editing memory on main. An ESLint rule lints source ASTs, not fs/git location. A path-resolver helper IS the feasible, testable, genuinely-wired form ŌĆö it has a real caller (the documented memory-write step), is exercised by a hermetic vitest test (create a temp repo + a linked worktree, assert the resolved path), and *positively guides* agents to the branch copy instead of negatively blocking. | (a) pre-commit husky hook that blocks main-checkout memory writes (rejected: no husky, bypassable, mis-fires on legit human main edits, can't tell "agent" from "human"); (b) ESLint rule (rejected: wrong tool ŌĆö fs/git location isn't a source AST); (c) CI lane that fails on any `.claude/memory/**` diff (rejected: INCOHERENT ŌĆö committing memory to the branch copy IS the desired behavior); (d) convention-only, no helper (acceptable fallback per the card; rejected here only because the resolver IS cleanly testable + wired, clearing the card's bar) |
