## 2026-05-25 ŌĆö ARCH-11: shared golden-vectors drift test for MCP validators (no cross-import)

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| Date | 2026-05-25 |
| Decision | Detect drift between the runner's hand-rolled `validateMcpEntry` (`packages/agent-claude-sdk-runner/src/installed-skills.ts`) and `@ax/sandbox-protocol`'s `McpServerSchema` via a single shared JSON fixture of golden vectors, asserted by TWO independent test suites ŌĆö one in each package ŌĆö both reading the same fixture file. A divergence (one validator accepts what the other rejects) fails one suite ŌåÆ CI red. |
| Rationale | The CRITICAL INVARIANT (and the ARCH-5 design intent) is that the runner stays independent of the host contract package: NO `@ax/sandbox-protocol` import (not even devDependency) in the runner, so the sandbox-side re-validation is genuine defense-in-depth, not a thin wrapper. A shared JSON fixture is data, not code ŌĆö neither package imports the other. Each side reads the fixture via `join(__dirname,'..','..','..','..',<path>)` (the idiomatic worktree-safe repo-root pattern from cli/e2e.test.ts), then maps its own validator over the vectors. |
| Alternatives | (a) Have the runner import McpServerSchema and delegate ŌĆö REJECTED, destroys the independence that is the whole point. (b) Cross-reference comment only ŌĆö REJECTED by dispatch: a comment doesn't *detect* drift. (c) Put the drift test in one package importing the other's validator ŌĆö REJECTED: sandbox-protocol is a pure zod package, pulling in the runner (with its SDK dep) reverses+bloats the dep graph; and importing the schema into the runner-side test re-creates the forbidden coupling. Two-sided fixture is the only shape with zero cross-import. |
| Fixture home | `packages/sandbox-protocol/src/__tests__/fixtures/mcp-server-golden-vectors.json` ŌĆö sandbox-protocol OWNS the canonical schema, so the canonical vectors live with it. The runner-side test reaches it read-only via repo-root-relative path (no package dep). |
| Scope of vectors | Only the security-relevant fields BOTH validators enforce: name regex, transport enum, command presence/non-empty, args max(32)/len(256), env Record<string,string> shape + size caps, url validity, and the stdio/http transport refine (cross-contamination). EXCLUDED: cases hinging purely on `allowedHosts`/`credentials` ŌĆö the runner intentionally ignores those (it only emits name/transport/command/args/env/url into .mcp.json), so they are a KNOWN, documented benign divergence, not drift. Each vector is normalized to drop allowedHosts/credentials before the runner sees it, OR the runner-side harness ignores them (the runner already does). |
| Known benign divergence | runner `validateMcpEntry` does not look at `allowedHosts`/`credentials`; `McpServerSchema` defaults+validates them. Documented inline in both the fixture header and a cross-reference comment on `validateMcpEntry`. |

### 2026-05-25 ŌĆö ARCH-11 follow-on: assertion SEMANTICS (runner may be stricter; symmetric on the security-critical core)

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| Decision | Each golden vector declares its expected verdict per side: `schema: 'accept'|'reject'` and `runner: 'accept'|'reject'`. The test asserts BOTH sides match their declared verdict. This models the legitimate asymmetry (runner = defense-in-depth, allowed to be a strict-superset rejecter) WITHOUT letting silent drift hide: any future change to either validator that flips a verdict breaks the test, forcing a conscious fixture update + cross-reference review. A `sameVerdict` invariant subset (the security-critical shape rules: name regex, transport enum, transport refine, command presence, url validity, args caps) is additionally asserted to be IDENTICAL on both sides ŌĆö those MUST never diverge; only the env entry-count/length caps are runner-stricter-by-design. |
| Rationale | Found a real today-divergence: runner caps env to Ōēż32 entries and Ōēż256-char keys/values; `McpServerSchema` (`z.record(z.string(), z.string())`) caps neither. The dangerous direction is "schema accepts, runner accepts, but it's malicious" ŌĆö the runner is the LAST gate, so runner-stricter is the safe direction and must be allowed. The unsafe direction is "schema rejects but runner accepts" (a hole past the last gate) ŌĆö vectors with `schema:'reject', runner:'accept'` are the ones we never want to exist; the test would surface any. |
| Decision on the env-cap gap | Do NOT "fix" it by loosening the runner or tightening the schema in THIS card (scope = drift DETECTION, per dispatch). Encode the current reality in the vectors (env-oversize: `schema:'accept', runner:'reject'`) + a documented note, and return "tighten McpServerSchema env caps to match runner (Ōēż32 entries, Ōēż256 key/val)" as a deferred follow-up for auto-ship to file. Tightening the schema is the right eventual fix (host should reject early) but it changes the host contract + needs its own boundary review. |
| Human-owned? | No ŌĆö resolvable from code + the documented defense-in-depth design intent. Not escalating. |

### 2026-05-25 ŌĆö ARCH-11 codex review [P2]: runner drift half invisible to PR affected-package selection ŌĆö FIXED

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| Finding | codex exec review --base main: the runner-side drift test reads the sandbox-protocol fixture by hard-coded path, so there's NO pnpm dependency edge runnerŌåÆsandbox-protocol (by design). CI's PR test selection is `pnpm --filter "...[$BASE_SHA]"` (affected + dependents). A PR touching ONLY packages/sandbox-protocol (fixture or schema) therefore would NOT select the runner ŌåÆ the runner half of the drift guard wouldn't run on the PR, only post-merge on main's full suite. A drift-introducing fixture edit could pass the PR. |
| Verdict | VALID (verified against .github/workflows/ci.yml lines 32-45). Accepted + fixed in this PR. |
| Fix | In the PR test step, detect `git diff --name-only "$BASE_SHA"...HEAD | grep -Eq '^packages/sandbox-protocol/'` and, when matched, append `--filter @ax/agent-claude-sdk-runner` (built as a bash ARRAY to avoid shellcheck SC2086) to BOTH the affected-package list-probe and the run. actionlint-clean. The symmetric case (runner-only change) is already covered: `...[SHA]` selects the runner so its drift test runs; the schema didn't change so the schema-side test can't newly fail. |
| Why not a dep edge or root-script test | A dep edge would re-create the forbidden coupling (defeats the whole card). A root `scripts/` test would need to import/build both packages from a third location, widening reach. A path-scoped CI inclusion keeps the fix entirely in CI config ŌĆö zero production-code or dependency-graph change ŌĆö and is the project's established pattern (see helm-render / image-build path-scoped lanes in the same workflow). |
| 2026-05-25 | FAULTA-5 (Faults B/D ŌĆö host bounce / network drop ŌåÆ silent finalize): fix the `@ax/channel-web` client's `done`-less SSE close so it no longer synthesizes a `finish` (`finishReason:'stop'`) that looks like a successful turn. Instead: (1) transport's `processResponseStream` `flush()` (the no-`done`-frame branch) emits an AI-SDK `error` UIMessageChunk whose `errorText` is a NEW shared sentinel `CONNECTION_LOST` (`'Connection lost. RetryingŌĆ”'`-class wording), exported from `transport.ts`; (2) the runtime's `onError` (runtime.tsx) tracks a per-turn retry count in a ref ŌĆö on the FIRST connection-lost error it SILENTLY retries via `regenerate()` (sets the agent-status row to a transient working "Connection lost ŌĆö retryingŌĆ”" label, NO error banner), and on a SECOND failure (or any non-connection-lost error) it falls through to the existing `applyTurnError` error banner + retry affordance. Distinguish connection-lost from orchestrator `error`-frame errors by matching `error.message === CONNECTION_LOST`. Reuses the existing AgentStatus row (error mode = red dot + retry button; working mode = "Connection lost ŌĆö retryingŌĆ”") ŌĆö NO new shadcn primitives. | The task scopes this as a transport-`flush()` concern, NOT an orchestrator-terminated-outcome (Fault A/F2b, already handled by the `error`-frame path). Root cause confirmed in code: `transport.ts` flush (lines 570-578) enqueues `{type:'finish',finishReason:'stop'}` on a `done`-less close, indistinguishable from success ŌĆö so a host bounce (Fault B, process dies ŌåÆ in-memory chunk-buffer gone ŌåÆ reqId 404 on reconnect) or network drop (Fault D, TCP severed ŌåÆ no `done`/`error` frame ever arrives) silently finalizes a half-streamed turn. In-transport SSE re-open of the SAME reqId is NOT viable: the server's chunk-buffer (`chunk-buffer.ts`) replays the FULL tail on reconnect (ŌåÆ duplicate text) AND is replica-local with a 60s TTL that's wiped by a host bounce (ŌåÆ 404). So the robust silent-retry primitive is the runtime's existing `regenerate()` (re-POSTs the last user turn ŌåÆ fresh reqId ŌåÆ fresh sandbox ŌåÆ re-answers), which `applyTurnError`'s retry already uses. The sentinel is an INTERNAL `@ax/channel-web` contract (not a hook payload) shared exactly like the existing `DEFAULT_TURN_ERROR` between transport.ts + turn-error.ts ŌĆö no I1/I2 violation. | (a) silent retry INSIDE the transport by re-GETting the same reqId (rejected: buffer-replay duplicates already-rendered text + host bounce 404s the reqId ŌĆö unreliable); (b) just emit the SAME error banner immediately on done-less close, no silent retry (rejected: task explicitly wants "silent retry first, THEN banner"); (c) a custom Error subclass to type the retryable error (rejected: the AI-SDK reconstructs a PLAIN `Error` from the chunk's `errorText`, so a subclass doesn't survive to `onError` ŌĆö match on the message sentinel instead); (d) infinite silent retries (rejected: a persistent outage would loop forever ŌĆö cap at one silent retry, then surface the banner) |
| 2026-05-25 | FAULTA-5 Phase-5 Codex review (2 P2 findings, both ACCEPTED + fixed against verified AI-SDK source): (1) **defer the silent `regenerate()`** ŌĆö the AI SDK (`ai@6` `chat.ts` `makeRequest`) calls `onError` INSIDE the failed request's `catch` (line 753), BEFORE the `finally` (758-773) sets `this.activeResponse = undefined`. A SYNCHRONOUS `regenerate()` from `onError` re-enters `makeRequest`, sets a NEW `activeResponse`, then the ORIGINAL request's finally nukes it ŌåÆ the retry loses its abort handle and its `onFinish` throws on `this.activeResponse!` (undefined) ŌåÆ `silentRetriedRef` never resets. Fix: wrap the silent `regenerate()` in `setTimeout(ŌĆ”,0)` so the failed request fully unwinds first (the manual banner-retry needs no defer ŌĆö it's already outside the request lifecycle). (2) **hard network drop wasn't covered** ŌĆö the transport `flush()` only fires on a GRACEFUL body close; a real mid-turn fetch drop (Fault D) ERRORS the fetch-body ReadableStream, SKIPS the TransformStream flush, and the AI SDK surfaces the raw fetch `TypeError` to onError (it even flags `isDisconnect` via the same heuristic). So the original diff showed the banner immediately on a true network drop instead of silently retrying. Fix: broaden `isConnectionLost` (turn-error.ts) to ALSO match a `TypeError` whose message includes "fetch"/"network" (mirrors the SDK's own `chat.ts` disconnect heuristic) ŌĆö covering BOTH the graceful done-less close (CONNECTION_LOST sentinel) and the hard drop. Added 4 unit tests (Bug Fix Policy) pinning the fetch/network-TypeError silent-retry + the second-failureŌåÆbanner + unrelated-TypeErrorŌåÆbanner negative. | Both findings are dead-on and go to the CORE behavior the card demands (silent retry on a genuine network drop; a clean retry lifecycle). Verified each by reading `ai@6` `node_modules/ai/src/ui/chat.ts`: the catchŌåÆfinally ordering (1) and the `TypeError`+`includes('fetch'/'network')`ŌåÆ`isDisconnect` path (744-751) that bypasses our flush (2). Codex is a colleague ŌĆö I confirmed against source rather than deferring blindly, and the AI-SDK heuristic is exactly the one I mirror. | (1) alt: `queueMicrotask` instead of `setTimeout` (rejected: a microtask still runs within the same async continuation as the awaited rejection's finally on some engines; `setTimeout(0)` macrotask guarantees the finally's `activeResponse=undefined` has executed). (2) alt: catch the stream error inside the transport and re-emit a CONNECTION_LOST chunk (rejected: the error originates in the fetch body feeding the TextDecoderStream ŌĆö intercepting it cleanly means wrapping consumeStream internals; matching the SDK's already-classified TypeError in ONE place (isConnectionLost) is simpler, DRY with the existing sentinel decision, and mirrors the SDK's own heuristic). |
| 2026-05-25 | FAULTA-5 Phase-5 Codex round 2 (1 P2, ACCEPTED + fixed): the silent-retry one-shot cap LEAKED ACROSS TURNS. A `silentRetriedRef` boolean reset only on a clean `onFinish` or a manual banner click ŌĆö so after a connection-lost turn spent its retry AND the retry also failed (both onFinish calls carry error/disconnect flags ŌåÆ no reset), the ref stayed `true`; if the user then SUBMITTED A DIFFERENT message instead of clicking the banner, that fresh turn's first drop saw `isFirstFailure=false` and went straight to the banner, skipping its own silent retry. Fix: replace the boolean + onFinish-reset with a PER-TURN budget (`createRetryBudget()` in turn-error.ts) keyed on the failing turn's identity ŌĆö the runtime passes the LAST USER MESSAGE ID as `turnKey`. `regenerate()` re-runs the same last user turn (key unchanged ŌåÆ budget persists across the retry); a new submission appends a new user message (new id ŌåÆ budget resets). Refactored `handleTurnError` to take `{turnKey, budget}` and consume the budget ONLY on the connection-lost path (a Fault A error never burns a later drop's retry). Dropped the `onFinish` handler entirely (the per-turn key makes it redundant). Added a `createRetryBudget` describe block (per-turn allow-one, reset-on-new-key, null-key-shared) + the exact end-to-end scenario Codex named (turn A exhausts+fails ŌåÆ turn B still silently retries). Net: 525 channel-web tests green. | Codex round 1's two findings were fixed in the prior commit; round 2 caught the budget-leak that the boolean approach introduced. Keying to the user message id is the natural per-turn boundary: it's stable across `regenerate()` (same turn) and changes on a new send ŌĆö exactly the semantics the cap needs. Extracting the budget as a pure `createRetryBudget` keeps the leak-prevention logic unit-testable without `useChat` (which the runtime test harness mocks), consistent with the applyTurnError/handleTurnError pure-helper pattern. | (a) reset the boolean on every `status==='submitted'` transition (rejected: useChat exposes no per-submit callback; status is a derived value, and distinguishing a fresh submit from a regenerate via status alone is racy); (b) reset in the transport's sendMessages on `trigger==='submit-message'` (rejected: the transport is a separate object from the runtime ref ŌĆö would need to thread the budget through the transport, coupling two layers; the message-id key lives naturally in the runtime); (c) keep onFinish + also reset on send (rejected: more moving parts than a single per-turn-keyed budget, and the onFinish-on-error timing was already subtle) |
| 2026-05-25 | FAULTA-5 Phase-5 Codex round 3 (2 P2, both ACCEPTED + fixed): (A) **non-idempotent silent replay** ŌĆö broadening `isConnectionLost` to match any fetch/network `TypeError` (round-1 fix #2) was TOO broad: a `TypeError('Failed to fetch')` can come from the non-idempotent `POST /api/chat/messages` or the initial `GET /api/chat/stream/:reqId` ŌĆö BOTH run in `sendMessages` BEFORE a stream is returned. If the POST already reached the host (agent started) but its response failed, a silent `regenerate()` re-POSTs ŌåÆ DUPLICATE conversation/turn/agent invocation (no client idempotency key). Fix: make the TRANSPORT the single authority for "safe to silently retry" ŌĆö narrow `isConnectionLost` back to ONLY the `CONNECTION_LOST` sentinel, and in the transport wrap the parsed SSE stream in an outer error-catching `ReadableStream` that converts a HARD mid-stream body error (the fetch body ReadableStream errors DURING consumption ŌĆö Fault D, after the stream exists) into the SAME CONNECTION_LOST chunk. Pre-stream POST/GET `TypeError`s now surface as a plain rejection ŌåÆ banner (manual retry), never a silent re-POST. (B) **status stuck in error mode** ŌĆö the silent-retry path used `agentStatusActions.set(CONNECTION_LOST)`, but `set()` only swaps TEXT when mode is already `error` (it preserves `mode:'error'` + the stale retry/dismiss handlers). So if a prior error banner was still visible when the silent retry began, the "silent" path still showed the red banner. Fix: use `agentStatusActions.show(CONNECTION_LOST)` (forces `mode:'working'`, clears retry/dismiss). Added tests: transport mid-stream-errorŌåÆCONNECTION_LOST conversion + body-error-after-doneŌåÆno-spurious-error; turn-error idempotency guard (raw fetch TypeErrorŌåÆbanner, NOT silent) + show()-forces-working-over-stale-error-banner. Net 527 channel-web green. | Both findings are correct and important. (A) is a genuine data-integrity bug I INTRODUCED in round 1 ŌĆö verified `sendMessages` does POST then GET before returning the stream (transport.ts:322,346), so a pre-stream TypeError WAS being classified retryable. Moving the mid-stream-errorŌåÆsentinel conversion INTO the transport is the right boundary: the transport alone knows whether the stream was established (= safe to retry the already-started turn) vs failed at request time (= unsafe). (B) verified against agent-status-store.set (preserves error mode) vs show (forces working+clears handlers). | (A) alt: thread an idempotency key through the POST so a re-POST dedupes server-side (rejected: bigger change touching the server route + conversations store; out of scope for a client-side flush fix, and the transport-authority approach is sufficient + simpler); (A) alt: keep the TypeError match but only on the GET phase (rejected: can't distinguish POST-vs-GET TypeError from the error alone; the stream-established boundary is the clean signal). (B) alt: clear the error row before each turn elsewhere (rejected: RunningEffect already does this on turn start, but the silent-retry path can fire before that effect settles ŌĆö forcing working mode AT the decision point is the robust local fix). |
| 2026-05-25 | FAULTA-5 Phase-5 Codex round 4 (1 P1, ACCEPTED ŌĆö fundamental rework): an automatic `regenerate()` on a CLIENT-SIDE mid-stream drop DUPLICATES a live server turn. Verified against the server: a client SSE disconnect only triggers `stream.onClose`ŌåÆ`cleanup()` which UNSUBSCRIBES the per-connection bus subscribers (sse.ts:196) ŌĆö it does NOT terminate the runner or evict the reqId buffer (eviction is turn-end/turn-error/60s-TTL only). And every `POST /api/chat/messages` MINTS A NEW reqId + dispatches a fresh `agent:invoke` (routes-chat.ts:51-55) ŌĆö `regenerate()` re-POSTs, so on a Fault-D network drop (host fine, turn still running) it queues a DUPLICATE prompt + duplicate tool side-effects while the original turn finishes. **Rework:** move the silent retry OUT of the runtime's regenerate and INTO the transport as a same-reqId RECONNECT loop. `sendMessages` POSTs ONCE (one reqId, one agent:invoke ever), then returns a single continuous outer `ReadableStream` whose `start` loops: GET `/stream/:reqId`, parse one attempt; a terminal `done`ŌåÆfinish or server `error` frame closes the outer stream; a NON-terminal end (graceful done-less close OR hard body error) RECONNECTS by re-GETting the SAME reqId (the server is purpose-built to replay the buffer tail ŌĆö sse.ts:214-238) ŌĆö NO new POST, so it can NEVER duplicate the turn. To avoid double-rendering the replayed tail, the transport tracks `emittedContent` count and SKIPS that many content chunks on each reconnect attempt. Bounded at `MAX_RECONNECTS` attempts; when the GET 404s (Fault B host bounce ŌĆö reqId+buffer gone) or the cap is exhausted, emit the CONNECTION_LOST `error` chunk ŌåÆ the runtime surfaces the BANNER with a manual-retry (regenerate) affordance. The runtime's onError NO LONGER does a silent regenerate at all ŌĆö silent recovery is 100% transport-side reconnect (idempotent); the banner's manual retry (a deliberate user action) is the only path that re-POSTs. | Codex's P1 is correct and decisive ŌĆö the regenerate-based silent retry was unsafe for the exact Fault D the card names. Considered escalating to the human (the "silent retry" requirement vs the no-duplication correctness constraint is a genuine tension given the POST-always-creates-a-new-turn server contract), but it's self-answerable: the correct primitive is reconnect-to-same-reqId (GET-only, idempotent), which the server already supports, and it honors BOTH the requirement (silent retry first) AND correctness (no duplicate turn). Rejected AI-SDK `resumeStream()`/`reconnectToStream`: on resume it mints a NEW message id (ai@6 chat.ts makeRequest) ŌåÆ pushes a SECOND assistant bubble and replays the full buffer into it (duplicate visible answer), and `reconnectToStream` isn't handed the reqId. The in-transport loop keeps ONE continuous stream ŌåÆ ONE assistant message, with prefix-dedup. | (a) keep regenerate but show banner only on hard error (rejected: still duplicates on the graceful-close path, and drops the silent-retry requirement); (b) server-side idempotency key on POST (rejected: out of the client-side scope, larger blast radius ŌĆö touches the route + conversations store); (c) AI-SDK resumeStream (rejected: duplicate message bubble + no reqId, per above); (d) escalate to human as blocked (rejected: responsibly self-answerable ŌĆö reconnect is the unambiguously-correct primitive the server already supports) |
| 2026-05-25 | FAULTA-5 Phase-5 Codex round 5 (3 P2 in the new reconnect logic, all ACCEPTED + fixed): (A) **abort treated as connection-loss** ŌĆö on user-Stop/teardown the AI SDK aborts the fetch; the body read rejects ŌåÆ `consumeSseAttempt` returns 'lost' ŌåÆ my `abortSignal?.aborted` branch emitted CONNECTION_LOST = a spurious retry banner for an intentional cancel. Fix: on a 'lost' attempt, if `abortSignal.aborted` close the stream WITHOUT an error chunk (let the SDK's abort path run). (B) **stale carry corrupts reconnect** ŌĆö `ctx.carry` retains a partial `data:` line stranded by a mid-line drop; the reconnect reuses the same ctx, so the replayed buffer's first frame gets prefixed with the stale fragment ŌåÆ JSON parse fails ŌåÆ a frame dropped. Fix: `ctx.carry=''` on every reconnect (alongside the skipContent reset). (C) **over-skip past the replay window** ŌĆö the server ring buffer retains only its last ~256 chunks; once `emittedContent` exceeds that, a reconnect's PARTIAL replay can't be count-deduped (skipping the full lifetime count eats live chunks = silent loss). Fix: only attempt the silent reconnect while `emittedContent <= SERVER_REPLAY_WINDOW` (=200, a conservative local mirror of the server's 256 ŌĆö NOT imported, I2); beyond it, surface the banner (user re-runs manually) ŌĆö flipping the failure mode from silent-loss to a visible banner. Added 3 tests: abortŌåÆno-error-chunk+no-reconnect; mid-line-dropŌåÆcarry-clearedŌåÆ"onetwo" intact; 201-frame turnŌåÆno reconnectŌåÆbanner. Net 522 channel-web green. | All three are correct functional bugs in the round-4 reconnect code. (A) verified against the AI SDK abort path (makeRequest's catch treats AbortError specially); surfacing a banner on Stop is clearly wrong. (B) the carry is per-attempt state that must reset with skipContent. (C) is a real wire-contract limitation: without a per-chunk server sequence number the client can't align a partial replay ŌĆö the honest fix is to bound the silent reconnect to the safe window and degrade to the (already-correct) banner beyond it. FOLLOW-UP for auto-ship: add a monotonic per-chunk sequence number to the SSE wire (server `chat:stream-chunk`/SseFrame + chunk-buffer) so the client can dedup an arbitrary partial replay exactly and reconnect past the 256-chunk window. | (A) alt: rethrow the AbortError (rejected: the outer ReadableStream start() rejecting is messier than a clean close; close is the documented graceful end); (C) alt: import the server's 256 const (rejected: I2 cross-plugin import ŌĆö mirror conservatively); (C) alt: dedup by content-fingerprint instead of count (rejected: a truncated replay's first chunk won't align to emitted[0] ŌåÆ would duplicate the boundary; needs a server seq number to do right ŌĆö filed as the follow-up); (C) alt: re-render the replayed tail without dedup past the window (rejected: duplicates visible text in the message ŌĆö worse UX than a banner the user can act on) |
| 2026-05-25 | FAULTA-5 Phase-5 Codex round 6 (2 P2, both ACCEPTED + fixed): (A) **abort DURING the reconnect GET** ŌĆö round 5 checked `abortSignal.aborted` after a 'lost' attempt but NOT in the reconnect `open(reqId, abortSignal)` catch. If the user aborts while that GET is pending, fetch rejects with AbortError and the catch called `endWithBanner()` = spurious banner on an intentional cancel. Fix: in the catch, if `abortSignal?.aborted`, close cleanly (no banner); else give up with the banner. (B) **replay side-effects before dedup** ŌĆö the skip was inside `enqueueContent`, but `ensureOpenForKind()` (text/thinking) already emitted text-start/text-end and tool frames already called `closeOpen()` BEFORE the enqueue ŌĆö so a deduped (replayed) chunk still injected stray structural chunks (empty/split parts, premature text-end) for replays that include thinkingŌåötext transitions or tool calls. Fix: gate the skip UPSTREAM ŌĆö detect a content-bearing frame and, if `skipContent>0`, decrement + `continue` BEFORE any framing/side-effects; `enqueueContent` is now emit-only (skip handled upstream). Added 2 tests: abort-during-reconnect-GETŌåÆno-banner; reconnect-replay-of-thinkingŌåÆtextŌåÆno-stray-text-start (asserts startIds stay `['thinking-0','text-0']` and the continuation reuses text-0). Net 524 channel-web green. | Both correct. (A) is the same abort-isn't-loss principle as round 5(A) but on the GET-pending path I'd missed. (B) is subtle: the framing side-effects (ensureOpenForKind/closeOpen) run for EVERY content frame, so skipping only the final enqueue still corrupts the part structure on replay ŌĆö the skip must happen before the branch does anything. Gating once, upstream, is also DRYer than guarding each branch. | (A) none meaningful. (B) alt: guard inside each of ensureOpenForKind/closeOpen with a skip flag (rejected: scatters the skip logic across 4 branches + 2 helpers; one upstream gate is clearer and matches "decide to skip before any side effect"). |
| 2026-05-25 | FAULTA-5 Phase-5 Codex round 7 (1 P2, ACCEPTED ŌĆö confirms count-dedup is fundamentally unsound; final design): the round-5 `emittedContent <= SERVER_REPLAY_WINDOW(200)` guard checks the WRONG quantity. The real hazard is the SERVER outrunning its 256-chunk ring buffer WHILE THE CLIENT IS DISCONNECTED: client emitted e.g. 50 chunks (emittedContent=50, under the guard), but during the disconnect the agent streamed to 400 ŌåÆ the buffer now holds chunks 144ŌĆō400 (0ŌĆō143 evicted). On reconnect the replay tail starts at #144, NOT #51 ŌĆö `skipContent=50` skips 144ŌĆō193 and the client NEVER sees 51ŌĆō193 (silent loss). The client CANNOT detect this without a per-chunk sequence number the wire doesn't carry. **Final resolution: gate silent reconnect on `emittedContent === 0` (PRE-CONTENT only).** Before any content streams, the replay is necessarily complete-from-the-start, dedup is a no-op, and silent recovery is loss-free ŌĆö this covers the common "blip before the first token" case (sandbox-starting, proxy idle-cull, tab refocus). Once ANY content has streamed, a drop surfaces the CONNECTION_LOST banner (manual retry) instead of risking a lossy resume. Removed the now-dead `skipContent` field + the per-frame skip-gate + `SERVER_REPLAY_WINDOW` (Half-Wired Code Policy ŌĆö no longer reachable). Rewrote the reconnect tests to the new semantics (pre-content drop ŌåÆ silent resume incl. hard body error; content-then-drop ŌåÆ banner no-reconnect; 404 ŌåÆ banner; cap; abort variants). Net 522 channel-web green. FOLLOW-UP (handoff ŌåÆ auto-ship): add a monotonic per-chunk sequence number to the SSE wire (SseFrame + chunk-buffer + the chat:stream-chunk producer) so the client can dedup an arbitrary partial replay exactly and resume MID-CONTENT ŌĆö that's what would let the silent retry cover the full Fault-D space, not just the pre-content window. | Codex is right and this closes the dedup question definitively: without a server cursor, ANY content-resuming reconnect risks silent loss, which is unacceptable for this project ("we're the secure one" ŌĆö silent data loss is worse than a visible banner the user can act on). The pre-content gate is the maximal SAFE silent-retry slice; it still delivers the task's "silent retry first" for the most common blip and degrades to the required "error banner with retry" once content is in flight. This is a defensible scope line: the loss-free silent recovery ships now; the mid-content resume needs a server wire change (sequence number) that's out of this client-side card's framed scope ŌåÆ tracked as a follow-up rather than silently shipping a lossy resume or unilaterally expanding scope. | (a) banner-only, no silent reconnect at all (rejected: drops the "silent retry first" requirement even for the safe pre-content case); (b) ship count-dedup accepting rare silent loss (rejected: silent data loss is non-negotiable here); (c) expand THIS card to add the server sequence number (rejected: card is framed as a client-side transport flush concern, not an SSE wire-protocol change ŌĆö file as follow-up); (d) escalate to human as blocked (considered ŌĆö the requirement-vs-correctness tension is real ŌĆö but self-answerable: the pre-content gate is the unambiguously-correct safe subset that honors the hard requirement (no silent finalize + banner+retry) AND a meaningful slice of the soft one (silent retry for the common blip), with the residual tracked) |
| 2026-05-25 | FAULTA-5 Phase-5 Codex round 8 (1 P2, ACCEPTED ŌĆö collapses to the simplest correct design): even the round-7 PRE-CONTENT-only reconnect can silently lose output. If the first attempt drops pre-content but the agent keeps streaming while the reconnect is delayed and produces >256 chunks before the new GET attaches, the server buffer has TRUNCATED to its tail ŌĆö the replay starts mid-answer, and the client renders the tail as a complete answer, silently omitting the earlier chunks. The `emittedContent===0` gate doesn't help because the truncation is server-side. This DEFINITIVELY proves NO client-side buffer-replay reconnect is loss-free without a server sequence number. **Final shipped design: REMOVE the silent reconnect entirely.** A mid-turn drop (graceful done-less close OR hard body error) ŌåÆ `buildTurnStream` emits CONNECTION_LOST ŌåÆ the existing AgentStatus error banner + manual retry. A server `error` frame keeps its mapped label; abort closes cleanly (no banner); clean `done` finishes normally. One POST + one GET per turn. Removed `buildReconnectingStream`/`MAX_RECONNECTS`/`openSseStream` reconnect helper (Half-Wired Code Policy); `sendMessages` GETs once ŌåÆ `buildTurnStream`. Rewrote tests to the banner-on-drop semantics (done-lessŌåÆbanner; hard-errorŌåÆbanner; clean-doneŌåÆfinish; Fault-A label; abortŌåÆno-banner; all 1-POST-1-GET). Net 520 channel-web green. **This is the correct, safe, shippable resolution:** it fully fixes the FAULTA-5 bug (no silent finalize) + delivers the required "error banner with retry"; the "silent retry first" UX refinement cannot be done loss-free client-side and is filed as a follow-up gated on the server sequence number. FOLLOW-UP (handoff): add a monotonic per-chunk seq number to the SSE wire (SseFrame + chunk-buffer + chat:stream-chunk producer) ŌåÆ enables exact partial-replay dedup ŌåÆ a transparent mid-turn silent resume. | Codex round 8 is the natural endpoint of the rounds-5ŌĆō7 dedup thread: it shows the unsoundness is intrinsic to buffer-replay-without-a-cursor, not fixable by any client-side gate. The project's "we're the secure one" ethos makes silent data loss strictly worse than a visible banner the user can act on. Removing the reconnect also removes a lot of subtle state (skip cursor, carry reset, abort-during-GET, replay framing) ŌĆö the simplest design is also the most obviously correct. I judged this self-answerable rather than blocked: every alternative that keeps a silent reconnect ships known silent loss (unacceptable), and the server-cursor fix is a wire-protocol change out of this client-side card's framed scope ŌĆö so the right move is to ship the loss-free banner now and file the cursor follow-up, which I can decide without a human. | (a) keep pre-content reconnect (rejected: round 8 proves it's still lossy on a truncated buffer); (b) ship with known rare silent loss (rejected: non-negotiable); (c) expand scope to add the server cursor now (rejected: SSE wire-protocol change beyond the client-side flush concern this card scopes ŌĆö follow-up); (d) escalate as blocked (considered, but self-answerable: the safe loss-free subset is unambiguous and fully satisfies the hard requirement; the deferred silent-resume is tracked) |
| 2026-05-25 | FAULTA-5 Phase-5 Codex round 9 (1 P2, ACCEPTED ŌĆö UX copy): the CONNECTION_LOST banner text was `'Connection lost. RetryingŌĆ”'`, a leftover from the (removed) silent-retry design. | 2026-05-25 | TASK-20: fix the dead "unknown artifact" chip by resolving `ax://artifact/<id>` prose-links in `MarkdownText` against ALL thread messages, not just the current message. Root cause (confirmed empirically): the `artifact_publish` tool-call result and the assistant text holding the `[Download <name>](ax://artifact/<id>)` link land in SEPARATE assistant messages ŌĆö the SDK runner emits the tool result, then the closing text as a fresh assistant turn (and `conversations:get` reload builds one renderable message per turn with distinct parent_id, so the two don't coalesce the way consecutive *streaming* deltas do). The old resolver scanned only `useMessage(m=>m.content)` (current message), never found the artifact tool-call, and fell back to the disabled "unknown artifact" pill. | 2026-05-25 | TASK-23: SSE per-chunk seq for loss-free silent turn-resume (FAULTA-5 follow-up). seq is assigned by channel-web's `ChunkBuffer` (the replica-local per-reqId stateful structure that already owns the chunk ring), NOT in ipc-core's `fireEventStreamChunk` and NOT on the `@ax/ipc-protocol` `EventStreamChunkSchema` IPC wire. `ChunkBuffer.append` mints the next per-reqId monotonic int (1-based) and stores it on the buffered frame; the buffer-fill subscriber stamps it onto the outgoing `chat:stream-chunk` payload by RETURNING the seq-stamped payload (bus contract `result!==undefined ŌåÆ current=result`, NOT an implicit mutation) so the per-connection live SSE subscriber and `tail()` replay both carry the SAME seq. `SseFrame` content variants gain an optional `seq: number`. Client (`transport.ts`) tracks `lastSeq`, skips any replayed frame with `seq<=lastSeq` (exact dedup), and on a contiguity gap that exceeds the bounded 256-chunk buffer falls back to FAULTA-5's CONNECTION_LOST banner (silent loss is worse than a banner ŌĆö honored). | The ipc-server `stream-chunk.test.ts` asserts the `chat:stream-chunk` subscriber receives the runner payload verbatim (`toEqual(body)`), and event-stream-chunk.ts's doc says "the handler MUST NOT reshape" ŌĆö so seq CANNOT be assigned host-side at the IPC dispatch layer without breaking that contract + leaking a channel-web concern into the IPC kernel. The buffer is already per-reqId, replica-local (J7), TTL-evicted ŌĆö the natural monotonic authority. Host assigns (not runner) so untrusted runner content never controls the dedup cursor (I5). seq is a plain monotonic int = transport/storage-agnostic (I1, no git/sqlite/k8s vocab). IPC wire + ipc-protocol stay UNCHANGED ŌåÆ no cross-package churn. | (a) assign seq in `fireEventStreamChunk` (rejected: breaks the verbatim-passthrough IPC contract + test, puts SSE-replay sequencing state in the IPC kernel ŌĆö wrong layer); (b) runner mints seq on `event.stream-chunk` (rejected: untrusted runner would control the client's dedup cursor ŌĆö a buggy/malicious runner could replay/skew seq and defeat loss-free dedup, I5 violation; also an IPC-protocol change); (c) buffer-fill mutates the shared payload object in place (rejected: implicit cross-subscriber side-effect that silently depends on registration order; returning the stamped payload uses the documented bus merge contract explicitly) |
| 2026-05-25 | TASK-23 (Codex review rounds, 4 findings, all fixed): (P1) the channel-web ChunkBuffer's IDLE_TTL sweep used to fully `map.delete` a still-live reqId entry that went quiet > 60s mid-turn (e.g. a long tool call); the next live chunk recreated it at seq 1, and a still-connected client with lastSeq>0 silently DEDUPED (dropped) it ŌĆö the exact loss seq exists to prevent. Fix: sweep now reclaims the heavy fields (chunks/phase) into a lightweight cursor-only SHELL but keeps `nextSeq` monotonic; only `evictReqId` (real turn-end/turn-error) resets the cursor. (P2a) client used to accept ANY first seq as a baseline ŌĆö a first frame at seq 257 (256-cap dropped the head before connect) rendered the tail as a complete answer, silently omitting 1..256. Fix: servers mint from 1, so a FIRST seq-bearing content frame > 1 ŌćÆ truncated head ŌćÆ CONNECTION_LOST (not silent render). (P2b) a content turn ending via chat:turn-error with NO SSE listener stored the error but no evictor ran; the reclaim path would keep its dead cursor shell forever. Fix: sweep FULLY deletes any entry holding a terminal turnError (cursor dead ŌĆö no chunks follow a turn-error) before the reclaimed-shell check. (P2c) an orphaned shell (runner crashed before any terminal hook) leaked one map entry each. Fix: reap a reclaimed shell once it ages past a ceiling. (P2d) the client's locally-detected seq-gap return('lost') left the fetch body OPEN (finally only releaseLock'd) ŌĆö the server kept per-connection subscribers/writes alive until turn-end/timeout. Fix: reader.cancel() (propagates upstream to the HTTP body) before returning, and skip the now-redundant releaseLock. (P2-round2) the fixed 15-min shell ceiling sits BELOW an operator-raised AX_CHAT_TIMEOUT_MS ŌĆö a legit quiet turn past 15 min would get its cursor reaped ŌåÆ seq reset ŌåÆ silent loss. Fix: ChunkBufferOptions.shellMaxAgeMs is configurable; ChannelWebServerConfig.chatTimeoutMs (sizing hint, NOT a 2nd source of truth ŌĆö orchestrator owns the timeout) ŌåÆ shellMaxAgeMs = chatTimeoutMs + 5min slack; preset/k8s passes orchestratorCfg.chatTimeoutMs (covers CLI `serve` too via createK8sPlugins). | Codex is a colleague: each finding was verified against the code before fixing (the P1/P2b/P2c interplay is real ŌĆö the reclaim shell I added for P1 created the P2b/P2c leak surfaces, which the subsequent rounds tightened). All fixes are test-first (Bug Fix Policy): chunk-buffer.test.ts gained cursor-monotonic-across-sweep, evict-resets-after-sweep, turn-error-full-reap, orphan-reap-after-ceiling, configurable-ceiling; transport.test.ts gained first-frame>1ŌåÆbanner, gapŌåÆcancel-body. | Per-finding alternatives rejected: (P1) "surface reset as connection loss" ŌĆö buffer can't see live connections, so keep the cursor instead; (P2b) keep the shell + reap later ŌĆö wrong, a turn-error turn is terminated so its cursor is dead, full delete is correct; (P2c) unbounded shells ŌĆö rejected (leak); (P2-round2) hardcode a bigger fixed ceiling ŌĆö rejected (still breaks for an even-larger operator timeout; configurable+derived is the only correct fix that stays above the max live turn for ANY configured timeout) |

## 2026-05-25 ŌĆö TASK-25: npm binary-download egress (docs + actionable error)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-25 | **#3's "clear actionable error" = add a message body to the CONNECT allowlist-miss 403** in `credential-proxy/src/listener.ts handleCONNECT`. | The HTTP-forward path ALREADY writes an actionable 403 body ("Domain X is not in any session allowlist. Install a skill that declares this domain, or ask an admin to approve it."); the HTTPS CONNECT path ŌĆö which is exactly what a binary download over https uses ŌĆö writes a BARE `403 Forbidden` with no body. Bringing CONNECT to parity is the minimal, in-boundary fix and reuses an established message. Extract a shared helper so the two sites can't drift. | (a) Surface the blocked-egress event into the chat turn ŌĆö bigger surface, touches the orchestrator turn-error path, and the card scoped #3 to "surface a clear error", which the 403 body satisfies at the boundary where the failing tool actually reads it. (b) Leave it as audit-log only ŌĆö rejected: that's the silent-failure status quo the card calls out. |
| 2026-05-25 | **#1's docs home = `docs/plans/2026-05-22-credentialed-cli-tools-and-git-auth-design.md` (Sub-project D, the `capabilities.packages` section).** | No standalone "skill-authoring guide" doc exists; this design doc is the canonical author-facing place where `packages.npm` ŌåÆ `registry.npmjs.org` auto-allowlist is documented. Putting the gotcha next to the behavior it qualifies is where an author reading about `packages.npm` will see it. | Create a new dedicated skill-authoring doc ŌĆö rejected (no precedent, and the conventions doc says docs are friction-driven; one gotcha subsection doesn't earn a new doc). |
| 2026-05-25 | **#2 (auto-allowlist github.com + release-assets.githubusercontent.com by default) stays OUT.** | Explicit card clarification + orchestration override: widening the default egress surface is a security-owner decision deferred to a separate card. ## 2026-05-25 ŌĆö TASK-26: no-TTY CLI stdout (env-hints)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-25 | TASK-26: TTY-detecting CLIs (cliffy/Deno e.g. @schpet/linear-cli, ink, many Rust/Go tools) emit ZERO stdout in the detached sandbox because the SDK Bash tool's child has no controlling TTY. Fix = ENV-HINT route (NOT a pty): a new pure helper `buildTtyHintEnv()` in `@ax/agent-claude-sdk-runner` returning `{ TERM:'xterm-256color', COLUMNS:'120', LINES:'40', FORCE_COLOR:'1', CI:'1' }`, spread into the SDK `query({options:{env}})` literal in main.ts FIRST (before proxyStartup.anthropicEnv) so a real forwarded TERM/COLUMNS from process.env still wins. These flip the common detectors: FORCE_COLOR (chalk/supports-color), TERM+COLUMNS+LINES (cliffy/Deno isTerminal heuristics + width), CI=1 (CI-aware tools choose plain non-interactive writers). | Per the card's explicit scope guidance, prefer env-hints; a pty is ON the table only if hints insufficient AND no significant sandbox-security concern. A pty MEANINGFULLY weakens the boundary (allocating a real `/dev/pts` master+slave for untrusted model-driven Bash adds a kernel-object + ioctl surface, complicates the gVisor/read-only-rootfs k8s pod, and grants the sandboxed process an interactive control channel it doesn't need ŌĆö capability-minimization I5 says no). Env-hints are inert strings, change zero capabilities, and `TERM`/`COLUMNS`/`LINES` are ALREADY in proxy-startup ENV_ALLOWLIST (just never set in the detached host), so the precedent is set. ŌåÆ pty TAKEN OFF THE TABLE. | (a) pseudo-TTY for the Bash child (rejected: significant sandbox-boundary cost per above, and env-hints suffice for the targeted class); (b) only FORCE_COLOR (rejected: color isn't the gate ŌĆö the tool emits NOTHING incl plain --help; need TERM+size+CI too); (c) document the limitation only (rejected: card's desired outcome is a CODE FIX that makes tools emit, plus a compat note ŌĆö not docs-only) |
| 2026-05-25 | TASK-26: helper lives in the RUNNER (`@ax/agent-claude-sdk-runner/tty-hint-env.ts`), spread into the single SDK env literal in main.ts ŌĆö NOT in the per-backend sandbox env (sandbox-subprocess open-session.ts / sandbox-k8s pod-spec.ts). | One source of truth (I4): both sandbox backends funnel their session env into the runner, which then builds the SINGLE `query({options:{env}})` env the SDK Bash tool actually inherits (proven by home-bin-env.ts / tool-cache-env.ts living there for exactly this reason ŌĆö the Bash tool is a non-interactive shell that gets PATH only from this literal, no rc sourced). Putting hints in both pod-spec + open-session would duplicate + risk drift; putting them in the runner covers BOTH backends with one edit and matches the existing buildHomeBinEnv/buildToolCacheEnv pattern. SPREAD FIRST (before anthropicEnv) so a genuinely-forwarded TERM/COLUMNS (if the host ever has a TTY) overrides the default ŌĆö defaults are a floor, not a clamp. | (a) set in sandbox-subprocess + sandbox-k8s env (rejected: two edits, drift risk, and those envs feed the RUNNER process not the SDK Bash child directly ŌĆö the runner rebuilds the SDK env from an allowlist, so a TERM set on the runner only reaches the Bash child if it's in ENV_ALLOWLIST AND set, which is the current gap); (b) add FORCE_COLOR/CI to proxy-startup ENV_ALLOWLIST + set them on the sandbox env (rejected: same two-place + allowlist-coupling problem; the runner env literal is the clean single seam) |

## 2026-05-25 ŌĆö TASK-24: Host OOMKill mid-turn silently loses the turn

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-25 | **Root cause (3 cascade points):** (1) the runner's IPC client (`ipc-client.ts`) retries transient errnos (incl ECONNREFUSED) only `maxRetries=5` with 100ŌåÆ30s-cap backoff = ~3.1s total, far shorter than a host OOMKill+pod-reschedule+boot. (2) After the budget exhausts, `commitNotifyWithResync` catches the throw ŌåÆ `kept` ŌåÆ turn never committed ŌåÆ `conversations:get` = 0 turns. (3) The NEXT `inbox.next()` (`session.next-message` long-poll) also throws the terminal `HostUnavailableError` ŌåÆ propagates to `userMessages()` ŌåÆ out of SDK `query()` ŌåÆ top-level catch ŌåÆ `exitCode=1` ŌåÆ `terminated`. Both the logged "commit-notify failed" AND the exit-1 are the same too-short retry budget. | The report attributed it to commit-notify alone, but the exit-1 is the inbox poll. Fixing only commit-notify would still crash the runner on the next poll. | ŌĆö |
| 2026-05-25 | **#1 commit-notify resilience: lengthen the IPC client's transient-error retry budget to ~2min (TASK clarification: 2min max), retry/backoff (NOT buffer-and-replay).** Add a per-call `maxElapsedMs` deadline to `ipc-client.ts withRetry` so transient/5xx retries keep going (backoff capped at 30s) until ~120s elapsed, then throw. This single change fixes BOTH the commit-notify drop AND the inbox-poll runner crash, because both go through the same client retry loop. A host OOMKill+restart on kind completes well within 2min, so the turn commits and the poll reconnects ŌĆö runner survives, turn persists. | retry/backoff chosen over buffer-and-replay: the IPC client already has a retry loop; adding a wall-clock deadline is a ~10-line surgical change vs. a whole disk-spool buffer subsystem. Buffer-and-replay would also need idempotency on the host commit-notify (it has it via parentVersion, but spooling adds complexity for no UX gain ŌĆö the user is already waiting on the turn). The 2min bound caps how long a genuinely-dead host hangs the user. | buffer-and-replay (rejected: heavier, no UX win); raise only maxRetries count (rejected: count is a poor proxy for wall-clock; a wall-clock deadline is the right knob for "survive a restart"). |
| 2026-05-25 | **#2 recovery UX: auto-retry the whole turn + show a "session interrupted, retrying" message.** TASK clarification mandates auto-retry (vs FAULTA-5's deliberate manual-retry-only stance). This case differs from FAULTA-5's: here the turn produced **0 committed turns** (nothing persisted, no partial replay hazard) ŌĆö so auto-retrying the whole turn is loss-free and duplicate-free (the server-side history is empty for this turn; `session:terminate` already cleared `active_session_id` so the retry routes to a fresh sandbox). Implement in channel-web transport/runtime: on the CONNECTION_LOST / sandbox-terminated path, auto-invoke `regenerate()` ONCE with an interim "Session interrupted ŌĆö retryingŌĆ”" status, falling back to the manual-retry banner if the auto-retry also fails. | FAULTA-5's manual-only stance was about mid-stream connection-lost where the server turn was LIVE (duplicate side-effect risk). TASK-24's OOMKill case = turn fully lost, host restarted, fresh sandbox on retry ŌåÆ safe to auto-retry. Bounded to ONE auto-retry so a persistently-dead host doesn't loop forever; then manual banner. | keep manual-only (rejected: TASK clarification explicitly wants auto-retry + message); unbounded auto-retry (rejected: infinite loop on a hard-down host). |
| 2026-05-25 | **#3a memory: raise host limit 512MiŌåÆ2048Mi in kind-dev-values.yaml** (TASK clarification). Bump request 128MiŌåÆ256Mi to keep the request/limit ratio sane for the scheduler. | Per TASK clarification. 512Mi was tipped over by one heavy proxy-MITM turn atop the orchestrator. | ŌĆö |
| 2026-05-25 | **#3b proxy buffering caps: (a) cap the plain-HTTP request-body buffer in `handleHTTPRequest` (currently UNBOUNDED `Buffer.concat`) at 16 MiB ŌåÆ 413; (b) add write-backpressure on both MITM data pumps (`clientTls.write`/`targetTls.write` ignore the bool return ŌåÆ unbounded socket buffer on a slow consumer) by pausing the source socket when write() returns false and resuming on 'drain'.** Builder's-recommendation cap = 16 MiB request body (generous for any legit upload; a multi-GB upload OOMs the 512Mi/2048Mi host otherwise). | The report's case is an HTTPS-MITM *download* (response) ŌĆö the response side already streams chunk-by-chunk but WITHOUT honoring write backpressure, so a slow runner-pod consumer lets chunks pile in the host's socket buffers unbounded. Backpressure is the real per-request buffering cap for the MITM download path. The plain-HTTP request-body concat is a separate unbounded vector worth capping in the same PR. | cap response body size (rejected: a legit large download should succeed, just not OOM ŌĆö backpressure bounds memory without capping size); leave plain-HTTP unbounded (rejected: it's a live OOM vector). |

- `2026-05-26` (TASK-33) | Followed the locked impl plan `docs/plans/2026-05-26-jit-per-user-skill-attachment-orchestrator-union-impl.md` verbatim after verifying every code anchor against worktree HEAD (zero drift). | The card says "decisions locked (design ┬¦4 + Appendix); implementation-only" and the plan ships real code for every step. Verifying anchors first (per receiving-code-review discipline) confirmed the orchestrator's exact 1045-1046 anchor, the `buildSkillsHooks`/`buildProxyHooks` test helpers, `TEST_AGENT.id='test-agent'`/userId='test-user', and the canary capture harness ŌĆö so no re-derivation needed. | Alt: re-brainstorm scope ŌĆö rejected, card is implementation-only and the plan's Self-Review already covers spec/placeholder/type/stale-anchor checks.
- `2026-05-26` (TASK-33) | Per-user attachment ownership lives in `@ax/skills` (new `skills_v1_user_attachments` table + `skills:attach-for-user`/`skills:list-user-attachments` hooks), NOT `@ax/agents`. `agent_id` stored as an opaque scoping key (no FK to agents_v1_agents, no agents:resolve validation). | Design ┬¦11.2 names the hooks `skills:*`; @ax/skills already owns the user's private skill world (`skills_v1_user_skills`); agent-global attachments remain @ax/agents' admin-managed config ŌĆö genuinely separate concept (admin-global vs self-serve), so one source of truth per concept (invariant #4). Capabilities minimized: a dangling attachment to a deleted agent simply never resolves at session open. | Alt: store in @ax/agents next to skill_attachments ŌĆö rejected (mixes admin-global with self-serve, and hooks are named skills:*).
- `2026-05-26` (TASK-33) | Three-source union precedence implemented by redefining the orchestrator's single `attachments` list as `[...userAttachments, ...agentGlobal.filter(id not in userAttachedIds)]` ŌĆö per-user FIRST, agent-global same-id copies dropped. | The whole downstream chain (resolve(ownerUserId), the per-attachment credential/host merge loop, defaults filter via explicitIds, installedSkills build) already keys off that one `attachments` list, so per-user > agent-global > default + per-user-binding-wins fall out with no other orchestrator change. Content override (user-scoped skill content wins) is already handled by skills:resolve(ownerUserId) mergeUserWins. | Alt: a separate merge pass post-resolve ŌĆö rejected, more code + duplicates the existing slot-owner logic.

- `2026-05-26` (TASK-33) | Accepted Codex P1: `skills:list-user-attachments` read failure now FAILS CLOSED (terminate turn, reason `user-attachments-failed`) instead of fail-open (`[]`). | The read is credential-bearing ŌĆö it decides which credential refs reach `proxy:open-session` and the per-user > agent-global precedence. Fail-open could silently spawn a session with the admin's agent-global ref for a slot the user activated a per-user override on (a credential the user never chose). This matches the `skills:resolve` fail-closed precedent in the SAME orchestrator function; the impl plan's original "throws non-fatal ŌåÆ []" copied the wrong sibling (`skills:list-defaults`, which is fail-open ONLY because defaults are instruction-only and can't carry credentials). Added a regression test (orchestrator.test.ts: thrown list-user-attachments ŌåÆ terminated + proxy never opened). | Alt: keep fail-open per the plan ŌĆö rejected, it's a credential-confusion bug; availability cost of fail-closed is acceptable (a per-user read fault would likely fail the subsequent skills:resolve too).

- `2026-05-26` (TASK-33) | REJECTED Codex P2 ("don't register skills:attach-for-user before its caller ŌĆö half-wired"). | The half-wired write window is an EXPLICIT, design-locked decision (impl plan "Half-wired window" + design ┬¦11): the write hook is registered + unit-tested + CANARY-REACHABLE (the canary's per-user cases call skills:attach-for-user through the real plugin stack to create the rows the orchestrator's read path then unions ŌĆö so it's load-bearing for THIS PR's own acceptance test, the opposite of dead infra), the READ path it feeds is fully wired into the orchestrator (returns [] today ŌåÆ byte-unchanged behavior), and the closing card (TASK-36, the post-approval host-side caller) is named. Invariant #3's "reachable from the canary acceptance test" clause is satisfied. The PR body states "half-wired window OPEN (write path), CLOSES in TASK-36". Splitting the write hook out would break the canary. Codex's accompanying tsc exit-2/127 lines are its own verification-shell env issue (my `pnpm typecheck` passed clean), not code findings. | Alt: defer the write hook to TASK-36 ŌĆö rejected, it would leave the read path + canary without a way to create rows, and contradicts the locked plan.

## 2026-05-26 ŌĆö TASK-44: persist grant is best-effort (don't 500 a successful live grant)

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| Decision | In `routes-allow-host.ts`, wrap the `host-grants:grant` persist call in try/catch (log `host_grant_persist_failed` + swallow). A persist failure returns `{ added }` 200, not 500. |
| Rationale | The LIVE `proxy:add-host` widen already succeeded before the persist attempt, so the host works for the current session. A persist-only failure (grant-limit at the 256 cap, or a transient DB blip) shouldn't surface as a request error ŌĆö it would confuse the user (the host IS live) and the only loss is durability, which the user recovers by re-hitting the wall next fresh spawn. Same fail-direction as the orchestrator's fail-open load: a failure yields fewer persisted hosts, never more, so it can't widen egress. Found in the `/code-review --effort high` substitute pass (Codex was usage-limited this session). |
| Alternatives | (a) Let it propagate ŌåÆ 500 on cap/DB-blip even though the live grant worked (rejected: bad UX, dishonest about the live state). (b) Map `grant-limit` ŌåÆ a specific 4xx (rejected: still fails a successful live grant; the persist is genuinely secondary). |

| 2026-05-26 | catalog decision route uses zod `.strip()` not `.strict()` for the decision body | `.strict()` 400s on extra fields; an attacker appending a spoofed `decidedByUserId` would get a revealing 400. `.strip()` silently drops it ŌĆö the route always uses `actor.id`. Matches the plan's "ignores any client-supplied decider" test (admit must still succeed with the extra field present). | `.strict()` ŌĆö fails the ignore-decider test. |

| 2026-05-26 | TASK-45 codex review found 2 P2s ŌĆö fixed both (test-first) | (1) Admit button enabled before bundle diff loaded / despite load error ŌåÆ admin could promote un-reviewed untrusted bytes, bypassing the review surface. Fixed: split error into loadError (blocks Admit) vs decideError (doesn't); canAdmit requires entries loaded + no loadError. (2) diffLines LCS allocates (m+1)*(n+1) cells ŌåÆ a valid 256KiB file with tens of thousands of lines OOMs the admin tab on opening the dialog. Fixed: cap at DIFF_LCS_MAX_LINES=2000, degrade to faithful whole-file replace (remove-all+add-all) above it ŌĆö bounded O(m+n), no bytes dropped. Both have regression tests. | Rejected nothing ŌĆö both findings were valid security-relevant correctness issues. |

| 2026-05-26 | TASK-45 codex round 2 found a P1 ŌĆö fixed (test-first) | A submitted bundle file with path `__proto__`/`constructor`/`prototype` is VALID (passes server PATH_RE: lowercase+underscores, not reserved) and catalog:admit promotes it verbatim. On a plain `{}` map, `map['__proto__']=...` is the prototype setter, not an own key, so Object.keys in compareBundles omitted it from the review diff ŌåÆ admitted-but-never-shown, a review-gate bypass. Fixed: build the submitted + current path maps with `Object.create(null)` in BundleReviewDialog. Regression tests at both compareBundles and dialog level. | Rejected nothing ŌĆö valid review-gate bypass. |

| 2026-05-26 | TASK-45 codex round 3 found a P2 ŌĆö the plan's Task 3 premise was WRONG; fixed by OMITTING files | The plan claimed skills:upsert wipes files when `files` is omitted. FALSE: store.upsert (store.ts:105) only rewrites the bundle tree when `input.files !== undefined`; absent = leave unchanged (plugin.ts:372-375 confirms). So my Task 2/3 re-read+re-send of existingFiles was redundant AND harmful: (a) stale-read could clobber a concurrent file change, (b) PUT name-mismatch (caught only AFTER the upsert) copied the path id's files onto the wrong parsed id before the 400. Fix: omit `files` entirely in both PUT update and PATCH setDefaultAttached ŌĆö the store preserves them. Removed the redundant skills:get in PUT. Added a name-mismatch regression test (400 + no id created). LESSON: verify plan premises about store/hook semantics against the actual code before building on them. | Rejected nothing ŌĆö the finding was correct and exposed a wrong plan premise. |

| 2026-05-26 | TASK-45 codex round 4: fixed P3 (route unwind), accepted P2 (PATCH stale-text race) as documented residual + follow-up | P3: registerCatalogRoutes threw before returning unregisters, leaking an already-live route on partial-init failure. Fixed: wrap the loop in try/catch that unwinds accumulated unregisters before rethrowing (+ unit test with a fake bus failing on the 2nd call). NOTE: the sibling registerAdminSkillsRoutes/registerSettingsSkillsRoutes share this latent gap ŌĆö aligning them is a deferred follow-up (not regressing passing code in this card). P2: PATCH setDefaultAttached read-then-writes manifest/body because the store has only full `upsert` (no flag-only setter, no optimistic version) ŌĆö same race class already documented+accepted in plugin.ts:407 (credential purge). Documented as a KNOWN LIMITATION; proper fix needs a new store-level atomic partial-update primitive = out of scope for this UI card ŌåÆ follow-up. | Rejected inventing a half-baked optimistic check (could regress); rejected refactoring the two passing sibling registrars in this card. |

| 2026-05-26 | TASK-45 codex round 5: fixed P2 (unbounded diff DOM nodes) | diffLines bounds the LCS *computation*, but BundleDiffView still rendered one <div> per physical line; a valid 256KiB mostly-newline file = ~hundreds of thousands of DOM nodes ŌåÆ freezes the review dialog on an untrusted share. Fixed: cap rendered rows at MAX_RENDERED_DIFF_LINES=500 in FileBody, show the first N + a "ŌĆ” N more lines not shown inline (file too large to diff in full)" notice. ## 2026-05-26 ŌĆö TASK-53: JIT broker cold-start (fire catalog:submit on miss, design ┬¦13)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-26 | TASK-53 scope = broker-side TRIGGER only. Fire a `catalog:submit` `kind:'cold-start'` from BOTH broker miss paths: `request_capability` ŌåÆ `not-found` AND `search_catalog` ŌåÆ empty `skills:[]`. The queue/store/hook already exist (TASK-41). No new store/hook/migration. | The card title says "search/request miss" and design ┬¦13 says "broker finds no catalog hit ŌåÆ files an admit-request (deduped)". Both broker tools are the no-hit boundary. catalog:submit's cold-start kind takes exactly `{skillId, requestedByUserId, description}` ŌĆö a perfect fit. Dedup is store-side (one pending per skillId) so repeated misses collapse, no queue spam. | (a) fire only on request_capability not-found (rejected ŌĆö card says search too; an exploratory search that finds nothing IS the strongest "the catalog lacks X" signal and is where the model lands first); (b) build a new "wishlist" hook (rejected ŌĆö TASK-41 already shipped catalog:submit cold-start for exactly this; would be a duplicate source of truth, I4). |
| 2026-05-26 | `catalog:submit` is an `optionalCall` on the broker manifest (hasService-guarded + best-effort try/catch), NOT a hard `calls` dep. A failed/absent submit NEVER changes the tool's return (`not-found` / empty stays) and never throws out of the tool. | Same established broker posture as `credentials:list` (decision 2026-05-26): the broker's core search/request must boot + work on a catalog-less/queue-less preset. The cold-start log is a side-effect, not the tool's contract. Capabilities minimized (I5): broker only gains the ability to FILE a request, never to admit one. | Hard `calls` dep (rejected ŌĆö breaks credential/queue-less presets' boot ordering, and a transient submit failure would fail an otherwise-correct not-found). |
| 2026-05-26 | UNTRUSTED INPUT (I5): for `request_capability` the cold-start `skillId` is the model's already-`SKILL_ID_RE`-validated id (re-validated at the top of the tool); description is a host-templated constant (`A user requested the '<id>' capabilityŌĆ”`) ŌĆö NO free model text. For `search_catalog` the untrusted `intent` free-text becomes the request `description` verbatim (capped to a sane length), and the dedup `skillId` slug is DERIVED locally by sanitizing intent to `^[a-z0-9][a-z0-9-]{0,63}$` (lowercase, non-alnumŌåÆ`-`, collapse/trim dashes, fallback `capability`) ŌĆö the broker re-validates the slug against SKILL_ID_RE before submit. The description is stored as a plain text column the admin triages; it is NEVER parsed as a manifest and a cold-start request is explicitly NON-promotable (`cold-start-not-promotable`, verified in skills plugin.test) ŌĆö so injected text can't forge an admitted catalog skill. | Invariant #5: untrusted at every hop. The slug is a dedup key, not code; the description is data, not a manifest. The "request, not a skill" boundary is enforced by TASK-41's admit path rejecting cold-start promotion. requestedByUserId always = toolCtx.userId (host-auth), never model input. | (a) import memory-strata `slugify` (rejected ŌĆö cross-plugin import, I2); (b) use raw intent as skillId (rejected ŌĆö fails SKILL_ID_RE, no dedup, unbounded length). |

## 2026-05-26 ŌĆö TASK-55: disable agent-SDK telemetry egress (datadog) in the runner

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-26 | TASK-55: disable the SDK's phone-home (datadog telemetry) in the runner via the `query({options:{env}})` literal, NOT a `datadoghq.com` allowlist entry (path (a)) | Product decision pre-resolved (we don't want the agent phoning home). Verified the mechanism from the pinned SDK 0.2.119: the vendored `claude` CLI binary POSTs to `https://http-intake.logs.us5.datadoghq.com/api/v2/logs` (fn `Vn8`/`kn8`=trackDatadogEvent, gated by `initializeDatadog` `LfK`). In the binary `LfK` bails (`NB$=!1`) when `rU()` is true; `rU()=BEDROCK||VERTEX||FOUNDRY||dT8()` and `dT8()=ha6()!=="default"`. `ha6()` (== bridge.mjs `Uf()`) returns `"essential-traffic"` for `CLAUDE_CODE_DISABLE_NONESSENTIAL_TRAFFIC`, `"no-telemetry"` for `DISABLE_TELEMETRY`/`DO_NOT_TRACK`. So ANY of those three flags makes `rU()` true and skips datadog init entirely. | (b) allowlist datadoghq.com ŌĆö rejected: the task explicitly says zero telemetry traffic should exist, an allowlist would still let the agent phone home. |
| 2026-05-26 | TASK-55: set THREE flags ŌĆö `CLAUDE_CODE_DISABLE_NONESSENTIAL_TRAFFIC=1` (umbrella, primary), `DISABLE_TELEMETRY=1`, `DISABLE_ERROR_REPORTING=1` ŌĆö in a new `buildTelemetryEnv()` helper, spread AFTER `...proxyStartup.anthropicEnv` in main.ts | Grounded in Anthropic's own docs (code.claude.com): the devcontainer.json example uses `CLAUDE_CODE_DISABLE_NONESSENTIAL_TRAFFIC:"1"`; data-usage page says it "opts out of all non-essential traffic". `DISABLE_TELEMETRY` + `DISABLE_ERROR_REPORTING` are the per-channel kill switches (defense-in-depth + readable intent). Spread AFTER anthropicEnv so a (currently impossible ŌĆö none are in proxy-startup ENV_ALLOWLIST) host-forwarded value can't override; these are non-negotiable security floors, unlike tty-hints which are intentionally overridable. | Single flag only ŌĆö works, but three flags document intent per-channel and survive a future SDK that splits the gate. Also setting DISABLE_AUTOUPDATER/DISABLE_UPDATES ŌĆö rejected: out of scope (not telemetry; the sandbox CLI is pinned/immutable and never self-updates). |

| 2026-05-26 | TASK-61: fix the BundleReviewDialog "expected 404" console error SERVER-SIDE ŌĆö add an opt-in `?missingOk=1` query param to `GET /admin/skills/:id` that returns `200 {skill:null}` (instead of 404) for a missing skill, and have `getSkillOrNull` request that param. | The browser auto-logs EVERY 4xx/5xx network request to the console regardless of how `fetch` handles the resolved Response ŌĆö JS cannot intercept/silence a 404 that already happened. So you can't "swallow" it on the client; you must avoid PROVOKING it. The diff only needs "is there a current catalog version?" ŌĆö turning that probe into a clean 200 removes the console noise. Opt-in param keeps strict `getSkill`/`GET` behavior (genuine 404) unchanged. | (a) Client `console.error` mute ŌĆö impossible (browser logs it before JS sees it). (b) Probe via `listSkills()` (always 200) then conditionally `getSkill` ŌĆö two round-trips + still 404s for a brand-new id whose summary isn't in the list.
