The orchestrator already maps `unionedSkills` ŌåÆ `installedSkillsForSandbox`; folding builtins into `unionedSkills` (deduped vs explicit+default) reuses the whole materialize path with zero downstream consumer changes. | (a) seeded default-attached row ŌĆö rejected: a real store row admins could edit/delete + re-seed/version handling; (b) system-prompt note only ŌĆö rejected: no progressive disclosure, not a discoverable skill, doesn't match "create a SKILL.md". |
| 2026-05-27 | Flip the chart default `skills.allowUserInstalled` **falseŌåÆtrue** (open mode ON by default everywhere); keep the plugin (`createSkillBrokerPlugin ?? false`) + preset env-gate intact so a deployment opts out with `skills.allowUserInstalled: false`. | User product decision. The sandbox-escape backstop is unchanged: agents PROPOSE capabilities, the human approval card GRANTS them; frontmatter capabilities are still stripped (I-P1-2); `mcpServers` stays unreachable from authoring. So the default-on widening is "agents may propose by default", not "agents may self-grant". | keep default off (opt-in per deploy) ŌĆö rejected by the user in favor of out-of-the-box authoring. |
| 2026-05-27 | Extend the authoring grant path with a **`packages` (npm/pypi) dimension**: `install_authored_skill` gains a `packages` arg (re-validated by `PKG_RE` allowing scoped npm `@scope/pkg`), the agents promote passes it through (was hardcoded `{npm:[],pypi:[]}`), `buildSkillManifestYaml` now serializes packages (it silently dropped them ŌĆö latent bug), and the approval card shows a fixed registry line. `mcpServers` stays hardcoded-empty (agent-authored MCP deferred, admin-only). | Found during design review: a package-using authored skill (npx/uvx/pip) had NO way to get its public registry allowlisted ŌåÆ silent egress-wall failure. Fix keeps the rule "frontmatter never grants; install args (human-approved) do". Package names only drive a fixed public-registry allowlist (orchestrator checks `.length`); names are never interpolated into shell/path and never rendered in the card DOM (card shows fixed `registry.npmjs.org`/`pypi.org` text). | (a) allow packages-only in frontmatter (surgical strip) ŌĆö rejected: splits the rule + lets the agent self-grant registry egress with no card; (b) tell the agent to pass registry hosts as `hosts` ŌĆö rejected: leaky (pypi needs pypi.org AND files.pythonhosted.org); (c) leave unsupported ŌĆö rejected: the Linear-style examples work but anything needing npx/pip wouldn't. |
| 2026-05-27 | The SKILL.md documents the **stricter** skill-id regex `^[a-z][a-z0-9-]{0,63}$` (the runner materialize gate, `agent-claude-sdk-runner/src/installed-skills.ts:25`), NOT the looser tool gate `^[a-z0-9][a-z0-9._-]{0,127}$` (`skill-broker .../install-authored-skill.ts:10`). | The two gates disagree: an id passing the tool but failing the runner installs + gets approved, then SILENTLY fails to materialize. Teaching the strict form prevents agents authoring doomed ids. The underlying gate MISMATCH is a pre-existing latent silent-failure bug this feature makes far more reachable ŌĆö logged as a FOLLOW-UP (align the tool's SKILL_ID_RE to the runner's, or reject-at-tool with a friendly error), NOT fixed in this PR (scope). | tighten the tool regex in this PR ŌĆö deferred to keep scope focused; documented + flagged instead. |
| 2026-05-27 | Channel-web carries `packages?` as OPTIONAL across the three SSE card re-declarations (server/types, transport SseFrame, permission-card-store) even though the broker producer fires it as required. | SSE is a serialization/trust boundary ŌĆö be liberal in what you accept (a payload predating the field, or a non-skill card, must still parse). The `kind:'host'` card branch correctly reconstructs without packages. The render guards on presence. | make consumer types required to match the producer ŌĆö rejected: brittle across the wire boundary. |
| 2026-05-28 | BUG-W3 (`workspace.materialize failed: response body too large`): fix by streaming the materialize bundle as a raw `application/octet-stream` HTTP response (runner drains it to a temp file, no in-memory base64/JSON round-trip, disk-bounded cap `MAX_BINARY_RESPONSE_BYTES`), NOT by shrinking the bundle. Touches: ipc-protocol (materialize response is now binary, request stays JSON), ipc-core (`HandlerBinary` result variant + `writeBinaryOk` + dispatcher branch + handler base64-decodes the hook output to a Buffer), ipc-client (`callBinary` drain-to-file, materialize off the JSON RESPONSE_SCHEMAS table), agent-claude-sdk-runner (`materializeWorkspace({root, bundlePath})` clones from the file; main.ts call site). The `workspace:export-baseline-bundle` HOOK keeps its base64 contract (used by commit-notify resync) ŌĆö decode happens only at the materialize wire edge. | Removes the 33% base64 tax (which is literally what pushed `ws-3f2c7b71`'s ~3 MiB bundle over the 4 MiB base64 wire cap) AND the in-memory cap wall, while preserving the baseline-OID contract byte-for-byte (same bundle bytes). The runner already temp-files the bundle before cloning, so streaming-to-disk is a natural fit and is memory-friendly for large bundles. | (1) Squash/re-root history to bound growth ŌĆö REJECTED for this fix (deferred as a follow-up): the materialized baseline OID is threaded as the first commit-notify `parentVersion` (main.ts:425) and MUST resolve in the host's git mirror (`exportBaselineBundle({version})`); a squashed OID isn't in the mirror, so bounding growth requires re-rooting the mirror history too ŌĆö a multi-component design change (materialize + commit-notify + mirror force-push + resync + multi-replica), not a bug fix. (3) Raise `MAX_RESPONSE_BYTES` ŌĆö REJECTED as sole fix: keeps base64 + full in-memory buffering on both ends; band-aid only. |
| 2026-05-28 | BUG-W3 implemented INLINE with strict TDD rather than fanning out per-task subagents. | The change is ONE coherent wire-format change across ~7 interdependent files (the schema change won't compile until every call site updates in lockstep) ŌĆö fragmenting it across subagents would leave each subagent's tree non-compiling. Matches the documented inline-fallback precedent (ARCH-6/TASK-32/41) for fully-mapped, tightly-coupled mechanical work. | per-task subagents ŌĆö rejected: the tasks aren't independently testable/compilable in isolation. |
| 2026-05-28 | BUG-W3 Phase-5 review: codex native reviewer + CLI both USAGE-LIMITED (resets 2026-05-31, same rolling quota as TASK-53/55/58/59). Substituted `/code-review high` (multi-agent finder+verify) + manual whole-branch trace. Applied 4 findings, rejected 1. | Documented precedent (meta ARCH-11/FAULTA-3, decisions TASK-59): when codex is usage-limited, don't wait ŌĆö substitute /code-review + manual trace. Findings APPLIED: (F1) raised `IPC_TIMEOUTS_MS['workspace.materialize']` 30sŌåÆ120s ŌĆö 30s was the new binding ceiling for streaming a large bundle, would relocate the BUG-W3 boot crash to a timeout; (F2) ws write-error (ENOSPC/EROFS) now non-retryable ŌĆö deterministic disk failure shouldn't re-stream for the 2-min window; (F3) Content-Length-vs-bytesWritten truncation guard ŌåÆ retryable (defensive; common truncation already surfaces as a retryable res 'error'); (F4) added `callBinary` to 5 test `IpcClient` literals (vitest-tolerates/tsc-rejects latent trap ŌĆö runner tsconfig excludes __tests__ so not a CI break, but type-incorrect). | (F5) restore `RESPONSE_SCHEMAS` to a full `Record<IpcActionName,...>` for compile-time exhaustiveness ŌĆö REJECTED: materialize legitimately has no JSON response schema (it's binary), so `Partial` is the honest type; the `schema===undefined` runtime guard throws loudly for any future action that forgets its entry. |
| 2026-05-28 | BUG-W3 codex re-review (quota recovered) found ONE P2 ŌĆö APPLIED: raised both IPC listeners' `IDLE_TIMEOUT_MS` 60sŌåÆ130s (`packages/ipc-http/src/listener.ts`, `packages/ipc-server/src/listener.ts`). | The earlier F1 fix raised the materialize CLIENT per-attempt timeout 30sŌåÆ120s, but the host's `server.setTimeout(IDLE_TIMEOUT_MS=60_000)` was left at 60s with no `'timeout'` listener (Node destroys the idle socket). Before the first response byte the materialize socket is IDLE (request received, host still building the bundle via `git bundle create` on a huge aged repo); a 60s idle timeout would reset it mid-build ŌåÆ ECONNRESET ŌåÆ retryable ŌåÆ rebuild ŌåÆ loop ŌåÆ boot crash, relocating the very BUG-W3 crash. 130s sits just above the 120s client budget so the CLIENT times out first (clean/handled) instead of the server resetting. Server-wide bump is safe: no per-action server timeout exists, the only long-lived actions are materialize (120s) + the 30s long-poll, and a wedged internal IPC socket lingering 130s vs 60s is acceptable (trusted hostŌåörunner channel). No test pinned the 60s value. | per-route socket timeout (`req.socket.setTimeout` in the dispatcher) ŌĆö rejected: more surface for a constant bump that's safe server-wide; host writing an early keepalive byte to reset the timer ŌĆö rejected: hacky. |
| 2026-05-28 | commit-notify re-sync "response body too large" (SAME bug class as BUG-W3, but on the commit-notify re-sync path instead of materialize): fix by streaming the baseline bundle OUT-OF-BAND via a NEW binary IPC action `workspace.export-baseline-bundle` (octet-stream, drained to a temp file via `callBinary`/`requestOnceBinaryToFile`), NOT inline in the commit-notify JSON response. Host commit-notify now returns only `{accepted:false, actualParent, reason}` at BOTH re-sync sites (export-baseline catch + apply-bundle catch); `resyncEnvelopeFromCause` trimmed to `actualParent`-only. Runner `commitNotifyWithResync` binary-fetches the bundle for `actualParent` then passes the FILE PATH to `resyncBaselineAndReplay` (signature changed `baselineBundleBytes:string` ŌåÆ `bundlePath:string`, file-owned/deleted by the callee, mirrors `materializeWorkspace`). `baselineBundleBytes` REMOVED from `WorkspaceCommitNotifyResponse`; new `WorkspaceExportBaselineBundleRequestSchema{version:string.min(1)}` + 120s timeout; `callBinary` Action union widened to the two binary actions. New host handler reuses the existing `workspace:export-baseline-bundle` SERVICE hook (no new hook, no backend import). | The re-sync envelope's `baselineBundleBytes` (base64 git bundle, ~MiB on aged workspaces) was the ONLY uncapped-growth field still on the JSON wire after BUG-W3 migrated materialize; on `ws-3f2c7b71` (~143 files, hundreds of commits) the base64 blew the runner's 4 MiB `MAX_RESPONSE_BYTES` ŌåÆ `response body too large` ŌåÆ turn never synced ŌåÆ 120s `agent:invoke` timeout ŌåÆ terminate ŌåÆ dying pod's late commit-notify hits terminated session ŌåÆ `unknown token` ŌåÆ infinite re-ask loop after a skill approval. actions.ts:240 even commented materialize "blew that cap" ŌĆö identical hazard left on commit-notify. Reuses BUG-W3's proven binary infra exactly. | (b) raise `MAX_RESPONSE_BYTES` ŌĆö REJECTED: band-aid, keeps base64+full-buffer on both ends, only defers the cap. (c) call `workspace.materialize` with `actualParent` to reuse THAT binary action ŌĆö REJECTED: materialize's request is `.strict({})` (no version param) and its semantics are "current HEAD / session-start clone"; overloading it for an arbitrary version muddies the contract. A dedicated sibling action keeps each binary action single-purpose and its schema honest. (d) host probes export-baseline-bundle for a FRESHER actualParent before replying (old apply-bundle-catch behavior) ŌĆö REJECTED: pointless now that the host doesn't inline bytes; if the head advanced again the runner's own binary fetch 500s and it re-materializes. |
| 2026-05-28 | commit-notify re-sync P1 (codex whole-branch review of fdd9332d): a FAILED `workspace.export-baseline-bundle` binary fetch on the re-sync path is NOT terminal `'kept'` ŌĆö it means "the head moved AGAIN" (a third writer advanced past `actualParent` between commit-notify returning it and the runner fetching its bundle ŌåÆ backend `parent-mismatch` ŌåÆ host 500 ŌåÆ `callBinary` rejects). Fix: split `commitNotifyWithResync`'s single try-catch into TWO ŌĆö a FETCH catch that `continue`s the bounded loop (same `parentVersion`, same original `bundle`; `attempt` already incremented so a writer storm still terminates at `MAX_RESYNC_ATTEMPTS` ŌåÆ rollback), and a RESYNC catch (the git rebase/replay) that stays terminal `'kept'` as before. The host handler is UNCHANGED (sanitized 500 on parent-mismatch is correct; retry logic lives runner-side). `callBinary` already unlinks its own temp file on any failure (ipc-client.ts:864-870) so no per-retry temp leak. | The prior entry's rejection-(d) reasoning ("if the head advanced again the runner's own binary fetch 500s and it re-materializes") was WRONG: the 500 surfaced as a `callBinary` reject inside the resync try-catch ŌåÆ terminal `'kept'` ŌåÆ on the final/idle commit path the runner exits with the local bundle never applied to the host ŌåÆ the turn tail is dropped in exactly this double-writer race. The pre-split code's apply-bundle-catch re-fetched at the fresher head; collapsing both sites onto a single fetch removed that recovery. Re-entering the bounded loop restores it without the host probing. | Make the host handler signal "stale, refetch" distinctly instead of a plain 500 ŌĆö NOT needed: the runner already learns the fresher head from the very next commit-notify's `actualParent`, so a plain 500 + loop re-entry is sufficient and keeps the handler's error envelope sanitized (no leak). |

## 2026-05-30 ŌĆö Skills out of git: DB+blob substrate + hybrid materialization gate (design doc)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|------|----------|-----------|--------------|
| 2026-05-30 | Wrote `docs/plans/2026-05-30-skills-out-of-git-design.md` (Proposed, needs sign-off): skills are the LAST data class still in git after the storage-out-of-git doc. Move authoring to `/ephemeral/skill-draft/<id>/`, agent calls `skill_propose(manifest,files,capabilityProposal,origin)` over IPC, host stores ONE skill row + bundle bytes via `blob:put` (kills TASK-40 isomorphic-git bundle-tree backing). Same DB/blob store for catalog/default/attached/authored = one source of truth (I4). Reuses storage doc's `blob:*` + `/ephemeral` substrate. | Finishes what the storage doc started: authored drafts in `/permanent/.ax/draft-skills/` (git) + bundle bytes in a git tree (TASK-40) + DB rows for installed = split-brain across 3 stores for one concept, and the last reason the per-turn git pipeline stays load-bearing. Skill bundles are opaque content-addressed last-write-wins units (like artifacts), they don't want versioning. | (a) keep skills in git (storage-doc ┬¦E status quo) ŌĆö rejected: split-brain + keeps git on the hot path; (b) Postgres-bytea for bundles ŌĆö viable but blob store is cleaner at scale + dedups by sha. |
| 2026-05-30 | **Hybrid materialization gate** (the key product decision, user chose it over pure-lazy or pure-strict): classify at propose time ŌĆö `clean scan Ōł¦ origin=authored Ōł¦ capabilityProposal=Ōłģ` ŌåÆ `active`, materialize FREELY (self-authored instruction scaffolding, no reach to consent to). Anything carrying caps (hosts/credentials/mcp/packages) OR `originŌłł{imported,attached}` ŌåÆ `pending`, APPROVE-BEFORE-MATERIALIZE (no bytes project, no caps inject until human approves the card). Scan hit (any class) ŌåÆ `quarantined` (omit + reason). | Interruption proportional to risk: silent for style-guide skills, explicit card when the agent asks for network+secrets. Moves the cap gate BEFORE first run for the DECLARED case (stricter AND simpler than phase-4's reactive-at-the-wall timing). Imported zero-cap still gated on provenance (supply-chain hop). | pure-lazy (phase-4 as merged: everything materializes, caps approved reactively at the egress wall) ŌĆö rejected: risky bytes run before consent for declared-cap skills; pure-strict (gate everything incl. self-authored instruction text) ŌĆö rejected: nags on zero-risk scaffolding. |
| 2026-05-30 | Re-times phase-4 reactive cap approval ŌåÆ before-materialize, BUT KEEPS: the TASK-35 approval-card SSE frame + `proposalŌł®approved` store (only the trigger changes), the `0555` ephemeral projection + `materializeInstalledSkillsFromEnv` (fed from `blob:get` not git), quarantine-as-host-state (phase-2), session-dirtyŌåÆre-spawn trigger, AND the TASK-37 runtime reactive egress wall as a safety net for UNDECLARED reach (its proper job, independent of skill approval). | The reactive wall is still right for "a skill tries a host it never proposed" ŌĆö that's a runtime egress guard, not skill approval. Only the DECLARED-cap approval moves upfront. Most of phase-3/4 survives substrate-swapped, not thrown away. | ŌĆö |
| 2026-05-30 | **Spawn-time discovery constraint** (stated loudly in the doc): a skill materialized mid-session is INVISIBLE to the running model ŌĆö (1) awareness: skill name+desc are injected into context AT SPAWN, writing to disk mid-turn doesn't edit context already sent; (2) readability: the `0555` dir is projected at spawn, post-spawn writes may not appear in the running sandbox. Adopt **version (a): re-spawn on next turn** ŌĆö host flips row to `active`, user's next message runs a fresh sandbox that projects+enumerates the skill. Reuses pending-turn re-spawn orchestration (2026-05-26-jit-pending-turn...). Build req: harness/system-prompt must TELL the agent it's on the (a) boundary so it words turn-1 right ("ready on your next message") and doesn't try to invoke a just-proposed skill. | No new machinery; honest fit for spawn-time discovery. The approval card IS the pause that hides the re-spawn (user reads card + pastes key > re-spawn cost). UX: gated "make a Linear skill" = askŌåÆapproveŌåÆuse across 2 msgs, feels normal; "create AND use in one breath" degrades to ONE extra "go" message (agent tees it up), never breaks. | version (b) live injection (writable dir + system-reminder context frame) ŌĆö DEFERRED: forks discovery into 2 paths + gives up 0555 immutability; if same-turn ever needed, cleaner form is transparent re-spawn + replay (single discovery path). |
| 2026-05-30 | Canonical UX example throughout = the Linear skill (matches the lazy-redesign doc's own motivating example). Linear needs `api.linear.app`+`LINEAR_API_KEY` ŌåÆ lands in the GATED class ŌåÆ user sees the approval card with named hosts+credential, pastes key (ŌåÆ vault, never bundle/blob/git), skill live next turn. Contrast: "commit-message style skill" = zero-cap self-authored ŌåÆ free, no card, live next turn. | The gate only appears when there's actual reach to consent to ŌĆö that's the whole point of hybrid. Wording points FORWARD ("ready on your next message"), not back ("you may need to restart") which leaks the mechanism + reads like a bug. | ŌĆö |

| 2026-05-30 (TASK-65) | **blob:* slice ships the host-side service hook + @ax/blob-store-fs backend + a canary blob:putŌåÆblob:get round-trip ŌĆö and DEFERS the IPC `blob.*` binary action / `callBinary` request-direction wire to the Part C card that introduces the first runner-side caller (artifact_publish/attachmentsŌåÆblob:put).** Adding a `blob.*` IPC action now with no runner caller would be a half-wired plugin (I3). The hook payload is SHAPED for the eventual wire today: bytes are a raw `Uint8Array` on the bus (NOT base64-in-JSON), the JSON envelope is just `{sha256,size}` ŌĆö so the later card is purely additive (it adds the octet-stream transport + a dispatcher action, no payload reshape). The canary IS the I3 "wire one real caller" proof. | The card's primary acceptance = the storage-agnostic `blob:*` hook reachable via canary round-trip; the "IPC/binary wire plumbing" line describes the eventual sandboxŌåÆhost transport whose only consumer (Part C) is a later card. I3 forbids dead infra. Sandbox-side bytes-up (`blob:put`) needs a NEW request-direction binary channel anyway (today's `callBinary` is response-direction only ŌĆö materialize/export-baseline-bundle drain a body to disk); that belongs with its consumer. | (a) ship a dead `blob.*` IPC action now ŌĆö rejected (I3 half-wired); (b) base64 bytes through the JSON `call()` path ŌĆö rejected (card forbids the 4 MiB JSON frame for bytes + design says callBinary octet-stream). |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-65) | **Did NOT wire @ax/blob-store-fs into `presets/k8s` in this slice.** No host-side consumer of blob:* exists yet (attachments/artifacts/skills onto blob = Part C/D). Wiring it into the preset with no caller is half-wired at the preset level (and the preset's `preset.test.ts` "every calls entry satisfied" derives sets dynamically ŌĆö a registrant with no caller is fine there, but it's still dead weight). The package-local canary (createTestHarnessŌåÆbootstrap) is the reachability proof instead. | Same I3 logic as the IPC defer. The plugin is fully registered + tested + reachable from ITS canary, which the card explicitly accepts ("the canary acceptance test must exercise a blob:putŌåÆblob:get round-trip"). | wire into preset now ŌĆö rejected, no consumer; deferred to the first Part C consumer card. |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-65) | **blob:get re-verifies the digest on read and rejects (throws `corrupt` PluginError) on mismatch ŌĆö never returns tampered bytes.** Lifted from lfs.ts's write-side `computed !== oid` check, applied to the READ side per the card's security requirement ("a corrupted/tampered object is rejected, not returned"). Caller-supplied sha is regex-gated (`^[a-f0-9]{64}$`) before any path is built (no traversal; the key is a content hash, never a caller path). Atomic temp-then-rename on put with a collision-safe `.tmp.<pid>.<uuid>` suffix (lfs.ts's concurrent-PUT-collision fix). | Untrusted-content storage substrate: an attacker who tampers a blob on disk (or a bitflip) must not be able to feed corrupted bytes back as if content-addressed-valid. Re-verify closes that. | trust the path (sha == content by construction) ŌĆö rejected: on-disk tamper / bitrot would silently serve bad bytes under a valid-looking hash. |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-65) | Codex Phase-5 review flagged ONE P1 ("root tsconfig references packages/blob-store-fs but the package isn't in the tracked diff ŌåÆ clean build fails"). REJECTED as a pre-commit artifact: the package files exist on disk + build+test+lint all pass; they were just UNTRACKED because the review ran before the commit (`git ls-files` reports nothing for an unstaged new dir). Resolves entirely on commit ŌĆö verified `git add --dry-run` stages all 11 source files (dist/node_modules/tsbuildinfo correctly gitignored). No code change. | The Codex companion reviews the TRACKED diff; a brand-new package's files are untracked until `git add`, so its own `git ls-files` check spuriously reports them missing. This is a known shape for the FIRST commit of a new package ŌĆö commit, then the diff is whole. | re-run review post-commit to confirm ŌĆö optional; the staging dry-run already proves the files land. |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-66) | **Display event log = `conversation_events` Postgres rows owned by `@ax/conversations`** (not a new plugin): append-only, keyed `(conversation_id, seq)`, columns `event_kind` (`turn`/`permission-card`/`turn-error`) + nullable `role` + `payload` JSONB + `created_at`. Persist via a `conversations:append-event` service hook; turn rows come from @ax/ipc-core's event.turn-end handler (awaited persist-before-ack) + the user turn from @ax/chat-orchestrator at dispatch; host-only display events from NEW `chat:turn-error` + `chat:permission-request` subscribers in @ax/conversations. `conversations:get` reads the log instead of `parseJsonlToTurns`; turn events ŌåÆ existing `Turn[]` (unchanged renderer path), host-only events ŌåÆ a new additive `displayEvents` field on `GetOutput`. | conversations already owns the conversation row + the get read; a separate plugin would split the SoT. Storing turn-end's already-folded `ContentBlock[]` makes redisplay==live by construction for content; host-only events (cards/errors) are absent from the jsonl so they MUST come from the host event stream. | A separate `@ax/display-log` plugin (rejected: splits the conversation SoT, needs its own ACL gate duplicating conversations'); persisting per-`event.stream-chunk` delta (rejected: duplicates the turn-end content, no redisplay benefit). |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-66) | **persist-before-ack (B3): @ax/ipc-core's event.turn-end handler awaits an ISOLATED `conversations:append-event` (a dedicated `persist` slot on the dispatcher EventSpec) BEFORE the 202, then fires the chat:turn-end broadcast fire-and-forget AFTER.** Only the durability-critical append precedes the ack; the broadcast (bump/clear-reqId/titles-LLM/evictor) stays off the ack path so a slow observer can't delay the runner. `conversations:append-event` is an OPTIONAL dispatcher dep (hasService-gated; CLI single-session skips it). A persist throw ŌåÆ 500 + loud `event_persist_failed` (no false ack). | The design's B3 literally requires "persist the turn's frames before the turn-end ack." Isolating the persist from the broadcast avoids coupling the turn-end ack latency to unrelated observers (the title-LLM subscriber). | Awaiting the whole chat:turn-end fire (rejected: title-LLM blocks every ack); persisting in the conversations subscriber (rejected: rides the broadcast, same coupling). |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-66) | **Client live-vs-reload render-path unification is OUT of scope for this card.** Today live render = `transport.ts` folding SSE frames into assistant-ui (+ separate `permission-card-store`/`turn-error` stores); reload = `history-adapter.ts` fetching `Turn[]`. This card switches the reload SOURCE (jsonlŌåÆevent log) but keeps the existing reload renderer; "same renderer path" holds for CONTENT by construction (turn-end blocks = folded stream-chunk terminal state). Host-only card/error events are PERSISTED + RETURNED on `GetOutput.displayEvents` (so the SoT is complete + tested) but the CLIENT does not yet fold them on reload. | The card scope is "ONLY the display SoT (event log + conversations:get switch)". A literal one-fold client rewrite (reload replays persisted card/error frames through the live transport) touches transport.ts + 2 client stores + history-adapter, isn't coverable by the host-side redisplay test the acceptance asks for, and is a distinct unit of work. The host SoT being complete now is what makes that follow-up cheap. | Full client unification in this PR (rejected: scope creep beyond "event log + conversations:get switch", large untested client surface); NOT returning host-only events at all (rejected: acceptance #3 requires redisplay to INCLUDE host-only UI, and the SoT must carry them even if the client folds them later). |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-66, post-review) | **Persist the USER display turn HOST-SIDE in @ax/chat-orchestrator at agent:invoke dispatch ŌĆö NOT via a runner-emitted user `event.turn-end`.** Codex review caught that the display event log was missing user turns (the SDK runner emits `event.turn-end` only for tool/assistant turns; the user prompt lives only in the jsonl). First attempt: emit a `role:'user'` `event.turn-end` from the runner. REJECTED after finding it fires the broadcast `chat:turn-end`, whose channel-web SSE subscriber closes the live stream on `ctx.conversationId` match (NOT reqId) ŌåÆ a user turn-end at turn START sends a premature `{done:true}` and kills the live stream; it also trips one-shot keep-warm + clear-active-req-id. Final: orchestrator calls `conversations:append-event` (kind:'turn', role:'user', blocks = typed text + attachment contentBlocks) once per agent:invoke before the route/spawn decision, off the turn-end path. Gated on `bus.hasService('conversations:append-event')` (same hasService posture as the conversations:* peers; NOT in `manifest.calls`); best-effort. | The orchestrator already holds the user's content + conversationId and is the single host-side dispatch chokepoint; persisting there has zero turn-end side effects. The tool/assistant turns persist via @ax/ipc-core's event.turn-end handler (awaited, isolated, persist-before-ack). Two persist sites, one per audience-of-turn, both host-side. | Runner-emitted user turn-end (rejected: closes the live SSE stream via the conversationId-keyed done-frame subscriber); persisting in channel-web's chat-messages route (rejected: the orchestrator is the canonical dispatch gate that ALL agent:invoke paths ŌĆö warm + fresh ŌĆö funnel through; channel-web would miss non-web callers). |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-66, post-review) | **persist-before-ack moved OUT of the broadcast chat:turn-end subscriber and INTO @ax/ipc-core's event.turn-end handler as an isolated, awaited `conversations:append-event` call.** Codex P2 caught that awaiting the WHOLE chat:turn-end subscriber chain (my first impl) blocks every turn-end ack on @ax/conversation-titles' `llm:call` (it subscribes to chat:turn-end). Fix: the event.turn-end handler does `await bus.call('conversations:append-event', ...)` (ONLY the persist) before firing the fire-and-forget broadcast for the OTHER subscribers (bump/clear-reqId/titles/evictor). `conversations:append-event` is an OPTIONAL dispatcher dep (bus.hasService-gated; CLI single-session skips it). And Codex P2: a persist FAILURE now re-throws ŌåÆ the dispatcher writes 500 instead of a false 202, so a turn that never reached the log isn't acked (B3 no-omission). | Isolating the awaited persist keeps persist-before-ack without coupling the turn-end latency to unrelated observers. The dependency-sync test enforces the new optional dep (string-literal hook name at the bus.call/hasService site so the scanner detects it). | Awaiting the whole chat:turn-end fire (rejected: title-LLM latency on every turn ack); a dedicated new `chat:turn-end-persist` hook (rejected: extra protocol surface for no gain over the optional bus.call). |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-66, re-review) | **Final persist-before-ack shape: a dedicated `persist` slot on the dispatcher EventSpec (awaited before 202) SEPARATE from `fire` (broadcast, fire-and-forget AFTER 202).** Re-review caught that my first split still awaited `fireEventTurnEnd` which itself awaited the chat:turn-end broadcast ŌåÆ titles' LLM still blocked the ack. Fix: `event.turn-end` now has `persist: persistEventTurnEnd` (the isolated conversations:append-event call, awaited) and `fire: fireEventTurnEnd` (just the broadcast, kicked off `void` after the 202). The dispatcher awaits `persist`, writes 202, then `void fire(...)`. A persist throw ŌåÆ 500 + loud `event_persist_failed` log. Guard tests: a slow conversations:append-event holds the 202 (persist-before-ack); a slow chat:turn-end subscriber does NOT (P2a regression). | Only the durability-critical append must precede the ack; everything else (bump/clear-reqId/titles/evictor) is observation. Coupling them was the latency bug. | Awaiting the whole fire (the bug); a 2nd hook (rejected ŌĆö extra surface). |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-66, re-review) | **appendEvent retries on the (conversation_id, seq) unique-violation (SQLSTATE 23505), bounded (8).** Re-review caught that `INSERT ... SELECT COALESCE(MAX(seq),0)+1` is NOT race-safe across two CONCURRENT statements (a permission-card persist racing the turn-end persist for the same conversation) ŌĆö both read the same MAX, one hits the PK. Retry recomputes MAX and re-inserts. Tested with 20 concurrent appends ŌåÆ 20 distinct contiguous seqs, none dropped. (NB: the host-only-event subscribers persist async/independently, so this race is real, not theoretical.) `isUniqueViolation` matches `err.code === '23505'` (pg driver SQLSTATE; storage-internal, never on a hook payload). | A monotonic per-conversation seq with concurrent writers needs either a DB sequence or retry-on-conflict; retry is the smaller change and the contention is tiny. | A Postgres SEQUENCE per conversation (rejected: unbounded sequence objects); an advisory lock (rejected: heavier than retry for rare contention). |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-66, re-review) | **projectDisplayEvents folds by keeping the LAST event per (kind,foldKey) but ORDERS the result by the terminal event's seq** (not Map insertion order). Re-review caught that `Map.set` preserves the original insertion position, so a card resolved later would render in its pending-frame slot, before host events that actually happened between. Fix: track `{event, seq}` per key, then `sort((a,b)=>a.seq-b.seq)`. Tested: card A pending (seq1) ŌåÆ card B (seq2) ŌåÆ A resolved (seq3) ŌćÆ order [B, A-approved]. | Replay must reflect the real timeline; the terminal frame's seq is when the card reached its shown state. | ŌĆö |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-66, re-review #3) | **Accepted-for-greenfield scope calls on 3 re-review findings, with followups filed:** (1) a LEGACY conversation (jsonl turns predating this PR) that gets a NEW turn shows only the new event-log turns on reload (the first event row flips conversations:get off the jsonl fallback). Accepted: ax-next has NO production data (context.md 2026-04-29 invariant); the only affected case is a dev conversation mid-deploy; TASK-67/70 retire the jsonl entirely, mooting it. A merge-the-jsonl-prefix fix risks duplication for a non-existent population. (2) The reactive-wall HOST permission card (kind:host, fired from event.http-egress) has no conversationId on its ctx (it is reqId-matched live), so it does not persist ŌĆö only the skill approval card (conversationId-matched) + turn-errors do. Deferred (followup): needs reqId-to-conversationId resolution in the orchestrator egress path. The primary host-only UI (skill cards, surfaced errors) DOES persist. (3) The runner swallows a turn-end 500 (.catch swallow), so a hard-DB-outage persist failure loses that turn's display row despite the 500. Accepted: the realistic concurrent failure (seq race) is handled by the store retry; a hard outage gets the B3 LOUD alarm (event_persist_failed at error + 500) ŌĆö "install the alarm now, swing the hammer only if it rings" (the design's staged-robustness posture). The user still sees the live reply; only redisplay of that one turn degrades. Making the runner non-swallow risks terminating chats on transient blips. | All three are real but each is mooted by greenfield+TASK-67, a narrow secondary variant, or covered by the loud-alarm posture the design stages. Fixing them fully is disproportionate for this card. | (1) merge jsonl prefix (rejected: duplication risk, no population); (2) persist host card now (deferred: orchestrator egress reqId-to-conv resolution is its own unit); (3) runner non-swallow + retry/queue (deferred: B3 escalation territory). |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-66) | **A literal NUL byte in a TS source file makes git/grep treat it as binary** (grep silently reports nothing / "binary file matches" and hides text matches ŌĆö this bit me repeatedly during the session). It crept into a Map-key template literal and a comment. Fix: escape as the unicode-0000 escape in code; plain space in comments. Detect with `grep -aPn` for the null pattern (the -a forces text mode) or `cat -v` (shows ^@). Scan the whole diff before commit. | A NUL is a fine Map-key separator (no field contains it) but MUST be escaped, never embedded literally, or it breaks every text tool that reads the file. | ŌĆö |

One plugin owns all conversation-scoped state (I4). | row-per-line in a 2nd plugin (extra cross-plugin hop); whole-file blob (O(n^2) re-upload ŌĆö design rejects). |
| 2026-05-30 | New host service hooks `conversations:append-transcript` / `conversations:replace-transcript` / `conversations:get-transcript` (host-internal, ctx-scoped) + matching IPC actions `session.append-transcript` (JSON) / `session.replace-transcript` (callBinaryUpload octet-stream) / `session.get-transcript` (callBinary octet-stream, resume read). | Mirrors TASK-66 `conversations:append-event` posture (host-internal hook fed by an IPC handler). append carries small JSON (lines[] of opaque strings); replace+read carry whole-file bytes ŌåÆ binary channel (TASK-68 callBinaryUpload/callBinary). Mismatch ŌåÆ loud `ctx.logger.error` + metric, NEVER throws/blocks. Install ALARM only; NO derivation escalation (YAGNI). | Card + design B3: structural not hash (hash false-positives on redaction). | 2026-05-30 | Codex finding 1 (FIXED): shipTranscriptDelta's `noop` path left the host transcript STALE when the SDK shrinks/compacts the prefix in-place with no new line ŌĆö the misleading comment claimed it verified the prefix but made no host call. Fix: resync NOW when `fileBuf.length < sentOffset` (the file shrank below what we shipped); extracted `resyncWholeFile` helper. | "never silent staleness" (B3 no-omission spirit). | 2026-05-30 | Codex finding 2 (FIXED): restoreTranscriptForResume threaded `sentOffset=buf.length` but `sentSeq=completeLines` ŌĆö inconsistent if the host ever returned non-`\n`-terminated bytes. Latent today (store emits trailing `\n`), but internally-consistent is correct. | defense in depth on the state-threading invariant. | leave it (latent ŌĆö store always terminates lines). |
| 2026-05-30 | SDK project-dir slug (resume-write path) is `realpath(cwd).replace(/[^a-zA-Z0-9]/g,'-')` truncated to 200 chars + `-${djb2hash}` when longer ŌĆö VERIFIED by grepping the vendored SDK 0.2.119 `sdk.mjs` (`var P0=200`, `kB`/`gE` hash). `encodeProjectSlug` ports it byte-for-byte. `/permanent` (the prod cwd, 10 chars) never hits the cap, but the port removes a latent resume-write-to-wrong-dir bug for long paths. Don't hand-wave the slug ŌĆö grep the binary. | a slug mismatch = silent resume failure (SDK can't find the jsonl). - `2026-05-30` (TASK-86) ŌĆö **Per-skill credential-slot namespacing fixes the skill-slot-collision LOCKOUT (two active authored skills sharing a slot like LINEAR_API_KEY terminated EVERY chat turn).** Chosen approach (a, human-decided in card Clarifications; (b) relevant-only-union rejected): namespace SKILL slots `skill:<id>:<slot>` in the host-side credentials map handed to `proxy:open-session`, keep AGENT/trusted base creds (`agent.requiredCredentials` / Anthropic default) BARE. Two skills' same-named slots ŌåÆ two distinct namespaced keys ŌåÆ two distinct `ax-cred:<hex>` placeholders ŌåÆ no collision. Skill-vs-agent collision is NO LONGER fatal: the trusted bare credential always WINS the flat sandbox env stamp; a skill's namespaced cred still exists in the proxy map for its own egress but can't hijack the trusted env var (old security guarantee preserved as a benign no-op suppression, not a lockout). KEY ARCH FACT making the bare-env requirement satisfiable: proxy substitution is VALUE-based (`registry.ts replaceAll` replaces `ax-cred:<hex>` wherever it appears, regardless of env-var name), so the env-var NAME is just a placeholder vehicle ŌĆö the orchestrator projects the namespaced `envMap` BACK to bare env names (`projectEnvMapToBareNames`, trusted-wins + deterministic skill precedence) before threading into `proxyConfig.envMap` (the flat sandbox env). Skills share ONE flat sandbox env (no per-skill process/env scope), so two skills sharing a bare slot name still collapse to ONE value in the flat env (precedence wins) ŌĆö IRREDUCIBLE; the win is no-lockout + each cred reaching the proxy independently. git-cred wiring (`buildGitCredentialEnv` @ax/sandbox-protocol) must use each skill's OWN placeholder (threaded as optional `credentials[].placeholder` on InstalledSkillSchema, back-compat falls back to `envMap[slot]`) so per-skill git egress stays correct even when the flat-env stamp went to the other skill. Also in scope (card Clarifications): (T4) tuned `CRED_EXFIL` scanner so benign `curl -H "Authorization: Bearer $X_API_KEY"` against an allowed host stops false-tripping `credential-exfiltration`; (T5) scoped the pending cap-skill JIT "ConnectŌĆ”" card to its PROPOSING conversation (in-memory `pendingSkillConversation: Map<skillId,conversationId>` set in `onSkillsProposed`, same single-replica posture as respawnSessions/upfrontCardsByConv) so it stops persisting across unrelated conversations.

- `2026-05-31` (TASK-88) ŌĆö **SSE-open retry extended from TASK-84's fixed ~1.45s (4-attempt) budget to a wall-clock ~30s budget of capped-exponential backoff (250ms doubling, cap 2s) so a cold-respawn 404 auto-recovers ŌĆö no manual Retry click.** Client-only, `packages/channel-web/src/lib/transport.ts` `openSseStream`. Replaced the counted loop with an open-ended `for(;;)` gated on a `Date.now()+SSE_OPEN_TOTAL_BUDGET_MS` deadline (each retry wait clamped to the remaining budget). Decided budget=30s (card said ~20-30s): a cold kind runner pod spawn + per-reqId bind takes ~5-15s, 30s gives margin; bounded so a turn that died before ANY bind still terminates ŌåÆ banner. SAFE per the card's key insight + FAULTA-5 history: the GET only replays a bounded per-reqId buffer (chunk-buffer.ts) and never starts a turn (only POST does), so re-opening it far longer than 1.45s can't duplicate a turn ŌĆö unlike a `regenerate()` re-POST, which FAULTA-5 (decisions 2026-05-25) forbids automating. Retryable set unchanged (404/425/429/5xx + network throw); 401/403/400/413 fail fast on attempt 1 (card: "unchanged"). **Review-fix decision:** the terminal throw now differs by reason ŌĆö a spent budget on a RETRYABLE failure throws `new Error(CONNECTION_LOST)` (the FAULTA-5 sentinel) so the runtime's `onError`ŌåÆ`applyTurnError` shows the user-facing "Connection lost. Retry to continue." banner + manual-retry button (the card's "fall back to the existing CONNECTION_LOST banner"); a fail-fast NON-retryable status keeps its verbatim `chat-flow SSE open failed: <status>` (a real client error is not a connection loss). TASK-84 had thrown the raw status string on ALL terminal exits ŌĆö that pre-existing gap missed the card's acceptance, so I fixed it with a `failFast` flag set only on the non-retryable break. During the wait surface `agentStatusActions.show(PHASE_LABELS['sandbox-starting'])` ("Starting sandboxŌĆ”") set LAZILY (only after the first retryable failure) so the happy-path first-open never flashes it. OUT OF SCOPE (handoff follow-up): harden the server early-bind to be authoritative (retry the bind / 503 the POST) so `active_req_id` is guaranteed before the 202. | Rationale: budget-driven (not attempt-count) is self-documenting and decouples the cold-boot window from the backoff curve; CONNECTION_LOST fallback honors the card acceptance + reuses the established sentinel/wording rather than inventing new copy; lazy status avoids a flash on the common warm-path. | Alternatives: (a) keep an attempt count, just bump it (rejected ŌĆö couples timing to count, harder to reason about a "~30s" budget); (b) throw raw status on budget exhaustion like TASK-84 (rejected ŌĆö misses the card's "surfaces CONNECTION_LOST" acceptance + shows dev-ish copy to users); (c) show CONNECTION_LOST for the 403 fail-fast too (rejected ŌĆö a 403 is a real auth error, not a connection loss; "unchanged" per card); (d) eagerly set "Starting sandboxŌĆ”" before the first open (rejected ŌĆö flashes on every warm turn).

- `2026-05-31` (TASK-90, epic connectors-first-class) ŌĆö **The capability shape now has a NEUTRAL canonical name: `Capabilities` in `@ax/skills-parser` (`packages/skills-parser/src/capabilities.ts`); `SkillCapabilities` is a back-compat `export type` alias of it.** Pure type/export-only refactor, no behavior/hook/table change. Why: per the connectors-first-class design a future connector object references the SAME `allowedHosts`/`credentials`/`mcpServers`/`packages` shape, and CLAUDE.md invariant #2 forbids a cross-plugin import ŌĆö so the shared shape must live under a neutral name in the dependency-free `@ax/skills-parser` (already eslint-allowlisted for both `@ax/skills` and `@ax/agents`). The sub-types (`CapabilitySlot`/`McpServerSpec`/`PackagesSpec`) were ALREADY neutral-named ŌĆö only the top-level interface needed renaming. `index.ts` now re-exports `Capabilities` + `PackagesSpec` (previously unexported) alongside the existing names. Migrated the two INTERNAL `src` consumers (`manifest.ts` `ParsedManifest.capabilities`, `build.ts` input) to the neutral name so `pnpm build` (tsc) is the load-bearing regression guard ŌĆö PROVEN: renaming the export away makes the build go red. External consumers (`@ax/skills`, `@ax/agents`, `@ax/skill-broker`) were left on the `SkillCapabilities` alias (zero churn, alias keeps them compiling). | Rationale: smallest honest diff that satisfies the card + makes the neutral name real and guarded; test files aren't type-checked anywhere in this repo's gate (build excludes `__tests__`, vitest strips types, eslint isn't type-aware) so a type-only test CAN'T be the guard ŌĆö a migrated `src` consumer is. | Alternatives: (a) mass-rewrite every consumer to `Capabilities` (rejected ŌĆö needless churn, the card says "Skills continue to consume the type exactly as before"); (b) add a runtime sentinel value to make the vitest test load-bearing (rejected ŌĆö adds unrequested runtime API, YAGNI); (c) leave both `src` consumers on the alias and rely only on the (unchecked) vitest test (rejected ŌĆö then nothing in the gate guards the neutral export).

- `2026-05-31` (TASK-90, Phase 5 review substitution) ŌĆö The `ax-code-reviewer` subagent / `Task` dispatch tool was NOT available in this orchestrated agent's tool surface (no dispatch tool surfaced via ToolSearch). Fell back to a manual whole-branch (`main...HEAD`) self-review against the six AX invariants + card acceptance. ## 2026-05-31 ŌĆö TASK-91 @ax/connectors plugin design decisions

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-31 | New `@ax/connectors` package mirrors `@ax/conversations` structure (migrations/store/scope/types/plugin/index). | 2026-05-31 | `Connector = { id, name, description, usageNote, keyMode:'personal'|'workspace', visibility:'private'|'shared' } + Capabilities`. `Capabilities` TYPE-imported from `@ax/skills-parser` (the only @ax/* type-only import allowed for connectors per eslint allow-list). Zod schema re-declared LOCALLY (no cross-plugin runtime import; invariant #2). | TASK-90 lifted `Capabilities` into skills-parser exactly for this. Re-declaring zod locally avoids a runtime import. | importing a zod schema from skills-parser (would be a runtime cross-plugin import ŌĆö forbidden). |
| 2026-05-31 | Five hooks: `connectors:list`, `connectors:get`, `connectors:upsert`, `connectors:delete`, `connectors:resolve`. Storage/mechanism-agnostic payloads ŌĆö NO `transport`/`command`/`stdio`/`url`/`mcp` as first-class hook fields (they live only inside the spec's `Capabilities`). `keyMode`/`visibility`/`usageNote` are fine. | Card acceptance + boundary review. resolve returns the mechanism-agnostic descriptor (full spec); get/list return metadata + spec. | folding resolve into get (rejected ŌĆö card lists 5 distinct hooks; resolve is the future routing entry point). |
| 2026-05-31 | Store keyed `(owner_user_id, connector_id)`; ownership-scoped. | 2026-05-31 | Wire into k8s preset ONLY (per Clarifications). Add to `PLUGINS_TO_DROP` in BOTH acceptance.test.ts + multi-tenant-acceptance.test.ts (postgres-backed). | 2026-05-31 | Half-wired window OPEN by design: the connector store exists but nothing routes through it yet (skill capability block stays authoritative). This is explicitly sanctioned by the card + design Phase 1 ŌĆö NOT an invariant-#3 violation because the plugin is fully registered + tested + reachable; the *consumer* lands in later phases. | Card: "This OPENS the half-wired window". Plugin itself is complete and reachable. | wiring a consumer now (out of scope ŌĆö later phases). |
| 2026-05-31 (TASK-93) | Extend the approved-caps wall to connectors via an ADDITIVE polymorphic-subject: add `connector_id TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT ''` to `skills_v1_approved_caps`, PK ŌåÆ 6-col `(owner,agent,skill_id,connector_id,cap_kind,cap_value)`. Grant subject is exactly one of `{skill, connector}`; the unused side carries `''` sentinel (PK cols can't be NULL). Store input is a discriminated `{skillId}\|{connectorId}` ref; existing `{skillId}` callers unchanged. | Card + design ┬¦"reuse the existing wall": extend, don't fork (invariant #4). Empty-string sentinel keeps it purely additive ŌĆö existing skill `WHERE skill_id=X` queries still match (connector rows carry skill_id=''). Migration header bans column rename (ŌåÆside-table), so `(subject_kind,subject_id)` rename is out; the additive column is the smaller back-compatible change. | rename skill_idŌåÆ(subject_kind,subject_id) (rejected ŌĆö destructive per migration header); nullable connector_id NOT in PK (rejected ŌĆö Postgres PK cols are NOT NULL, and it'd allow dup rows). |

| 2026-05-31 | TASK-91: `connectors:upsert` `created` flag = "no LIVE row existed" ŌĆö resurrecting a tombstoned connector reports `created:true` (a tombstoned row is invisible to its owner via get/list, so re-connecting it is a creation from the user's view). | Matches the user mental model; the alternative (PK-existence) would surface a confusing `created:false` for a connector the user thinks is brand new. | `created` = "no row with this PK at all" (rejected ŌĆö leaks the soft-delete tombstone into the API semantic). |

## 2026-05-31 ŌĆö TASK-96 connector keyMode connect flow + reach-by-attachment

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|

| 2026-05-31 | The `account:<service>` service tag for each slot = the slot's existing `CapabilitySlot.account` when present, else the connector `id`. | 2026-05-31 | Consent gate: `requiresSharedKeyConsent` is true iff the resolved key becomes spendable by an identity the keyholder doesn't solely control ŌĆö i.e. `keyMode==='workspace'` (one key, every allowed agent spends it) OR `visibility==='shared'`. `personal`+`private` ŌåÆ false (you only ever act as yourself). The consent COPY ("Sharing this key lets their assistant act as you on <service>. They can't copy the key ŌĆö but they can use it.") is a single exported constant `SHARED_KEY_CONSENT_COPY` + a `sharedKeyConsentMessage(service)` formatter in @ax/connectors. | Design "Consent caveat (invariant #5)": the proxy stops theft, not authorized misuse; the consent is one explicit moment, surfaced BEFORE the key becomes spendable by a shared/team agent. Exporting the copy + a boolean gate lets the future connect surface render it and a test pin it ŌĆö without the deferred UI. | hard-code the copy in the (not-yet-built) UI (rejected ŌĆö then nothing in THIS card surfaces/tests the consent acceptance criterion). |
| 2026-05-31 | NO new visibility/public/private flag on @ax/credentials. Reach derives solely from the credential SCOPE (`global|user|agent`) the key is bound to ŌĆö `personal`ŌåÆuser, `workspace`ŌåÆglobal, a shared agentŌåÆagent-scope. Pin with a guard test asserting `credentials:set`/`credentials:list` payload shapes carry no `visibility`/`public`/`private`/`shared`/`reach` field. | Card acceptance #2 + design "Credentials: reach by attachment, never by visibility". The existing scope model already expresses every reach (private/shared/personal-default/company-key). | add a visibility column to credentials (rejected ŌĆö directly violates the card + design; reach is already fully expressible via scope). |
| 2026-05-31 | The scope vocabulary (`'user'|'global'`) is re-declared LOCALLY in @ax/connectors (a `CredentialScope`-shaped string literal union), NOT imported from @ax/credentials. | Invariant #2 (no cross-plugin runtime import); same posture as the existing local zod re-declaration of Capabilities. The credential-plan's `scope` strings are a stable contract, not @ax/credentials internals. | import CredentialScope from @ax/credentials (rejected ŌĆö cross-plugin import, forbidden by eslint no-restricted-imports). |

Check `git fetch origin main` + diff the shared files BEFORE assuming your base is current; auto-ship merges siblings ahead of you.** Also: `connectors:resolve` does NOT carry `usageNote` (it's the routing descriptor); only `connectors:list-defaults` (full Connector) does ŌĆö private connectors resolved via resolve fall back to a generic synthetic SKILL.md body (acceptable; the note is a nicety, not load-bearing for reach).

## 2026-05-31 | TASK-95 architecture: host-executed connector_propose tool (NOT a sandbox executor + IPC chain)
- **Decision:** The model-facing connector-authoring tool is `connector_propose`, a HOST-executed tool (`executesIn: 'host'`) in a new package `@ax/tool-connector-propose` ŌĆö mirroring `@ax/skill-broker`'s `request_capability`, NOT `@ax/tool-skill-propose`'s sandbox-executor+IPC pattern. It registers BOTH the descriptor (tool:register) AND `tool:execute:connector_propose`, reads (userId, agentId) from the host-trusted tool ctx, and calls the existing `connectors:install-authored` hook on the bus.
- **Rationale:** connector args are pure structured JSON `{connectorId,name,hosts,slots,packages,mcpServers,usageNote,keyMode}` the model produces inline ŌĆö there is NO draft directory to read from the sandbox FS (unlike skill_propose which must read /ephemeral/skill-draft/<id>/). So the sandbox-executor + IPC-action chain TASK-94's note sketched is UNNECESSARY complexity; the request_capability host-tool shape is the right, smaller fit. The host hook `connectors:install-authored` is the authoritative validator (I5 trust boundary); the tool is a thin scope-stamping adapter (light shape check + clean error map, like request_capability's skillId check).
- **Alternatives:** (a) sandbox executor + connector.install-authored IPC action (TASK-94's literal sketch) ŌĆö rejected: no FS bytes to read sandbox-side; pure overhead. (b) add connector_propose into @ax/skill-broker ŌĆö rejected: broker's identity is skill-CATALOG brokering (hard calls skills:*); a new package per authoring tool matches the @ax/tool-skill-propose convention and keeps the connectors:install-authored dep isolated + hasService-gated.
- New package needs project refs in root tsconfig.json AND presets/k8s/tsconfig.json (TASK-91 gotcha) + an entry in ALWAYS_ON_BROKER_TOOLS so non-wildcard agents see it.

| 2026-05-31 (TASK-111) | **SkillŌåÆconnector cap-resolution bridge: resolve each skill's `connectors[]` via `connectors:resolve` and fold through the EXISTING `foldConnectorCaps` path, deduped against TASK-97's agent effective set.** Add `connectors` to the orchestrator's `ResolvedSkillForOrch` mirror (`skills:resolve` already returns it via @ax/skills `ResolvedSkill.connectors`; the mirror just dropped it). In orchestrator.ts collect the union of `connectors[]` over `unionedSkills`, resolve the not-already-resolved ids (new `resolveSkillReferencedConnectors` helper in connector-union.ts), append to `effectiveConnectors`, then the single existing `foldConnectorCaps` call folds them. (b) resolve inside @ax/skills `skills:resolve` and return folded caps ŌĆö REJECTED, cross-plugin coupling + the orchestrator is the materialization owner. |
| 2026-05-31 (TASK-111) | **`skill_propose` migration is already done at the instruction layer** ŌĆö `ax-skill-creator/SKILL.md` already teaches `connectors:` references + forbids a `capabilities:` block (TASK-92/94), the parser rejects misplaced cap keys, and the skill-propose executor ships raw `manifestYaml` so `connectors:` round-trips to the host re-parse. (b) keep it in @ax/connectors keyed by agent_id ŌĆö REJECTED, would split the agent's config across two plugins (the agent-global attachment is admin-managed agent config, exactly like skill_attachments which lives in @ax/agents per the 2026-05-26 TASK-33 decision). |
| 2026-06-01 | **Connector attachments do NOT participate in the wildcard sentinel; `mcpConfigIds` reverts to MCP-only meaning (the acceptance criterion).** The orchestrator's `withBrokerDefaults` + `@ax/mcp-client` `filterByAgentScope` wildcard stays `allowedTools=[] && mcpConfigIds=[]`. The admin route's `rejectsWildcardScope` (Ōēź1 tool or Ōēź1 MCP config) is UNCHANGED. An agent attached only to connectors still needs Ōēź1 allowedTool (or the dev-mode empty-empty wildcard) ŌĆö identical to a skill-only agent today. | This is the EXACT precedent skill_attachments set: a separate column that does not gate the sentinel. NOT a product decision ŌĆö connectors mechanically don't belong in the host tool-dispatcher catalog binding (`mcpConfigIds` = `mcp.<configId>.<tool>` visibility via filterByAgentScope), whereas a connector's MCP servers reach the agent as sandbox `.mcp.json` installed-entries (foldConnectorCaps), an ORTHOGONAL mechanism gated by the SDK. TASK-98's overloading actually mis-fed connector ids into filterByAgentScope as host mcp config ids ŌĆö reverting is a correctness fix, not just a refactor. | (a) make connectors count toward the sentinel ŌĆö REJECTED, would re-overload the field the card removes + diverge from skill_attachments. (b) block on "how does a connector-wildcard map" as a product decision ŌĆö REJECTED, the scoping-caution trigger does not fire: connectors never legitimately mapped to the wildcard sentinel (the sentinel is MCP+tools dev-bypass); skill_attachments already answered "an attachment-only agent isn't a wildcard". |
| 2026-06-01 | **The orchestrator union reads attachments as a THIRD source inside `resolveEffectiveConnectors`, resolving each attached id via `connectors:resolve` (owner-scoped, deduped against defaults + owner's-own).** Pass `agent.connectorAttachments` into `resolveEffectiveConnectors(bus, ctx, attachments)`. | The resolved `agent` already flows into runAgentInvoke (line 1204); `connectors:resolve` is owner-scoped (store `getByIdNotDeleted(userId, connectorId)`), so an attached connector resolves under the agent owner = the chat user (personal agents). Folds through the EXISTING `foldConnectorCaps` (no second materialization path, invariant #4). NON-FATAL per the existing union posture (a resolve miss skips that connector, never widens reach). | (a) a 4th separate fold path for attachments ŌĆö REJECTED, duplicates foldConnectorCaps (I4). (b) resolve attachments in @ax/agents and return folded caps from agents:resolve ŌĆö REJECTED, the orchestrator is the materialization owner + would couple @ax/agents to connector caps. |
| 2026-06-01 | **AgentForm writes connector ids to the new store via a dedicated `PATCH /admin/agents/:id/connector-attachments` (mirroring skill-attachments), NOT via agents:create/update's `mcpConfigIds`.** For a NEW agent the connector section saves after first create (same deferral skill_attachments uses ŌĆö "New agents get their section after first save"). The connector picker's selections no longer feed the create/update body's mcpConfigIds (reverted to []). Idempotent migration: existing agents whose connector ids were stuffed into `mcpConfigIds` are NOT auto-migrated at the data layer (ax-next has no prod data; mcpConfigIds genuinely held MCP config ids historically too, so a blind migration would misclassify real MCP ids as connectors). The migration is idempotent-by-construction (the new column defaults to []); existing connectors keep folding while attached via the new picker. | The card says "existing attachments migrated if needed; idempotent migration". With no prod data + the field's dual historical meaning (MCP ids AND TASK-98 connector ids are indistinguishable), a data migration that reclassifies mcpConfigIdsŌåÆconnectorAttachments would corrupt genuine MCP bindings. The honest idempotent migration is the additive NOT-NULL-DEFAULT-'[]' column (every existing row reads [] safely) + the UI moving the write to the new store. No regression: a connector attached via the new picker folds via the union (TASK-97 path). | (a) auto-copy every agent's mcpConfigIds into connector_attachments on migrate ŌĆö REJECTED, can't distinguish a real MCP config id from a TASK-98 connector id ŌåÆ would mis-bind. (b) a backfill keyed on "id exists in connectors table" ŌĆö REJECTED, over-engineering for zero prod rows + still racy vs MCP ids that happen to match a connector id. |

|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-06-01 | **Service-tag derivation lives in FOUR places, not the two the design names.** Design lists `connectors/src/credential-plan.ts` + `channel-web/src/lib/connectors.ts`. Reality also has `chat-orchestrator/src/connector-union.ts` + `connector-card.ts` (and `skill-broker/request-capability.ts`) re-deriving `slot.account ?? connectorId`. **Resolution: change only the two named `serviceTagForSlot` fns + drop `account` from the connectors `CapabilitySlotSchema`.** The connectors store re-validates capabilities on read (`store.ts` `validateCapabilities`), so dropping `account` from the connector schema STRIPS it on every read ŌåÆ the orchestrator/skill-broker (which resolve via store-parsed hooks) see `account===undefined` and their `?? connectorId` fallback collapses to connectorId automatically. Runtime stays consistent (invariant #4) with zero orchestrator edits. | The orchestrator's `account` is a GENERAL skills+connectors capability mechanism (`skills-parser/capabilities.ts:10`, `orchestrator.ts` foldAuthoredSkillCaps uses `account:<svc>` for skill slots too). Removing it there would break skills + expand scope into another plugin's tests for inputs the connector store can no longer produce. | (a) Also edit orchestrator/connector-card/skill-broker ŌåÆ rejected: out of design scope, touches skill-cap path, breaks orchestrator tests that feed `account` directly (testing an input now impossible for connectors). Tracked as optional follow-up: vestigial `slot.account` reads in connector-union/connector-card are now dead-but-harmless. |
| 2026-06-01 | **`CredentialSlotForm` has NO Remove button today** ŌĆö `onCleared` is a prop on the form + `CredentialSlotRow` but the form never renders Remove or calls it; Remove lived only in `KeysTab` (being deleted). Design change #3 assumes "Replace/Remove via the form's existing onCleared." **Resolution: wire the dead `onCleared` ŌĆö add a Remove button to `CredentialSlotForm` shown only when `current.set`, calling `clearDestinationCredential` + `onCleared`.** | The design names the form's onCleared as the mechanism; it's the one-source-of-truth (invariant #4) home for Remove. Form tests use `set:false` so no Remove renders there ŌåÆ unaffected. | (a) Implement Remove only in the Connect dialog wrapper ŌåÆ rejected: duplicates clear logic, contradicts "via the form's onCleared". Side effect: ProvidersPanel + RoutinesList sheets gain a Remove for set keys (benign improvement; verify their tests). |
| 2026-06-01 | **Implement directly (not subagent-per-task).** | The change is tightly coupled ŌĆö two `serviceTagForSlot` mirrors must stay byte-identical, shared presence logic, and the schema strip ripples through ~5 backend test files. A subagent split risks the two derivations diverging. Context budget healthy. | Subagent-driven-development per yolo-ship default (rejected for this coupling). |
| 2026-06-01 | **`serviceTagForSlot` keeps its `(slot, connectorId)` two-arg signature; body returns `connectorId`; slot param renamed `_slot`** (lint `^_` ignore). | Minimizes call-site churn (deriveCredentialPlan unchanged) and lets the test prove "legacy account tag ignored" by passing a slot WITH account and asserting connectorId. | Single-arg `serviceTagForSlot(connectorId)` (rejected ŌĆö loses the direct ignore-account assertion; more churn). |
| 2026-06-01 | **`connectors:delete` purge: `credentials:delete` declared as `optionalCalls` + `bus.hasService` guard; failures logged + swallowed.** Mirrors `@ax/routines` sync.ts posture. Connector loaded BEFORE softDelete (getByIdNotDeleted returns null after). ownerId = userId (user scope) / null (global). | A stripped preset without `@ax/credentials` must still delete the connector (degraded: key lingers). A credential hiccup must never wedge connector deletion. No new hook signature (credentials:delete already exists). | Hard `calls` dep (rejected ŌĆö breaks credential-less presets). |

### 2026-06-01 ŌĆö ax-code-reviewer findings (whole-branch review before PR)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-06-01 | **BLOCKER fix: reject `keyMode:'workspace'` on the user authoring route** (`rejectAdminOnlyFields`, connectors/admin-routes.ts). Reviewer found a non-admin could create-then-delete a `workspace`-keyMode connector (allowed by the user route ŌĆö it only gated `visibility`/`defaultAttached`) and the new purge-on-delete would tombstone the SHARED global key `account:<id>` (owner-independent) ŌåÆ cross-tenant credential DoS. | The global credential WRITE is already admin-gated (/admin/destinations); the connector that drives the global PURGE must be too. With workspace rejected on the user route, non-admins own only private/personal connectors ŌåÆ their purge only ever hits their OWN (scope:user, ownerId:userId) rows. Fixes at the same authz layer where visibility/defaultAttached are gated. | (a) skip global purge in the hook ŌåÆ rejected: breaks the legit admin purge-on-delete; the hook can't see admin-ness. Bug-Fix-Policy regression tests added (user create + PATCH-flip to workspace ŌåÆ 400). |
| 2026-06-01 | **SHOULD-FIX: widen the account-service destination regex** (`/^[a-z][a-z0-9-]{0,63}$/` ŌåÆ `/^[a-z0-9][a-z0-9_-]{0,127}$/`) in @ax/credentials-admin-routes/destination-routes.ts. | Service is now ALWAYS the connector id (id grammar allows leading digit + `_`, e.g. `1password`, `my_crm`); the stricter destination grammar 400'd those, making such connectors unconnectable once the `account`-tag workaround was removed. | 2026-06-01 | **SHOULD-FIX: retarget stale `slot.account ?? id` comments** in connector-union.ts / connector-card.ts / skill-broker request-capability.ts to say the `?? connectorId` is VESTIGIAL for connectors (store strips `account` on read) and only live for skill slots. ### 2026-06-01 ŌĆö ax-code-reviewer round 2 (BLOCKER only partially fixed)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-06-01 | **BLOCKER (round 2): gate the GLOBAL credential purge at the delete PRIMITIVE, not just the HTTP route.** Round-1's `rejectAdminOnlyFields` keyMode gate only covered `/settings/connectors`; the authored-connector approve path (`connector_propose` tool ŌåÆ `connectors:install-authored` ŌåÆ non-admin approval ŌåÆ `applyAuthoredConnectorGrant` promotes via the `connectors:upsert` HOOK with `keyMode: draft.keyMode`) is a 2nd non-admin door to owning a live workspace connector ŌåÆ delete ŌåÆ global-key DoS. Fix: `connectors:delete` gains `purgeGlobal?: boolean` (default false); `deleteConnector` skips `scope:'global'` entries unless set; both route destroy handlers pass `purgeGlobal: actor.isAdmin`. Closes ALL paths (route, authored, legacy) at the operation. Tests: hook purgeGlobal:falseŌåÆno global purge (the security regression) + purgeGlobal:trueŌåÆpurged; route test admin-destroy purges / non-admin-destroy doesn't. Kept the round-1 route keyMode gate as defense-in-depth. | Reviewer's Option A (skip global purge entirely) ŌĆö **rejected**: it would orphan a workspace connector's global company key on delete with NO UI home (this PR removes the Credentials tab; the AI-model-keys tab is provider-keys-only), violating the design's core "no secret lingers" goal. Option C (authority flag) is secure AND preserves admin purge-on-delete. The reviewer's "the hook can't distinguish authorized from unauthorized" is resolved by passing the caller-granted authority (`purgeGlobal`), an invariant-#5-minimized flag. | (a) skip global entirely (orphans the key); (b) gate keyMode at every write chokepoint incl. the promote path (more surface, doesn't fix legacy-owned state). |
| 2026-06-01 | **CORRECTION to the round-1 decision:** my claim that `orchestrator.ts:2753` is "the general capability-card builder where account is live for skills" was WRONG. The reviewer showed it's inside `applyAuthoredConnectorGrant` (the CONNECTOR grant path); `draft.proposal` is store-stripped of `account`, so the read is vestigial-for-connectors exactly like the other 3 sites. Retargeted that comment too. | Factual error caught by the reviewer ŌĆö `applyAuthoredCapabilityGrant` (skill twin) has no account row-builder; the live skill account path is `foldAuthoredSkillCaps`. | ŌĆö |

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-06-02 | **Move "Agents" from the Admin nav to the user "Settings" nav** (AdminSidebar USER_NAV + AdminShell TAB_META eyebrow Settings); visible to every user. | User: even non-admins should list+manage their own agents. Agent CRUD (`/admin/agents` create/list/show/update/destroy) is ALREADY `requireUser` + owner-scoped ŌĆö only the nav hid it. | ŌĆö |
| 2026-06-02 | **Open the admin-only attachment routes to non-admin OWNERS, owner-scoped** (`/admin/agents/:id/{skill,connector}-attachments`): replace `if (!isAdmin) 403` with a workspace-connector guard. The attachment HOOKS already enforce owner-or-admin (`assertWriteAllowed`); the route gate was the only block. Security rule: a non-admin's set is rejected iff any **directly-attached OR skill-referenced** connector resolves owner-scoped (`connectors:resolve {userId: actor.id}`) to **keyMode:'workspace'** ŌĆö the only path to a GLOBAL/company credential. Personal connectors (the user's own per-user key) are their own reach ŌåÆ no escalation. Not-owned/dangling ids are runtime no-ops ŌåÆ tolerated (matches existing orphan tolerance). Admin bypasses. Fail-closed if `connectors:resolve` is absent (reject non-admin attach of a non-empty connector set). | User chose "Full: attach own connectors/skills (owner-scoped); workspace/shared stay admin-only." | (a) keep admin-only (rejected ŌĆö user wants full); (b) basic CRUD only (rejected ŌĆö agents couldn't use picked connectors). |
| 2026-06-02 | **Add `connectors:resolve` as an `optionalCall` to @ax/agents** (the attachment routes call it to check keyMode). Boundary review: alternate impl = @ax/connectors-sqlite registers the same hook; payload `{userId,connectorId}`ŌåÆ`{keyMode,...}` storage-agnostic; one-way agentsŌåÆconnectors (connectors never calls agents ŌåÆ no cycle); not an IPC action. | Needed for the owner-scoped keyMode guard. | Embed the check in the orchestrator at runtime (rejected ŌĆö write-time validation is the right place + less invasive). |
| 2026-06-02 | **Keep `AuthoredSkillsSection` (the agent's model-proposed skill DRAFTS + approval) admin-only for now**; hide it for non-admins in AgentForm; `/admin/agents/:id/authored-skills*` routes stay admin-gated. | The user's ask is "attach connectors/skills" = SkillAttachmentsSection (attach existing skills) + the connector picker. Authored-skill approval is a distinct capability-grant flow deserving its own security pass. Tracked as a follow-up. | Open it now (rejected ŌĆö scope + separate security surface). |

| 2026-06-02 | **FIX (review Finding 1): `setSkillAttachments` must pass `ownerUserId: actor.id` to `skills:resolve`.** Without it, `skills:resolve` returns only GLOBAL catalog skills (plugin.ts:575) ŌĆö so a non-admin attaching their OWN user-scoped skill (the picker now lists `/settings/skills`) resolved to `[]` ŌåÆ validator `skill-not-found` ŌåÆ 400, silently breaking the feature. Passing ownerUserId unions global + the caller's user-scoped skills (user-wins); a superset for admins (no regression) and it also lets the workspace-connector guard see a user-scoped skill's referenced connectors (closes the over-stated-guarantee Finding 3). Test stub now models ownerUserId (user-scoped ids only when passed); the 200-path test uses a genuinely user-scoped skill so it would catch the regression. | Caught by the pre-PR ax-code-reviewer; the original test stub resolved ids regardless of ownerUserId, masking it. | ŌĆö |

| 2026-06-02 | TASK-139 open-question 3 (budget policy) PINNED: NO renderMinimal/drop machinery in Phase 1 ŌĆö the modules are all small fixed runner prose EXCEPT the inject-if-present `.ax/` files, which are agent-authored and unbounded. Policy: inject each `.ax/` file in full; do not truncate or drop in Phase 1. If a file read exceeds a generous hard cap (256 KiB) the runner skips that single file with a logged warning (a runaway/corrupt file can't blow the prompt) ŌĆö it does not truncate mid-content. | v1's per-module token-budget allocator is over-engineered for Phase 1 (4 short fixed modules + 3 small identity files). Drop-when-tight is a real concern only once identity files grow large; that's a follow-up, not MVP. The 256 KiB per-file guard is the thin safety net (a corrupt multi-MB file is the only realistic blow-up), implemented as skip-with-warn not truncate so identity is never silently half-injected. | Port v1's allocateModules budget allocator (rejected ŌĆö YAGNI for Phase 1; 4 fixed modules don't need a priority/minimal allocator). Truncate large files mid-content (rejected ŌĆö silently corrupts identity; skip-whole-file-with-warning is honest). |
| 2026-06-02 | TASK-139: templates (BOOTSTRAP.md + IDENTITY.md/SOUL.md scaffolds) live as versioned TS string constants in the runner package (`src/identity-templates.ts`), not a separate `@ax/agent-identity` package. | Task allows either; a TS string constant needs no postbuild copy step (unlike a .md file in `files`), is trivially unit-testable, and avoids spinning up a new package + tsconfig ref for ~3 strings. Phase 2's bootstrap route will import the BOOTSTRAP string from here (or it gets re-homed then if a second consumer appears). | New `@ax/agent-identity` package (rejected ŌĆö premature; one consumer at Phase 1, no cross-plugin-import need yet). Ship as `.md` files copied by postbuild (rejected ŌĆö adds a copy step + runtime fs read of a packaged asset vs. a compiled-in constant). |

| 2026-06-02 | TASK-139 codex Phase-5 review ŌĆö 3 findings triaged. [P2 read-before-size] FIXED: `readAxFile` now `stat`s before `readFile` (skip non-regular files + over-cap by file-type/size, so a multi-GB blob or symlink-to-/dev/zero never OOMs/hangs runner startup); +symlink-to-dir regression test. [P1 warm-runner staleness] ACCEPTED-AS-KNOWN: the SDK has no mid-`query()` setSystemPrompt and the runner drives ONE long-lived query per warm sandbox, so the prompt is composed once per SPAWN not per in-query turn ŌĆö identical to the existing `agentConfig.systemPrompt`+augment lifecycle (orchestrator already augments fresh-spawn-only). Documented in code; bootstrap-graduation respawn is design Phase 2's job. [P1 bootstrap-trust] OUT-OF-PHASE: `.ax/` files are agent-writable and `@ax/validator-identity` (the gate) is explicitly design Phase 3; documented as a trust note at the bootstrap branch. | The two P1s are scope/architecture boundaries the design already drew (validator=Phase 3, bootstrap-flow=Phase 2), not regressions this patch introduced; the SDK constraint is real (no setSystemPrompt). The P2 was a genuine bug in my own code (read-then-measure) ŌĆö fixed test-first. | Pull the validator forward into Phase 1 (rejected ŌĆö half-wired, the plugin doesn't exist; violates Invariant #3). Force a respawn after each turn (rejected ŌĆö defeats warm-runner keepalive PR #124; the bootstrap-only respawn belongs to the Phase-2 first-run flow). |

| 2026-06-02 | TASK-139 codex round-2 caught a P1 in MY round-1 P2 fix: `stat()` FOLLOWS symlinks, so an agent-planted `.ax/SOUL.md -> /proc/self/environ` (a regular file) passes `isFile()` and `readFile` injects the runner's env + IPC/proxy token into the system prompt = workspace-escape + secret leak to the model. FIXED by switching `stat` ŌåÆ `lstat` (reports the link itself; `isFile()` is false for any symlink ŌåÆ rejected; identity reads stay strictly inside `.ax/`). +symlink-to-secret regression test. | `.ax/` files are agent-writable (untrusted), and ANY follow-symlink read of an agent-controlled path is a secret-exfil primitive when the bytes land in the prompt. lstat is the correct primitive for "read only files the agent legitimately wrote, never a link out". | Resolve realpath and assert it stays under `.ax/` (rejected ŌĆö heavier; lstat-reject-symlink is simpler and sufficient since legitimate identity files are never symlinks). Keep `stat` + path-prefix check on the resolved target (rejected ŌĆö TOCTOU-prone vs. a flat lstat-reject). |

## 2026-06-03 ŌĆö TASK-142 shipped as PR #305 (Phase 4 conversational-agent-identity)

Drops `agents_v1_agents.system_prompt` (DROP COLUMN IF EXISTS migration). Closes the
half-wired string-fallback window (Invariant #3): `.ax/` files are the only identity
source of truth (Invariant #4). Key changes:
- Runner `buildSystemPrompt(displayName, augment, ŌĆ”)` ŌĆö removed `buildFallbackPrompt` +
  the claude_code-preset path; no-IDENTITY.md falls back to a `You are <displayName>, ŌĆ”`
  line (the canonical `fallbackIdentityLine` in @ax/agent-identity-templates, formerly
  `backfillIdentityFile`). Bootstrap trust-note updated (validator wired in TASK-141).
- `AgentConfig` session snapshot: `systemPrompt` ŌåÆ `displayName` + new `systemPromptAugment`,
  threaded through ipc-protocol/session-*/sandbox-*/mcp-client/chat-orchestrator.
- File-based admin editor: AgentForm Identity/Soul/Operating(ŌåÆAGENTS.md, opt-in) via new
  channel-web GET/PUT /admin/agents/:id/identity (workspace:read + workspace:apply ŌåÆ
  validator-identity). Route added `workspace:read` to channel-web manifest calls.
- memory-strata seeds system/agent.md from composed `.ax/` identity (new compose-identity.ts,
  reads `<rootPath>/permanent/.ax/`).
- Removed dead runIdentityBackfill + its plugin wiring + workspace optionalCalls.
Two bugs caught pre-merge: (1) empty `systemPromptAugment` rejected by session requireString ŌĆö
fixed with requireStringAllowEmpty (only surfaced in @ax/cli e2e); (2) identity PUT
parent:null was a strict-CAS miss ŌåÆ 500 for existing-history agents ŌĆö fixed with the
parent-mismatch retry contract.

## 2026-06-03 ŌĆö TASK-147: decouple admin identity save from the tools-required gate (wildcard/bare agents)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|------|----------|-----------|--------------|
| 2026-06-03 | The AgentForm tools-required gate fires only when the save would CREATE a new wildcard agent or DEMOTE a tool-listed agent to wildcard ŌĆö never on a bare-stays-bare identity edit. On such an edit the PATCH OMITS `allowedTools`+`mcpConfigIds`. | TASK-143 walk GLITCH: the combined AgentForm Save was over-gated ŌĆö its unconditional `if (allowedTools.length===0) return` aborted the whole submit (incl. `putAgentIdentity`) for an existing wildcard/bare agent. The standalone `PUT /admin/agents/:id/identity` route is ungated and worked. A bare agent (`allowedTools=[]`) is a legit store-allowed state; the server only rejects the wildcard sentinel when BOTH `allowedTools` AND `mcpConfigIds` are present-and-empty (`rejectsWildcardScope`, agents/admin-routes.ts), on create AND update. So omitting both empty fields from the PATCH leaves the agent bare and avoids the server rejection. | (a) Suppress the gate globally ŌĆö rejected: would let the form create new wildcard agents, which the server (correctly) rejects, and let a tool-listed agent be silently demoted. (b) Always send `allowedTools:[]` on the bare edit ŌĆö rejected: server `rejectsWildcardScope` 400s on the both-empty PATCH. |

Key facts learned (server-side wildcard rule, `packages/agents/src/admin-routes.ts`):
- `rejectsWildcardScope` triggers ONLY when `allowedTools` AND `mcpConfigIds` are both present-and-empty; runs on both `create` and `update`.
- `updateBodySchema` makes every field optional ŌåÆ a PATCH that omits the tool fields is accepted and leaves the agent's tool scope untouched.
