Walked end-to-end on `ax-next-dev` (branch image): Part A ŌĆö "Connect Acme Test" card appeared on the proposing turn; Part B ŌĆö dismissed card, Settings shelf showed it, Approve promoted it to Connected/Ready (draftŌåÆactive + registry row + creds, DB-verified). Test artifacts cleaned up. | 2026-06-03 | TASK-151 (k8s native-sidecar rendering). The per-session readiness BUDGET (which scales with service count) is computed by a pure `computeReadinessBudgetMs({ baseTimeoutMs, serviceCount, perServiceColdStartMs })` exported from `@ax/sandbox-k8s/config.ts`, called in `open-session.ts` step 4 where `input.services.length` is in scope ŌĆö NOT baked into `ResolvedSandboxK8sConfig.readinessTimeoutMs` (that stays the service-LESS 60s default). Formula: `serviceCount === 0 ? baseTimeoutMs : baseTimeoutMs + serviceCount * perServiceColdStartMs`. New config fields: `serviceCpuLimit`/`serviceMemoryLimit`/`serviceCpuRequest`/`serviceMemoryRequest` (per-sidecar resourcing) + `perServiceColdStartMs` (default 120_000 ŌĆö JVM cold-start + image pull + sequential gate). | Card pins the policy to config.ts but the budget VALUE is per-session (service count is a request quantity, not a config constant). A pure fn keeps the policy constants in config while the count multiplies at the call site. Baking a fixed timeout into the resolved config would lose the "scales with N" requirement. | (a) compute inside config.resolveConfig ŌĆö rejected, resolveConfig has no service count. (b) inline the formula in open-session ŌĆö rejected, the constants belong with the other config defaults + a pure fn is unit-testable. |
| 2026-06-03 | TASK-151 per-`writablePaths` emptyDir volume naming: `svc-<serviceName>-<i>` where i is the writablePaths index. serviceName already matches ID_RE (lowercase alnum + dashes, k8s-name-safe); the index disambiguates a service's multiple writable paths and prevents collisions across services. Each volume is `{ name, emptyDir: {} }`; the matching sidecar volumeMount is `{ name, mountPath: <writablePath> }`. | DNS-1123 + Ōēż63-char k8s volume-name rules + uniqueness across N services ├Ś M paths. ID_RE-constrained name keeps it valid without sanitization; index keeps it unique. | Hashing the path ŌĆö rejected (opaque in `kubectl describe`, and ID_RE name + index is already collision-free). |
| 2026-06-03 | TASK-151 sidecar env: stamp ONLY the descriptor's own `env` map. Sidecars get NEITHER the runner's git-paranoid/proxy/CA env NOR AX_* ŌĆö they're third-party service images, not the runner. The egress lock (I4) is enforced at the NetworkPolicy layer (S1), not via env; services bind 0.0.0.0 by their own image default, the descriptor never encodes a bind address. startupProbe comes from `healthcheck` ({kind:'tcp',port}ŌåÆtcpSocket; {kind:'exec',command}ŌåÆexec); omitted when healthcheck absent. portsŌåÆcontainerPort. Locked containerSecurity reused verbatim (runAsNonRoot/uid+gid 1000/caps drop ALL/readOnlyRootFilesystem). | I5 (minimize capabilities) + I1 (backend-agnostic descriptor). A leaked AX_AUTH_TOKEN or proxy CA on a third-party sidecar would widen blast radius for no benefit. | Inheriting runner env "for convenience" ŌĆö rejected, it's a capability leak onto an untrusted-adjacent container. |
| 2026-06-03 | TASK-151 review finding (self-caught, fixed in-branch): k8s container + volume NAMES are DNS-1123 labels capped at 63 BYTES, a DIFFERENT constraint from the session-id LABEL VALUE that `sanitizeLabel` already handles. `ServiceDescriptorSchema`'s `ID_RE` (`^[a-z][a-z0-9-]{0,63}$`) permits a 64-char service name, so a naive `svc-<name>` (and `svc-<name>-<i>` volume name) overflows ŌåÆ the API server rejects the WHOLE pod with an opaque 422 ŌåÆ session roll-back. Added `serviceNameBase()` in pod-spec.ts: deterministic truncate-+-sha1-suffix when `svc-<name>` plus a 3-byte index reserve would exceed 63; short names (postgres/kafka/mongo) pass through unchanged. | When rendering any k8s resource name (container/volume/label-KEY Ōēż63) from a schema-permitted string whose max length can exceed the k8s limit, bound it deterministically. ID_RE's `{0,63}` quantifier means MAX 64 chars (1 anchor + 63), not 63 ŌĆö easy off-by-one to miss. | Reuse `sanitizeLabel` ŌĆö rejected, it sanitizes label VALUES (different char rules, no `svc-`/index-reserve awareness); a focused helper is clearer. |

| 2026-06-03 | **TASK-149: TCP-mode discriminator for the credential-proxy is `config.proxySocketHostPath` EMPTY + `proxyConfig.endpoint` set; hostPath-mode is `proxySocketHostPath` non-empty.** The credential-proxy plugin ALREADY supports `listen: { kind: 'tcp', host, port }` and `buildEndpointString` already emits `tcp://host:port` ŌĆö the gap was never the listener, it's (a) the advertised cluster Service URL (bind host ŌēĀ reachable host) and (b) CA delivery without a shared dir. In TCP mode pod-spec stamps `AX_PROXY_CA_PEM=<pem>` + points cert vars at a tmpfs path (`/home/runner/.ax/proxy-ca/ca.crt`, the existing HOME emptyDir) and the RUNNER writes the PEM at boot; hostPath mode keeps the mounted `/var/run/ax/proxy-ca/ca.crt`. The runner's CA-from-env writer no-ops when the file already exists, so hostPath mode "wins when present" (card requirement) with one code path. | The card's file pointers named pod-spec.ts:327 (the `pc.endpoint` branch) + open-session.ts:506 (subprocess CA-write to mirror). The subprocess backend already writes the CA to a per-session tmpdir + points NODE_EXTRA_CA_CERTS/SSL_CERT_FILE/GIT_SSL_CAINFO/DENO_CERT there ŌĆö k8s TCP mode is the same shape, except the CA arrives as an env var (the host can't write into the runner pod) and the runner does the write. | (a) keep CA on a hostPath even in TCP mode (rejected ŌĆö GKE Sandbox bans hostPath, the whole point); (b) ship CA via a downward-API projected volume or a Secret mount (rejected ŌĆö extra k8s object per session, env-var is simplest and the cert is public per I1); (c) discriminate TCP via a new explicit `mode` enum (rejected ŌĆö `proxySocketHostPath` empty + endpoint set is already an unambiguous signal, no new field needed on the resolved config beyond `proxyEndpoint`). |
| 2026-06-03 | **TASK-149: add `advertisedEndpoint?` to CredentialProxyConfig (analogous to sandbox-k8s `hostIpcUrl`) so `proxy:open-session` returns the cluster Service URL, not the bind address.** `buildEndpointString` returns `tcp://<host>:<port>` where host defaults to `127.0.0.1` / the bind host ŌĆö unreachable from another pod. The chart computes a `credentialProxyServiceUrl` helper (mirror of `hostIpcUrl`) and the preset threads it into the plugin as `advertisedEndpoint`. The plugin returns it verbatim (must be `tcp://...` so the orchestrator's `endpointToProxyConfig` rewrites it to `http://host:port` for HTTPS_PROXY). | The IPC listener solved the identical bind-vs-advertised problem with `hostIpcUrl` (config.ts) ŌĆö copy the shape exactly. No new hook surface (open-session output `proxyEndpoint` field pre-exists; only its VALUE changes in TCP mode). | (a) have the orchestrator compute the Service URL (rejected ŌĆö the proxy plugin owns the endpoint contract, one source of truth I4); (b) reuse the bind host as the advertised host (rejected ŌĆö 127.0.0.1 is wrong cross-pod and 0.0.0.0 isn't a dialable address). |
| 2026-06-03 | TASK-149 Phase 5 (codex review, BOTH accepted as real bugs): **P1 ŌĆö a new TCP proxy Service needs BOTH a runner-egress rule (sandbox-restrict.yaml) AND a host-INGRESS rule (agent-runtime-network.yaml) or the CNI denies the connect.** The host NetworkPolicy selects the host pod and only admitted the IPC port (8080) from runners; the proxy listens inside the SAME host pod on 8888, so without a host-ingress rule for 8888 packets are dropped before reaching the proxy container ŌĆö TCP sessions boot with a correct AX_PROXY_ENDPOINT but every proxy connect fails. Fix: gate a 2nd ingress port (credentialProxy.tcp.port) into the runnerŌåÆhost ingress rule under `if .Values.credentialProxy.tcp.enabled`. **P2 ŌĆö a TCP listen port WITHOUT an advertised endpoint silently ships an unreachable proxy** (binds 0.0.0.0, advertises tcp://0.0.0.0:<port> ŌåÆ http://0.0.0.0:<port>, undialable cross-pod). Fix: env loader throws when tcpPort set + advertisedEndpoint unset, AND createK8sPlugins throws the same (defense-in-depth for a hand-rolled config). | Both are reachability gaps a unit/render test caught only once written: the NetworkPolicy contract is two-sided (egress on the caller + ingress on the target) and I only wrote the egress half; the advertised endpoint was `?optional` on the config but is load-bearing in the k8s TCP posture. Regression tests added: render-test asserts the host-network NP proxy ingress port (+ its absence in hostPath mode); preset-test asserts the throw on port-without-endpoint. | (P1) put the host-ingress on the public NP instead ŌĆö rejected, runners must NOT reach the public surface (issue #39); the IPC-rule's runner selector is the right place. (P2) auto-derive the advertised endpoint from the bind host ŌĆö rejected, 0.0.0.0 has no derivation to a Service DNS name; the chart owns that URL (the credentialProxyAdvertisedEndpoint helper), so fail-loud on a partial config is correct. |

| 2026-06-03 | TASK-149 Phase 5 round 2 (codex, BOTH accepted): **P2a ŌĆö the pod-spec TCP discriminator must key off `proxyConfig.endpoint` (set) + no hostPath, NOT a second `config.proxyEndpoint` knob.** My first cut required `config.proxyEndpoint.length>0 && proxySocketHostPath empty && pc.endpoint` ŌĆö but a programmatic caller who set the proxy to TCP (so `pc.endpoint` is a URL) yet forgot `sandbox.proxyEndpoint` would get `AX_PROXY_ENDPOINT` stamped while the CA vars still pointed at the unmounted hostPath path + `AX_PROXY_CA_PEM` omitted ŌåÆ every TLS call fails. Fix: `tcpMode = proxySocketHostPath empty && pc.endpoint !== undefined` (the runner's ACTUAL inputs, not a lockstep config knob). `config.proxyEndpoint` survives ONLY as the config-level mutual-exclusivity gate in resolveConfig ŌĆö not dead, but no longer read by pod-spec. **P2b ŌĆö `printf "%s-proxy" fullname | trunc 63` truncates AFTER appending, so a 62-63-char fullnameOverride loses the suffix and the proxy Service collides with the host Service (helm refuses two Services, one name).** Fix: reserve the suffix first ŌĆö `$base := fullname | trunc 57` then `printf "%s-proxy" $base | trunc 63` (the git-server-experimental helper's pattern). | The first round's discriminator coupled CA-delivery to an operator config field instead of the runner's actual env; the lesson is to derive a security-relevant branch from the data the consumer truly receives. The helm-truncation bug is a known footgun the chart already solved once (gitServerExperimentalComponentName) ŌĆö I should have copied that suffix-reserving form for ANY new `<name>-<suffix>` helper. Regression tests: pod-spec asserts TCP mode with config.proxyEndpoint UNSET; render asserts unique Service names + `-proxy` suffix under a 62-char fullnameOverride. | (P2a) require sandbox.proxyEndpoint whenever TCP proxy is enabled ŌĆö rejected, that re-introduces the same lockstep-coupling the bug is about; deriving from pc.endpoint is the single source of truth. (P2b) shorten the suffix ŌĆö rejected, `-proxy` is already minimal; reserving 6 chars of head budget is the standard fix. |

| 2026-06-03 | TASK-149 Phase 5 round 3 (codex, BOTH accepted): **P2 ŌĆö a skill/connector credential slot NAMED like a proxy control var (e.g. `AX_PROXY_CA_PEM`) lands in `pc.envMap`, which pod-spec appended LAST, so the kubelet's last-duplicate-wins rule lets the `ax-cred:<hex>` placeholder shadow the real control value** ŌåÆ runner writes `ax-cred:...` as the CA file ŌåÆ all proxied TLS fails. Fix: build a `reservedProxyEnv` Set from the already-stamped proxy control vars and SKIP any envMap key that collides (control wins over slot env ŌĆö TASK-86 trusted-base-wins precedent). This also closes the same latent collision for AX_PROXY_ENDPOINT/UNIX_SOCKET/TOKEN/cert vars in BOTH transports. **P3 ŌĆö the tcpPort-without-advertisedEndpoint guard checked `=== undefined` but not `=== ''`**, so a hand-rolled config with `advertisedEndpoint: ''` slipped through and advertised the bind address. Fix: normalize emptyŌåÆundefined before the guard + before building the listen config. | The envMap-last ordering is the documented "per-session credentials win over ordinary env" rule ŌĆö correct for credential placeholders, WRONG for trusted control vars the host stamps; the reserved-set is the minimal fix that keeps credential precedence for everything except the control names. Empty-string-as-present is a recurring config-validation footgun (the codebase uses `!== '' && !== undefined` everywhere for exactly this). Regression tests: pod-spec asserts a colliding AX_PROXY_CA_PEM slot can't shadow the real PEM (single entry, real value); preset asserts createK8sPlugins throws on both missing AND empty advertisedEndpoint. | (P2) reserve only AX_PROXY_CA_PEM ŌĆö rejected, the same shadowing hits every control var, so reserve the whole stamped set. (P3) trust the env loader to never emit '' ŌĆö rejected, createK8sPlugins is a public entry a hand-rolled config reaches directly; defense-in-depth normalizes there too. |

| 2026-06-03 | TASK-149 Phase 5 round 4 (codex P1 ŌĆö REJECTED as a blocker, tracked as a follow-up; NOT silently dismissed): codex flagged that opening the proxy cluster-wide in TCP mode lets a compromised runner in session A reach a host that only session B allowlisted (and get B's ax-cred placeholders substituted), because `findAllowingSession` ORs the allowlist across ALL sessions and `Proxy-Authorization` is attribution-only. **This is a REAL property but it is PRE-EXISTING, not a regression introduced by TASK-149:** (1) listener.ts:52 documents "the allowlist check ORs across all registered sessions" ŌĆö identical in hostPath/kind mode, where every runner pod already reaches the same shared socket; (2) decisions.md TASK-52 (2026-05-26) records that per-session egress ISOLATION "was considered and REJECTED as out-of-scope ŌĆö it would change the allow/deny gate (regression risk on the egress path)". My change is TRANSPORT-ONLY and keeps `findAllowingSession` UNTOUCHED (the card's "Keep I1/I5 untouched" + "S1 has no code-level dependents"). Per-session proxy authorization is a separate, larger architectural decision that touches the security-critical egress gate ŌĆö exactly the blast radius this card forbids. Disposition: ship TASK-149 (transport migration, legacy path unchanged, acceptance met), surface per-session-isolation as a deferred follow-up card + flag it in the PR security note. | The card scope is explicit (transport + CA delivery; no gate change), and the cross-session OR is a documented, deliberately-deferred design ŌĆö redesigning it inside a transport-migration PR would be scope creep AND would re-open the exact egress-gate regression risk TASK-52 avoided. This is the "accept minor/out-of-scope review issues as non-blocking + track them" pattern, not a silent dismissal. | (a) add per-session token authz to findAllowingSession in THIS PR ŌĆö rejected: changes the allow/deny gate (TASK-52's explicit no-go), out of card scope, large blast radius; (b) per-session listener-per-pod isolation ŌĆö rejected: a much bigger architecture change (N listeners or a sidecar), its own design; (c) ignore it ŌĆö rejected: it's a real production-multi-tenant gap worth a tracked card, just not a blocker for the transport migration. |
